# Capabilities ‚Äî the loop's only success metric

Append-only inventory of **real, user-exercisable** Muse
capabilities. One line per capability: what the user can do, the
exact command/surface, and the executable check that proves it.

Rules (enforced by `.claude/rules/iteration-loop.md`):

- Every shipped outward goal MUST append exactly one new line here.
  The `<check>` MUST be a concrete automated test or smoke id that
  actually runs green under `pnpm check` / `pnpm smoke:broad` /
  `pnpm smoke:live` and asserts the *capability* end-to-end (not
  that code compiles). Prose with no runnable id is not a check.
- **Cross-time falsification:** every iteration's first action is
  to run the newest line's check and prove it still passes. A
  faked/broken line = the next iteration's whole job is to fix it.
- **Regression sweep:** every 10th iteration re-runs ALL checks;
  any regression = next iteration must restore it.
- A request/response-path capability whose `smoke:live` did NOT
  actually run is tagged `[UNVERIFIED-LIVE]`; it does not count
  until a later iteration runs the live check and drops the tag.
- Append-only. Never delete or weaken a line.
- **The success metric is NOT this line count.** It is
  `OUTWARD-TARGETS.md` bullets flipped `[ ]`‚Üí`[x]`. A line here is
  the *evidence* for a flip (cite the bullet it delivers); a line
  that adds no bullet flip is thin and does not satisfy the metric.
  No bullet flipped in the last 5 iterations ‚áí next iteration's
  sole mandate is to flip one end-to-end. Flat bullets =
  degeneration; act on it ‚Äî never stop, never ask a human.

Format: `- [<axis>] <capability> ‚Äî <command/surface> ‚Äî <runnable check id> ‚Äî P<n> bullet`
axis ‚àà Reach | Anticipation | Autonomy | Presence

## Inventory

P0‚ÄìP21's full verified ledger is preserved in
`archive/CAPABILITIES-through-2026-05-27.md` (human reset
2026-05-27 to keep the loop-facing file lean ‚Äî history intact, not
deleted). The lines below are the delivered foundation that the
active P22 target extends; new P22 lines append here.

- [Anticipation] Proactive notice loop (upcoming events / reminders) ‚Äî `apps/api` proactive daemon tick ‚Äî `apps/api` proactive-tick tests
- [Anticipation] Self-queued follow-up promises fire later ‚Äî followups daemon tick ‚Äî `runDueFollowups` tests
- [Autonomy] Standing-objective evaluation fires its actuator ‚Äî objectives daemon tick ‚Äî `runDueObjectives` tests
- [Anticipation] Ambient OS signal drives a proactive notice ‚Äî `runAmbientNoticeTick` + `MacOsActiveWindowSource` ‚Äî ambient-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] Page-change web-watch fires an edge-triggered notice ‚Äî `createWebWatchRunner` (HTTP + Chrome source) ‚Äî web-watch-runner / web-watch-chrome tests
- [Anticipation] Proactive notice delivered to a real channel ‚Äî `ProactiveNoticeSink` over the messaging registry (Telegram) ‚Äî `sendWithRetry` + proactive-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] One-process daemon launcher fires a real proactive tick ‚Äî `muse daemon --once` ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` (imminent task delivered to a contract-faithful messaging sink; quiet tick sends nothing; unknown provider fails closed) ‚Äî P22-1a bullet
- [Presence] Episode forgetting is now importance-aware ‚Äî a pivotal old session resists being vacuumed away while a trivial recent one fades (FadeMem, arXiv 2601.18642: biologically-inspired forgetting, decay modulated by importance) ‚Äî `vacuumEpisodes` dropped purely-oldest-by-`endedAt` at the cap; now `computeEpisodeRetention` scores each episode `exp(-ageDays / (halfLife¬∑(1 + w¬∑importance/10)))` so importance EXTENDS the half-life (importance-10 ‚áí ~3√ó slower fade), and `selectRetainedEpisodes` keeps the highest-retention `cap` (newest-then-id tie-break). Back-compatible: an UNSCORED corpus reduces to recency ordering, so chronological vacuum is byte-identical until importance is present ‚Äî `@muse/mcp` episode-retention.test.ts (age decay; importance slows fade; unscored‚Üírecency; unparseable‚Üí0; importance tips comparable ages: a 35-day importance-10 session out-retains a 25-day importance-1 one at the cap; deterministic ties) + existing vacuum suite stays green (unscored episodes still pruned oldest-first) ‚Äî research-applied slice (no new dep, deterministic/local; builds on the importance arc)
- [Presence] Auto-extracted memory now resolves each fact with an explicit operation instead of blind-overwriting (Mem0, arXiv 2504.19413: per-candidate ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NOOP) ‚Äî `classifyMemoryOperation(existing, incoming)` is deterministic over the extractor's output (no extra model call): NOOP when a value re-confirms what's stored ‚Üí SKIPS the redundant write + provenance entry (a re-mention no longer logs a fresh "learned" event); DELETE when the value is a no-value/retraction token (none/n/a/unknown/ÏóÜÏùå/Î™®Î¶Ñ/‚Ä¶) ‚Üí the key is FORGOTTEN via the store's `forget` instead of storing junk like "unknown"; ADD/UPDATE upsert + record provenance as before; the auto-extract persist reads existing memory once and routes each fact/preference through it ‚Äî `@muse/memory` memory-operation.test.ts (classifier: add/noop/update/delete EN+KO tokens; auto-extract integration: re-confirm ‚Üí no new provenance, changed ‚Üí upsert+provenance, retraction ‚Üí key forgotten) + full memory suite 213 green (new facts still ADD as before, back-compatible) ‚Äî research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; deterministic, no new dep, no extra LLM call)
- [Reach] A natural-language tool-selection path is available + measured against the native one (Natural Language Tools, arXiv 2510.14453: stating the tool choice in prose + parsing it deterministically beats forcing JSON on small/open-weight models) ‚Äî `parseNaturalLanguageToolSelection(text, toolNames)` deterministically maps a model's prose answer to one known tool (earliest-named wins; whole-token match so `time_now` ‚âÝ `my_time_now_helper`; explicit no-tool/none/ÏóÜÏùå ‚Üí none) and `pnpm eval:tools:nl` compares NATIVE (Hermes JSON tool-call) vs NL one-shot accuracy on the confusable time set ‚Äî `@muse/tools` nl-tool-selection.test.ts (single pick, "use A not B"‚ÜíA, no-tool EN+KO, embedded-name not matched, empty) + LIVE qwen3:8b: native 7/7 (100%) AND NL 7/7 (100%) on the confusable time set ‚Äî verified finding: Muse's tuned tool names are ALREADY at the selection ceiling, so the NL path is kept as a reusable parser + comparison gate rather than wired (evidence-based: add NL complexity only when a confusable set's native accuracy drops below ceiling) ‚Äî research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep, core tool path untouched)
- [Presence] Muse applies LEARNED STRATEGIES from past feedback, not just avoidances ‚Äî a self-improving playbook (ACE ‚Äî Agentic Context Engineering, arXiv 2510.04618: a frozen model improves by accumulating small strategy deltas in an evolving context, no fine-tuning) ‚Äî the POSITIVE counterpart to veto-avoidance: `applyPlaybook` injects a `[Learned Strategies]` system block (mirrors the veto-avoidance seam; conservative ‚Äî zero strategies/no userId ‚áí exact no-op; fail-open) wired into the live agent-runtime context pipeline behind a duck-typed `PlaybookProvider`; the durable `~/.muse/playbook.json` store (`@muse/mcp`, atomic/tolerant/capped) is adapted by `buildPlaybookProvider` (MUSE_PLAYBOOK default-on) and populated via `muse playbook add|list|remove` ‚Äî `@muse/agent-core` playbook.test.ts (conservative/fail-open/inject + injection-collapse + LIVE-runtime wiring: a recorded strategy reaches a real createAgentRuntime run's system prompt, none ‚Üí no-op) + LIVE qwen3:8b EFFECT MEASUREMENT: with the strategy "answer in at most 6 words" injected, a question that drew a long multi-paragraph reply WITHOUT it returned a 7-word "Paris. Famous for art, fashion, and culture." WITH it ‚Äî the learned strategy measurably changed the model's output ‚Äî research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep; mirrors the proven veto-avoidance pattern end-to-end)
- [Anticipation] The daemon launcher also fires due follow-ups in the same process ‚Äî `muse daemon --once` (proactive + followup ticks) ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` (a DUE followup is synthesized + delivered to a contract-faithful sink alongside the proactive tick; proactive-only cases stay hermetic) ‚Äî P22-1b bullet
- [Anticipation] The daemon launcher also fires ambient (perception) rule matches in the same process ‚Äî `muse daemon --once` (proactive + followup + ambient ticks) ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` (a matching ambient rule delivers a notice to a contract-faithful sink; ambient skipped cleanly when no MUSE_AMBIENT_RULES) ‚Äî P22-1c bullet

- [Presence] The learned-strategy playbook injects only the strategies RELEVANT to the current turn, not the whole bank (ReasoningBank, arXiv 2509.25140: a self-evolving agent retrieves relevant reasoning memory rather than dumping it) ‚Äî `rankPlaybookStrategies` (CJK-aware token-overlap + tag boost, top-K with a recency floor so a non-empty bank never injects zero) wired into BOTH `applyPlaybook` (runtime `--with-tools`) and the chat-only `muse ask` path via `selectPlaybookSection` (env `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_INJECT_TOPK`, default 6); when the bank is ‚â§ topK the SET is unchanged (today's inject-all), only ordered most-relevant-first ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (relevance ranks above irrelevant; ‚â§K returns all best-first; >K drops least-relevant; recency floor on zero-overlap; Korean CJK match; applyPlaybook orders by the latest user message) + `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-playbook.test.ts` (an email prompt injects the email strategy and drops a scheduling-only one at topK=1) ‚Äî research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; deterministic, no new dep, no extra LLM call; foundation for slice-2 correction-driven auto-distillation)
- [Presence] Muse auto-LEARNS a strategy from a correction the user made ‚Äî at session end it distills a generalised `[Learned Strategies]` entry from a corrected exchange into the SAME `~/.muse/playbook.json` (ReasoningBank, arXiv 2509.25140: a self-evolving agent distills reusable strategies from its own experience; the outcome signal is the RELIABLE explicit correction, NOT small-model self-judgement per arXiv 2404.17140) ‚Äî auto at REPL exit (`MUSE_PLAYBOOK_DISTILL_ENABLED`, default off) + manual `muse playbook distill`; pipeline = `detectCorrections` (EN+KO, precision-first rule pass) ‚Üí `distillStrategyFromCorrection` (one LLM call, secret-redacted, fail-soft) ‚Üí `strategyTextSimilarity` dedup (‚â•0.6, makes re-runs idempotent) ‚Üí `recordPlaybookStrategy` ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detector EN+KO + false-positive guard + no-prior-assistant + cap; distiller parse/omit-tag/fail-soft) + `playbook.test.ts` (similarity) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (records from a corrected session, skips no-correction, dedups, skips no-userId) + `commands-playbook.test.ts` (distill subcommand); LIVE qwen3:8b: the Korean correction "Í∑∏Í≤å ÏïÑÎãàÎùº Î∂àÎ¶ø Ìè¨Ïù∏Ìä∏Î°ú ÏÝïÎ¶¨Ìï¥Ï§ò" distilled "when asked to summarise, use bullet points not prose" into the playbook end-to-end via `muse playbook distill` ‚Äî research-applied slice (arXiv ids cited in code; deterministic detection+dedup, single offline LLM call, no new dep; completes ReasoningBank retrieval‚Üídistillation)
- [Knowledge] knowledge_search grades retrieval confidence and FRAMES weak grounding as low-confidence instead of telling the small local model to cite it (CRAG, arXiv 2401.15884: a lightweight retrieval evaluator scores evidence quality) ‚Äî `classifyRetrievalConfidence` over the TOP match's ABSOLUTE cosine (surfaced as `KnowledgeMatch.cosine`, separate from the hybrid RRF `score`): confident‚Üí"cite the [source]", ambiguous‚Üí"Possibly-related (LOW confidence ‚Äî verify, don't cite as fact)", none‚Üíno passages; `renderKnowledgeMatches` (the agent `knowledge_search` + notes corpus-search tools) and the ambient `createKnowledgeEnricher` (Related line only when confident) gate on it ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-agent.test.ts` (verdict none/ambiguous/confident; cosine surfaced in both paths; render header by verdict) + `knowledge-render-litm.test.ts` + `packages/autoconfigure/test/knowledge-enricher*.test.ts` (weak match ‚Üí no Related line) ‚Äî research-applied slice. HONEST scope: live-calibrated on nomic-embed (relevant ~0.61 vs personal distractors ~0.44‚Äì0.51 ‚Üí `confidentAt` 0.55), but nomic's cosine space is compressed (unrelated encyclopedic text can score ~0.54), so this is a BEST-EFFORT low-confidence flag for personal corpora, not a hard relevant/irrelevant separator (same honesty class as the P24-2 MMR nudge). No web fallback (deferred); deterministic, no new dep, no extra round
- [Autonomy] The plan-execute planner reuses a similar PAST plan as a few-shot exemplar so the small local model plans better in one shot (Agentic Plan Caching, arXiv 2506.14852: extract plan templates from completed runs and reuse them on similar tasks) ‚Äî completed plans auto-captured to `~/.muse/plan-cache.json`, retrieved by Jaccard token overlap (`selectPlanExemplar`, reuses `strategyTextSimilarity`), rendered as a `[Similar Past Plan]` block injected into the planning prompt before `[User Request]`; threaded `PlanCacheProvider` ‚Üí `PlanExecuteRunner` ‚Üí `AgentRuntime`, built by `buildPlanCacheProvider` (default-on, opt out `MUSE_PLAN_CACHE=false`), conservative (no userId / no match ‚áí no exemplar + no record), fail-open ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/plan-cache.test.ts` (retrieval picks most-similar / none below threshold; render shape) + `agent-runtime-plan-cache.test.ts` (a plan-execute run records its plan; a cached similar plan is injected into the planning request; no userId ‚áí neither) + `packages/mcp/test/personal-plan-cache-store.test.ts` (record/query/filter/upsert/cap/tolerant) + `packages/prompts/test/prompts.test.ts` (exemplar before [User Request]) ‚Äî research-applied slice. HONEST scope: this is APC's faithful store/match adapted for a LOCAL free model as planning GUIDANCE (improves one-shot plan reliability), NOT APC's skip-the-planner efficiency play (cloud cost benefit is moot locally; exact repeats already covered by responseCache). Deterministic, no new dep, no extra model round
- [Autonomy] Muse AUTHORS a reusable SKILL.md from a procedural user correction at session end (fork-and-review, after Hermes Agent's background-review loop, MIT ‚Äî see THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md) ‚Äî deterministic `detectSkillCandidates` (reuses `detectCorrections`, EN+KO) ‚Üí one local-Qwen `draftSkillFromSignal` (returns `NONE` for mere preferences so those stay playbook-only, secret-redacted, fail-soft) ‚Üí `AuthoredSkillStore.writeOrPatch` (EXECUTE-GATED by type: a SkillDraft has no `requires` field so an authored skill can never declare runnable bins ‚Üí `muse.skills.run` refuses it until a human promotes it; dedup‚Üípatch/skip, cap 30 with archive-never-delete, atomic fsync+rename 0600) into `~/.muse/skills/authored/`, loaded as the LOWEST-precedence registry root (a same-named user/workspace skill always wins) so it is picked up next session and surfaced by `selectRelevantSkills` on a similar request; auto at REPL exit (`MUSE_SKILL_AUTHOR_ENABLED`, default off) + manual `muse skills author` ‚Äî `packages/skills/test/authored-skill-store.test.ts` (create + execute-gate + dedup patch/skip + cap-archive + collision suffix) + `packages/agent-core/test/skill-review.test.ts` (detect EN+KO + cap; draft parse / NONE‚Üínull / malformed‚Üínull / fail-soft) + `packages/autoconfigure/test/skills-registry-precedence.test.ts` (user overrides authored; authored-only still loads) + `apps/cli/src/chat-author-skills.test.ts` (authors from a corrected session, skips no-correction, fail-soft, AND end-to-end: authored ‚Üí loaded next session via buildSkillRegistry ‚Üí selected by selectRelevantSkills on a similar request, not on an unrelated one); `pnpm check` + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + `pnpm smoke:live` (request path unaffected) ‚Äî self-improvement slice (the inputs already existed ‚Äî ReasoningBank distiller, reflection, UserModel; this is the missing bridge: experience ‚Üí durable reusable skill)
- [Autonomy] Authored skills record `lastUsedAt` when body-injected per turn, are now included in the REPL's per-turn skill selection (not only the agent-core catalog), and `muse skills authored` lists them with authored/last-used dates (curator lifecycle foundation, after Hermes Agent curator, MIT ‚Äî see THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md) ‚Äî `AuthoredSkillStore.recordUsage()` (60s throttle, fail-soft, atomic write) + `buildSkillsPrompt` `onSelected` callback + REPL authored-skill merge (user overrides authored on name collision) ‚Äî `packages/skills/test/authored-skill-store.test.ts` (recordUsage stamps lastUsedAt; returns false for unknown skill; throttled within 60s; updates after >60s) + `apps/cli/src/chat-skills.test.ts` (onSelected fires for body-injected skill only, not for index-only skills); `pnpm check` + `pnpm lint` 0/0
- [Knowledge] Muse synthesises GROUNDED reflections ("dreaming") ‚Äî higher-level insights about the user from recent episodes/notes ‚Äî that CANNOT make things up (after OpenClaw's dreaming + Generative Agents reflection, arXiv 2304.03442; honest/local Muse key) ‚Äî `synthesizeReflections` (agent-core) prompts the LOCAL model over `{id,text}` items; `parseReflections` deterministically strips any cited source id absent from the inputs and drops a reflection below `minSupport` distinct real sources, so an insight can only be grounded in episodes the user actually has ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/src/reflection-synthesis.test.ts` (11: grounding strips invented ids, minSupport, dedupe, junk-tolerant JSON, fail-soft) + a LIVE qwen3:8b battery `apps/cli/scripts/verify-reflection-synthesis.mjs` in `eval:self-improving` (a recurring networking theme across 3 episodes synthesised + grounded in the right real ids; grounding invariant holds for every reflection); `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî P32-1 differentiation slice (idle-daemon wiring + persistence is P32-2)
- [Knowledge] `muse reflections [refresh]` surfaces Muse's GROUNDED "dreaming" ‚Äî higher-level insights about the user synthesised from past episodes, each citing the real episodes it came from (P32-2; OpenClaw dreaming + Generative Agents reflection in Muse's honest/local key) ‚Äî `reflections-store` (atomic + mutation-queued, dedup on normalised insight, FIFO-trim) + `muse reflections refresh` (reads recent episodes ‚Üí `synthesizeReflections` over the local model ‚Üí `addReflections`, dedup) + `muse reflections` (lists newest-first WITH source episode ids). - [Knowledge] The daemon AUTO-dreams while idle ‚Äî a throttled background reflection pass synthesises GROUNDED insights about the user from recent episodes with NO user action, persisting only insights cited to real episodes (P32-3; off by default `MUSE_REFLECTION_ENABLED`, slow cadence `MUSE_REFLECTION_INTERVAL_MS` default 6h) ‚Äî `muse daemon` `reflectionTick` (gated + throttled by `shouldRunReflection`; now writes via `resolveReflectionsFile(e)` ‚Äî FIXED to honor the daemon's injected env instead of a global `process.env` path, so a configured daemon dreams to the right file) ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` ("grounded dreaming tick (P32-3)": enabled + 3 seeded episodes ‚Üí exactly one grounded reflection persisted citing only the real ids e1/e2/e3 and a `reflections: +1` line; flag unset ‚Üí nothing written + no `reflections:` line, the gate is real). - [Reach] Muse-to-Muse SWARM shares KNOW-HOW only (skills/strategies/reasoning), NEVER personal data, with inbound INERT ‚Äî `muse swarm share|serve|pending|promote`: a peer's shared skill crosses as a PII-redacted, HMAC-signed A2A `message/send`, lands QUARANTINED on the receiver (a peer can never trigger compute), and runs nothing until the user promotes it to an EXECUTE-GATED authored skill (no `requires:` ‚Üí `muse.skills.run` refuses it). Off by default (`MUSE_A2A_ENABLED`, fail-closed), peer-allowlisted, draft-first share (`--yes`); the Agent Card advertises the contract (`acceptsExecution:false`, `inboundDisposition:[quarantine,reject]`, `piiRedacted:true`) ‚Äî `packages/a2a` (68 tests/12 files: signing, transport, handler, quarantine, agent-card, council-wire) + `apps/cli/src/commands-swarm.test.ts` (11: full send‚Üíquarantine‚Üípromote e2e + draft-first redaction + unknown-peer reject). - [Reach] The swarm can convene a COUNCIL ‚Äî `muse swarm council <q>` asks allowlisted peers to reason (data-light: only PII-redacted reasoning crosses ‚Äî no corpus, no execution), then synthesises ONE grounded answer that cites ONLY the real members who weighed in (Multiagent Debate, Du et al. 2023, arXiv 2305.14325; the honesty gate carries through so a non-participating peer is never cited) ‚Äî `packages/a2a` council-wire tests (`signCouncilRequest`/`verifyCouncilRequest`) + `packages/agent-core` council synthesis (`produceCouncilReasoning`/`synthesizeCouncilAnswer`/`parseCouncilAnswer` drop non-real members). - [Autonomy] Muse runs REINFORCEMENT LEARNING over its learned-strategy playbook (model is fixed ‚Üí RL on the MEMORY, not the weights): each strategy carries a clamped `reward` that reward-weighted `rankPlaybookStrategies` blends into selection, so a proven strategy surfaces first and one that keeps getting corrected DECAYS out of the injected top-K; the signal is AUTOMATIC ‚Äî at session end the strategy a correction implicates (most similar to the corrected request) is docked via `adjustPlaybookReward`, alongside ReasoningBank distillation of the new lesson. Reward flows through BOTH injection paths (agent-runtime `buildPlaybookProvider` + chat-only `muse ask` `selectPlaybookSection`); `muse playbook` shows each strategy's learned reward and `muse playbook distill` reports what it decayed ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (reward breaks a relevance tie; a ‚àí5 strategy sinks out of top-K below a fresh peer; absent reward == 0; `clampReward` bounds) + `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (`adjustPlaybookReward` accumulates/clamps/unknown-id/non-finite no-op; back-compat read of a reward-less entry; non-numeric reward quarantined) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (a corrected session docks the implicated strategy to ‚àí1, unrelated untouched). LIVE: `muse playbook list` renders ‚ü®reward +3‚ü©/‚ü®reward ‚àí4‚ü© and a ‚àí4 prose strategy is deranked below an equally-relevant bullet strategy through the BUILT CLI; `pnpm check` green (agent-core 1064 / mcp 1108 / autoconfigure 450 / cli 1547 / api 747) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî P33-1 RL slice (ACE arXiv 2510.04618 + the sibling veto store; reward-shaped, model-fixed)
- [Autonomy] The RL reward signal is now BIDIRECTIONAL ‚Äî an explicit user APPROVAL reinforces the strategy that applied, the mirror of correction-driven decay, so the playbook learns from both "you got it right" and "you got it wrong" (not just absence-of-negative). `detectApprovals` (agent-core) is a precision-first EN+KO detector mirroring `detectCorrections` (fires on "perfect"/"exactly right"/"nailed it"/"ÏôÑÎ≤ΩÌï¥"/"Îî± Ï¢ãÏïÑ"/"Î∞îÎ°ú Í∑∏Í±∞Ïïº" ‚Äî NOT bare "ok"/"thanks"/"Ï¢ãÏïÑ"/"Í≥ÝÎßàÏõå", which acknowledge but don't endorse); at session end `distillSessionCorrections` credit-assigns each approval to the existing strategy most similar to its request and REINFORCES it (+1, `adjustPlaybookReward`), once per strategy (never both decayed and reinforced in one session), alongside correction-decay + distillation. `muse playbook distill` now reports both ‚Üë reinforced and ‚Üì decayed ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detectApprovals: 13 EN+KO endorsements fire, 9 bare-acknowledgement phrases do NOT, assistant‚Üíuser pairing + request backfill + maxExchanges cap) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (an approval session with no correction lifts the applied strategy to +1, unrelated untouched, status still "skipped"-for-distillation). agent-core 1068 / cli 1548 tests pass + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî P33-2 RL slice (bidirectional reward from explicit feedback)
- [Autonomy] LEARNED AVOIDANCE closes the RL extinction loop ‚Äî a strategy corrected into the floor (reward ‚â§ `PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW` = ‚àí4, ~4 implicating corrections) is EXCLUDED from injection ENTIRELY, not merely deranked: `rankPlaybookStrategies` filters it out before selection even when the bank is ‚â§ topK (where ranking otherwise returns everything, so a deeply-negative strategy would still slip into a small bank). Soft + reversible (the veto-store parallel): it stays in the bank, shows in `muse playbook` as "¬∑ avoided (not injected)", and a later approval can lift its reward back above the line. `isAvoidedStrategy` is the shared predicate ‚Äî `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (an avoided strategy is dropped even at bank ‚â§ topK; reward ‚àí3 still injects ranked last; all-avoided ‚Üí empty; `isAvoidedStrategy` boundary incl. absent=not-avoided). LIVE: `muse playbook list` renders "‚ü®reward ‚àí4 ¬∑ avoided (not injected)‚ü©" and a ‚àí4 strategy is excluded from a 2-strategy bank's injection through the BUILT CLI. agent-core 1072 / cli 1548 tests pass + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî P33-3 RL slice (learned avoidance; the soft, reversible veto)
- [Autonomy] The RL reward loop now spans AUTHORED SKILLS too, not just the strategy playbook ‚Äî a skill the user keeps correcting stops being applied; one they approve earns standing (the same decay/reinforce/avoid mechanics, extended to a second memory type). A sidecar `skill-rewards.json` (name‚Üíreward, kept OUT of each SKILL.md so a decay never rewrites the body) holds the reward; `adjustSkillReward` (clamped, mutation-queued) moves it; at session end `applySkillRewardsFromSession` credit-assigns each correction/approval to the authored skill the live prompt WOULD have applied ‚Äî via the SAME `selectRelevantSkills` the per-turn prompt uses, so credit lands on the skill that actually applied ‚Äî and decays (‚àí1) / reinforces (+1) it; `buildSkillsPrompt` then DROPS an avoided skill (reward ‚â§ `SKILL_AVOID_BELOW` = ‚àí4) from the per-turn prompt entirely (no body, not even an index line). `muse skills authored` shows each skill's reward + "¬∑ avoided (not applied)" ‚Äî `packages/mcp/test/skill-rewards-store.test.ts` (read/clamp/adjust/avoid-boundary) + `apps/cli/src/chat-skills.test.ts` (selectRelevantSkills + buildSkillsPrompt drop an avoided skill, keep the rest) + `apps/cli/src/chat-author-skills.test.ts` (a corrected request decays the applied skill to ‚àí1, an approval reinforces to +1, a bare ack ‚Üí no change). LIVE: `muse skills authored` renders "reward: ‚àí4 ¬∑ avoided (not applied)" and a ‚àí4 skill is excluded from a matching prompt through the BUILT CLI. mcp 1112 / cli 1553 tests pass + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî P33-4 RL slice (reward loop extended from the playbook to authored skills)
- [Autonomy] The user can STEER the RL reward directly ‚Äî `muse playbook reward <id> [amount] [--down]` and `muse skills reward <name> [amount] [--down]` manually reinforce (or, with `--down`, penalise) a learned strategy/skill, clamped via the SAME `adjustPlaybookReward`/`adjustSkillReward` the auto-signal uses. So a strategy/skill the auto-loop wrongly penalised can be RESCUED back above the avoid line, and a known-good one PRE-TRUSTED ‚Äî the reversibility + control that makes the (default-off) auto-RL safe to turn on. `amount` is a positive integer (default 1) so `--down` sidesteps commander parsing a leading `-` as a flag; an unknown id/name is refused and never written ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-playbook.test.ts` (reinforces +amount, --down penalises, clamps, prefix-matched id, unknown id refused) + `apps/cli/src/commands-skills.test.ts` (adjusts an authored skill, --down penalises, unknown skill refused + not written; `resolveSkillRewardsFile` env/default). - [Knowledge/Edge] `muse ask` no longer FALSE-REFUSES a question its corpus answers when the answer note's embedding cosine ranks below near-misses ‚Äî the headline chat-only recall path is now HYBRID (embedding-cosine + lexical keyword RRF), the same fusion the `knowledge_search` agent path already used (P23, RRF: Cormack et al. SIGIR 2009), but it was never applied to the headline `muse ask` path, which ranked notes by PURE cosine. On nomic's compressed embedding space a query with strong distinctive terms ("WireGuard", "MTU") ranked the one answer-bearing note ~5th, so the default top-3 excluded it and Muse honestly-but-WRONGLY said "I'm not sure" ‚Äî the "GUARD THE EDGE" failure mode (a false refusal turns honest into useless). `diversifyAskChunks` gains an optional `query`: when present it fuses the cosine rank with a lexical-overlap rank (reusing agent-core's now-exported `lexicalTokens`/`lexicalOverlap`/`fuseByReciprocalRank`) via RRF, normalises the fused relevance to [0,1] so MMR's diversity term stays comparable, and selects the top-K from that ‚Äî WITHOUT re-embedding (index embeddings reused) and KEEPING each chunk's absolute cosine `score` so the CRAG confidence framing is unchanged; a stopword-only query falls back to the prior cosine MMR ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-mmr.test.ts` (hybrid: a keyword-matching answer note that pure-cosine top-3 EXCLUDES is rescued into the top-3; the rescued chunk keeps its absolute cosine 0.50; a stopword-only query is byte-identical to cosine selection). - [Knowledge/Edge] A correctly-grounded `muse ask` answer no longer carries a FALSE "‚öÝ LOW confidence ‚Äî verify, may not be in your notes" caution ‚Äî the CRAG confidence framing now considers LEXICAL strength, not absolute cosine alone. nomic's cosine space is compressed, so a genuinely-relevant note (e.g. the WireGuard note at cosine ~0.50) sat just below the confident threshold and got flagged LOW even when ranked first and cited correctly ‚Äî a SOFT false-refusal that tells the user not to trust an answer that IS grounded, eroding the trust edge. `notesGroundingFraming` now takes the query: a STRONG lexical match (‚â•2 distinct query content tokens present in a grounded chunk, reusing agent-core's `lexicalTokens`/`lexicalOverlap`) upgrades an ambiguous-cosine verdict to `confident`; a must-refuse question shares no content tokens so it stays LOW/none, and the output-side citation gate remains the hard backstop ‚Äî fabrication=0 is preserved by construction ‚Äî `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-crag.test.ts` (ambiguous-cosine + strong-keyword query ‚Üí confident, plain header, no weak-match guidance; a must-refuse query ‚Üí stays LOW; a single shared token does NOT upgrade ‚Äî needs ‚â•2). - [Self-learning] A reinforced strategy is no longer forgotten just for being old (B1 Slice 3 ‚Äî reward-/recency-weighted eviction). When the learned-strategy playbook overflows its 100-entry cap, eviction was blind FIFO (drop the oldest regardless of value), so a strategy you reinforced repeatedly could be evicted while a never-used newer one survived. New `retainPlaybookEntries` (mcp) keeps the highest-value entries instead ‚Äî value = reward, then recency: a high-reward OLD strategy beats a low-reward NEW one, reward ties break toward the newer, negative/avoided entries are evicted first, and survivors keep their original insertion order (the recency proxy `rankPlaybookStrategies` relies on). `recordPlaybookStrategy` now caps via this helper instead of `.slice(-MAX)`. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (at/under cap returned unchanged; high-reward-old kept over low-reward-new with order preserved; reward-tie‚Üírecency; avoided evicted before neutral/positive; record-path overflow of 120 neutral fillers keeps a +5 champion) + a LIVE end-to-end run on this box (HOME-isolated mock playbook, never real ~/.muse): a `+5` champion recorded FIRST then buried under 120 newer neutral records survived the cap and `muse playbook list` shows `[champion] ‚ü®reward +5‚ü©` still present, total capped at 100 (blind FIFO would have dropped it as oldest). mcp 1227 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî the bank now keeps what you've proven matters, not merely what's newest ‚Äî P36-12 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse learned` now shows the WHY behind each learned strategy (B1 Slice 4 ‚Äî provenance + legibility). A strategy used to be just a sentence; now each carries its ORIGIN (`grounded` = distilled from a real correction, `reflected` = synthetic, `manual` = you typed it) and the `source` correction that taught it, so `muse learned` prints "‚Ü≥ learned from your correction: '<the exact thing you said>'" under both trusted and probation strategies ‚Äî the legibility precondition to trusting unattended learning (you can judge whether to keep what Muse learned). PlaybookEntry/PlaybookStrategy gain `origin`/`source`; both correction-distill writers (idle daemon `distill-queue.ts` + chat-exit `chat-distill-corrections.ts`) stamp `origin: "grounded"` + the correction; `renderLearnedDigest` renders the why line; and a small ranking tie-break (`REFLECTED_RANK_PENALTY`, far below a reward step or relevance point) makes a `reflected` strategy never outrank an otherwise-equal `grounded` one ‚Äî evidence beats synthesis at a dead heat. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (origin/source round-trip + non-string-drops), `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (grounded outranks equal reflected; penalty is tie-break-only, a more-relevant reflected still wins), `apps/cli/src/commands-learned.test.ts` (why line for grounded incl. probation; reflected flagged synthetic; long source truncated; legacy/manual gets no line) + a LIVE full chain on qwen3:8b (HOME-isolated, never real ~/.muse): enqueue "no, that is not what I meant ‚Äî give me bullet points, not prose" ‚Üí idle `distillQueuedCorrections` ‚Üí `muse learned` printed the probation strategy WITH "‚Ü≥ learned from your correction: '<that correction>'". agent-core 1238 / mcp 1229 / api 817 / cli 1618 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî the user can now SEE why Muse believes each learned thing ‚Äî P36-13 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse playbook undo <id>` now makes Muse forget a learned strategy AND not re-learn it (B1 Slice 5 ‚Äî undo that TEACHES; `--pause` deferred). Plain `remove` only deletes a strategy, so the idle distiller re-learns the same lesson the next time the user gives a similar correction. `undo` removes the strategy AND records a suppressed-lesson veto keyed on its SOURCE correction (the provenance captured by P36-13), so the idle daemon distiller skips that signal BEFORE the LLM call and bumps the veto's blocked counter. Keying on the stable correction signal (not the LLM's run-to-run paraphrase of the strategy) is what makes the suppression actually stick ‚Äî a flaw the live test caught and drove the redesign. New `suppressed-lessons.json` store (`packages/mcp/src/suppressed-lessons-store.ts`: record/read/query/incrementBlocked, atomic, capped) + `resolveSuppressedLessonsFile` (autoconfigure); `distill-queue.ts` (api) consults it via `strategyTextSimilarity` on the source; `muse playbook undo` (cli) wires it. - [Self-learning] `muse playbook pause` now stops ALL background self-learning with one command (B1 Slice 5 complete ‚Äî the kill-switch half). - [Edge/Measurement] `muse doctor --grounding` now scores the "shows its work" edge into two numbers a user reads on their own box (P38-1). The same scorer is the `verify-faithfulness-rate` battery in `eval:self-improving` as the regression gate; shipped floor 0.84 / 0.25 sits one miss below the deterministic live baseline 0.93 / 0.08 (nomic-embed-text + qwen3:8b) so a retrieval/calibration regression trips it. - [Edge/Grounding] `muse ask` now catches the WRONG-VALUE answer the lexical rubric was blind to (P38-2). A confident, high-coverage, fully-cited answer asserting a wrong number ("MTU 9000" where the note says 1380) passed `verifyGrounding` as `grounded` (one wrong token barely dents whole-answer coverage) and the weak-band judge never fired ‚Äî the deepest documented hole. `verifyGroundingWithReverify` now escalates a `grounded` answer that asserts a numeric value absent from the evidence to ONE judge pass, FAIL-OPEN (the base already cleared every deterministic criterion, so only an explicit unsupported verdict demotes it); the recall wedge (`groundingVerdictNotice`) inherits it with no caller change. The `--grounding` corpus gained 2 wrong-value cases that WITHOUT this fix drop faithfulness to 0.80 < the 0.84 floor, so `muse doctor --grounding` / `verify-faithfulness-rate` now GUARD it. Proof: `packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-reverify.test.ts` (5 escalation cases: demote-on-unsupported, uphold, fail-OPEN-on-error, no-escalation-when-supported, no-numbers) + a LIVE `node apps/cli/scripts/verify-claim-grounding.mjs` (the real qwen judge rejects "MTU 9000" at the DEFAULT threshold ‚Äî the grounded path, not the forced-weak band; "MTU 1380" stays grounded). agent-core 1336 + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ‚Äî Self-RAG ISSUP arXiv:2310.11511 / Chain-of-Note arXiv:2311.09210 ‚Äî P38-2 bullet
- [Edge/Constructive] `muse ask --repair` makes the edge CONSTRUCTIVE ‚Äî an ungrounded answer is corrected, not just warned (P38-3). - [Edge/Recall] `muse ask` now refuses a question whose only retrieval is a flat off-corpus near-miss, instead of presenting it as confident (P38-4, adaptive confidence calibration). Near nomic's compressed-cosine floor a single absolute bar is fragile ‚Äî an out-of-corpus query ("how much did I spend on groceries last month?") clipped a near-miss note at 0.563 > the 0.55 bar, so `classifyRetrievalConfidence` said `confident` and the model was invited to cite it. The gate now demotes a `confident` top that is BOTH borderline (within 0.05 of the floor) AND flat (top‚àírunner-up < 0.08 ‚Äî the query matches several notes weakly, not one strongly) to `ambiguous`, while a clearly-high top or a clear lead stays confident so genuine single-note matches are untouched. Calibrated from the live per-case margins (the lowest confident answerable sits at 0.627 with a 0.18 gap, far outside the band; only the flat near-miss flips). Drives both the recall framing and the proactivity gate. - [Actuation] `muse ask "remind me next month ‚Ä¶" --with-tools` now works ‚Äî Muse understands "next week / next month / next year" (P40-1). - [Honesty/Agent] `muse ask` never falsely claims to act ‚Äî even in a MIXED question+action request (P39-8). P39-6 short-circuits a PURE imperative ("remind me to ‚Ä¶"), but a MIXED request that OPENS with a question ‚Äî "what is my rent and remind me to pay it tomorrow" ‚Äî flowed through the normal path: Muse answered the rent (correctly cited) and then tacked on "I will remind you to pay it tomorrow", a false promise on the no-tools path (and fabricated a `[reminder: ‚Ä¶]` citation the gate stripped). A new `answerPromisesAction` (agent-core) detects the false promise in the ANSWER itself (not the query, so it catches mixed/compound requests the start-anchored classifyActionRequest misses): it matches an action-TOOL claim ‚Äî "I'll remind you / set a reminder / add a task / event / schedule / book / email", "I've set/added/scheduled/booked/emailed" ‚Äî but NOT a conversational "I'll explain", a plain cited answer, or a recall "you have a reminder to pay rent". Proof: 2 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-calendar.test.ts (an unreachable API on `calendar events` lists the locally-added "Dentist" event via the LocalCalendarProvider read-back; a 500 on `events` STILL throws ‚Äî the fallback is unreachable-specific) + the existing 33 calendar tests green (the closure-extraction refactor is behavior-preserving) + a LIVE server-less sequence on the built CLI (no --local, no server): `calendar add "Dentist cleaning" --at "tomorrow 3pm"` then `calendar events` ‚Üí "API not reachable ‚Äî using the local calendar store" then the event listed ("[cal_74c8] 15:00‚Äì16:00 Dentist cleaning (local)"), and tomorrow/free/conflicts/providers all fall back too. cli 164 files / 1733 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user on a local-first box can now both add AND read their calendar without a server or --local ‚Äî P40-5 bullet
- [Front-door/Privacy] `muse doctor` now reports the TRUE local-only model instead of a misleading "inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY" (P34-12). Under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY (default-ON, the core privacy posture), the model router IGNORES any ambient cloud key and runs the local ollama/qwen3:8b (per resolveDefaultModel) ‚Äî but the doctor's model-env check did NOT account for local-only: on any box that merely carried a GEMINI_API_KEY in the environment, it printed "[warn] model env: inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY". So a privacy-bound user running `muse doctor` precisely to CONFIRM that nothing leaves their machine was told their model is Gemini ‚Äî the diagnostic undercut the exact guarantee local-only exists to provide. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-doctor.ts by extracting a pure, exported `modelEnvCheck(env)` that mirrors the runtime's resolveDefaultModel exactly: an explicit MUSE_MODEL is reported verbatim; under local-only (parseBoolean(MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY, true)) it reports "ollama/qwen3:8b (local-only default ‚Äî ambient cloud keys ignored)" as OK; and the cloud-credential inference WARN ("inferred from GEMINI_API_KEY (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false)") appears ONLY under an explicit opt-out. - [Grounding edge/Perception] `muse ask` now treats facts the user told `muse remember` as a first-class CITED grounding source ‚Äî no more misattribution to a random note (P38-15). - [Actuation] `muse remind add` warns when the due time is in the PAST ‚Äî catching the date typo instead of silently creating a useless overdue reminder (P40-6). Crucially this does NOT relax or bypass the gate ‚Äî unlike the P38-15 answerability-relaxation attempt that was reverted last iteration for leaking a wrong drug, this keeps the judge in the loop and only makes it better at the cross-language comparison, so a WRONG cross-lingual value is still rejected. - [Felt/Grounding edge] A `muse ask` refusal now reads clean ‚Äî no self-contradicting "Removed citation ‚Ä¶ treat those claims as unverified" warning on an answer that asserts nothing (P34-13). When the small local model tacks a spurious citation onto a refusal (e.g. the Korean "ÏÝÄÎäî ÎãπÏãÝÏùò ÌòàÏï°ÌòïÏóê ÎåÄÌïú ÏÝïÎ≥¥Î•º Í∞ÄÏßÄÍ≥Ý ÏûàÏßÄ ÏïäÏäµÎãàÎã§ [from n.md]" or the English "I don't have that [memory: ‚Ä¶]"), the citation gate correctly strips it ‚Äî but the code then printed "‚öÝÔ∏è Removed 1 citation(s) to source(s) you don't have (‚Ä¶) ‚Äî treat those claims as unverified," which is nonsensical on a refusal (it makes no claims to "treat as unverified") and especially jarring for a Korean user, where the small model fabricates a stray citation on a refusal noticeably more often. - [Grounding edge/Perception] A Korean memory recall now cites `[memory: <key>]` cleanly instead of a false `[from <key>]` that gets stripped (P38-17). Probing ÏßÑÏïà's core "knows you" flow: `muse remember "ÎÇ¥ Ï∞® Î≤àÌò∏ÌåêÏùÄ 12Í∞Ä 3456Ïù¥Ïïº"` stored fact.car_license_plate = "12Í∞Ä 3456" fine, but `muse ask "ÎÇ¥ Ï∞® Î≤àÌò∏Ìåê Î≠êÏïº?"` answered correctly ("ÎãπÏãÝÏùò Ï∞® Î≤àÌò∏ÌåêÏùÄ 12Í∞Ä 3456Ïù¥ÏóêÏöî") yet cited it `[from car_license_plate]` ‚Äî the NOTE citation verb with the memory KEY ‚Äî which the exact-match note gate then false-stripped with a "Removed 1 citation ‚Ä¶ treat those claims as unverified" warning on a TRUE recalled fact. Root cause: the Korean query tokens ("Ï∞®", "Î≤àÌò∏Ìåê") don't lexically match the English fact key ("car", "license", "plate"), so selectMemoryFacts returns nothing and the `[memory: <topic>]`-hint grounding block isn't injected; the persona still lists the fact (so the model knows it) but, without the hint, the small model falls back to the note verb. This is the same class as the P38-10 contact-citation normalization, now for memory: a new normalizeMemoryCitations (packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts) rewrites a `[from <X>]` whose <X> EXACTLY matches a known memory fact key (separator- and case-insensitive) into `[memory: <X>]` BEFORE enforceAnswerCitations runs, while a real `[from note.md]` whose name is not a memory key is left untouched ‚Äî so a note citation is never mistaken for a memory, and the gate (validating against all the user's facts from P38-15) then keeps the corrected memory citation. Applied in commands-ask alongside normalizeContactCitations. Proof: 4 new unit tests in agent-core (rewrites `[from car_license_plate]`‚Üí`[memory: car_license_plate]` incl. a "Car License Plate" spacing variant; leaves `[from home.md]` / `[from projects/vpn.md]` untouched; the rewritten form flows through enforceAnswerCitations with zero strips; a no-op when there are no memory keys) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: `muse ask "ÎÇ¥ Ï∞® Î≤àÌò∏Ìåê Î≠êÏïº?"` run 3√ó ‚Üí ZERO "Removed citation" warning and the "üßÝ from what you told me: car_license_plate" receipt now shows; a Korean WiFi-note query still cites `[from home.md]` (a real note is not rewritten to memory). agent-core 112 files / 1377 tests + cli 165 files / 1755 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a Korean user can now recall a fact they told Muse and see it cited to memory, not stripped as if it were a fabricated note citation ‚Äî P38-17 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] A Korean task / reminder / event recall now keeps its citation instead of being false-stripped ‚Äî the lexical citation gate tokenizes Unicode, and a coverage-only miss is routed to the judge, not hard-failed (P38-18). Probing ÏßÑÏïà's real Korean actuation‚Üírecall loop: `muse remind add "ÎÇ¥Ïùº Ïò§ÌõÑ 3Ïãú" "ÏπòÍ≥º ÏòàÏïΩ Í∞ÄÍ∏∞"` + `muse tasks add "Î∂ÑÍ∏∞ Î≥¥Í≥ÝÏÑú ÏûëÏÑ±ÌïòÍ∏∞"` both stored fine, but `muse ask "ÎÇ¥Í∞Ä Ìï¥Ïïº ÌïÝ ÏùºÏù¥ Î≠êÍ∞Ä ÏûàÏñ¥?"` answered correctly and cited `[task: Î∂ÑÍ∏∞ Î≥¥Í≥ÝÏÑú ÏûëÏÑ±ÌïòÍ∏∞]` / `[reminder: ÏπòÍ≥º ÏòàÏïΩ Í∞ÄÍ∏∞]` (the EXACT Korean titles) ‚Äî yet the citation gate STRIPPED both ("Removed 2 citations") and the rubric verdict false-flagged the answer. Root cause: `lexicalTokens` ‚Äî the token-overlap basis that `resolvesByOverlap` uses to validate the non-note citation classes (tasks / reminders / events / sessions / contacts / commands / commits / memories / actions) ‚Äî split on `/[^a-z0-9]+/` (ASCII only), so "Î∂ÑÍ∏∞ Î≥¥Í≥ÝÏÑú ÏûëÏÑ±ÌïòÍ∏∞" tokenized to `[]` (empty) ‚Üí zero overlap with the Korean title ‚Üí a perfectly valid Korean citation looked unresolvable and was dropped. Two coordinated fixes in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts: (1) `lexicalTokens` now splits on Unicode `/[^\p{L}\p{N}]+/u` and KEEPS single-character CJK tokens (a 1-char Hanja/Hangul/Kana carries meaning) while still dropping 1-char Latin ‚Äî ASCII English tokenization is byte-for-byte unchanged (so no English regression); (2) because Unicode coverage of a CORRECT cross-lingual answer (Korean prose over English evidence) can legitimately dip below the coverage floor, `verifyGroundingWithReverify` now ESCALATES a confident, validly-cited coverage-only failure to the re-verification judge instead of hard-failing it ‚Äî the judge stays in the loop, so a WRONG cross-lingual value is still rejected, and a judge error fail-closes to ungrounded. Proof: 6 new agent-core unit tests (lexicalTokens tokenizes "Î∂ÑÍ∏∞ Î≥¥Í≥ÝÏÑú ÏûëÏÑ±ÌïòÍ∏∞" ‚Üí {Î∂ÑÍ∏∞, Î≥¥Í≥ÝÏÑú, ÏûëÏÑ±ÌïòÍ∏∞}, keeps single-char CJK "Ï∞®"/"Î≤àÌò∏Ìåê" but drops 1-char Latin x/y; the coverage-escalation upholds a correct cross-lingual answer to GROUNDED, keeps a wrong value UNGROUNDED when the judge rejects, fail-closes on a judge error, and does NOT escalate a coverage miss whose citation is INVALID) + the verify-claim-grounding battery still 6/6 on two consecutive runs (the cross-lingual correct/wrong cases route through the new branch) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the Korean task/reminder recall above is now clean (no "Removed citation", no "treat as unverified"); the cross-lingual WiFi recall (P38-16) is unregressed; and a Korean absent-fact "ÎÇ¥ Ïó¨Í∂å Î≤àÌò∏ Î≠êÏïº?" still refuses ("ÏÝïÎ≥¥ÏóêÎäî Ïó¨Í∂å Î≤àÌò∏Ïóê ÎåÄÌïú ÎÇ¥Ïö©Ïù¥ ÏóÜÏäµÎãàÎã§") with no fabrication. agent-core 112 files / 1383 tests + cli 165 files / 1755 tests + cited-recall 6/6 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a Korean-speaking user (or anyone whose tasks, reminders, and events are titled in their own language) now sees those recalls cited and un-warned instead of false-stripped as fabrications ‚Äî P38-18 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The grounding DRIFT verdict now runs under `muse ask --with-tools` too ‚Äî the agent (tool-using) recall path gets the same "treat as unverified" protection as chat-only, closing the one surface where "shows its work" was silent (P38-19). The recall edge's post-hoc rubric verdict (`groundingVerdictNotice` + the weak-band MaTTS reverify judge + the `--repair` offer) was gated `!options.withTools`, so a `muse ask --with-tools` answer that DRIFTED (asserted a value present in no source) printed confidently with NO grounding signal ‚Äî fabrication=0's "one deterministic grounding gate under EVERY surface" promise was literally false for the agent recall path. It had been skipped for a real reason: the verdict scores the answer against the CLI's pre-retrieval top-K notes (`scored`), but the `--with-tools` agent can pull a chunk via `knowledge_search` (often on a REFORMULATED query) that the top-K didn't include ‚Äî so scoring against `scored` alone would false-flag a legitimately grounded agent answer "treat as unverified". Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: the verdict guard drops from `!options.json && !options.withTools` to `!options.json` (so it runs on both paths), and a new pure, exported `augmentNoteEvidenceWithCited(baseNotes, citedSources, liveNotes)` augments the verdict's note evidence with the FULL text of every note the answer ACTUALLY cites (each already gate-validated against the live corpus by the citation gate above) ‚Äî so a note the agent retrieved outside the top-K is always covered. The augmentation is ADDITIVE ONLY: it can only prevent a false "ungrounded", never cause a false "grounded" ‚Äî a drifted value that appears in no cited note still scores uncovered ‚Üí ungrounded. Proof: 6 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-verdict-withtools.test.ts (pulls in a cited note's full chunks when the top-K missed it; ignores a note the answer never cited; never duplicates a chunk already in the base set; is a no-op when nothing or an invalid/stale source is cited; the additive-only invariant ‚Äî base evidence is never dropped or rewritten) + the existing verdict-source / grounding-verdict tests green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: a `muse ask --with-tools` answer asserting "WireGuard default MTU is 1420 [from net.md]" against a note that never states an MTU now fires "‚öÝÔ∏è Grounding check: this answer's claims aren't fully backed by your notes (low coverage rejected by re-verification) ‚Äî treat as unverified" + the `--repair` nudge (it was SILENT before this change); two grounded `--with-tools` answers (garage door code 4417, home wifi password) do NOT false-flag; and the chat-only path is byte-for-byte unchanged (only the `options.withTools && index` branch is new). cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who runs `muse ask --with-tools` for a recall question now gets the same honest drift warning (and constructive --repair) as the plain ask, so the agent path can no longer present a fabricated value as a confident sourced fact ‚Äî P38-19 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] `muse ask` no longer auto-saves the model's own answer as a durable "fact you told me" ‚Äî closing a provenance fabrication on the memory surface (P38-20). DISCOVERED live in P38-19's iteration and confirmed here: a `muse ask --with-tools` general-knowledge answer ("WireGuard default MTU is 1420") was silently persisted to `~/.muse/user-memory.json` as `wireguard_default_mtu: "1420"`, and the NEXT recall cited it `[memory: wireguard_default_mtu]` with the receipt "üßÝ from what you told me" ‚Äî i.e. Muse asserting the USER had stated a fact the MODEL fabricated from general knowledge. Root cause: the shared user-memory auto-extract HOOK (`createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook.afterComplete`) mines the ASSISTANT output (not just the user's statements), and it was installed globally so it ran on EVERY agent run including one-shot `muse ask` recall ‚Äî so a question-answer turn distilled the model's own assertion as a user fact (a second, latent vector also existed: the `remember_fact` write tool was exposed on the recall agent). Fixed by making recall read-only for durable memory: in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts the `--with-tools` agent run now sets `metadata.skipUserMemoryAutoExtract: true` (a new per-run opt-out the hook honors via a new exported `readSkipAutoExtract(context)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts ‚Äî early-returns before any extraction) AND `metadata.forbiddenToolNames: ["remember_fact"]` (defense in depth, via the existing exposure-layer block). Durable memory authoring stays with the explicit `muse remember` command (user-directed) and the conversational chat surface, whose auto-extraction is unchanged. Proof: 3 new memory unit tests in packages/memory/test/auto-extract-skip.test.ts (readSkipAutoExtract is true only when the flag is explicitly set; the hook writes NOTHING on an opted-out recall turn even when the extractor stub returns a fact-bearing payload; a normal/chat turn STILL extracts the fact ‚Äî so the skip is the ONLY behavior change, no chat regression) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the exact `muse ask --with-tools` WireGuard probe that wrote `wireguard_default_mtu` before now leaves NO memory file across two runs, while P38-19's drift verdict still fires ("treat as unverified"). memory 30 files / 312 tests + autoconfigure 73 files / 484 tests + cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who asks Muse a question can no longer have its general-knowledge answer silently turned into a fabricated "fact about you" that later recall presents as your own words ‚Äî P38-20 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] Chat auto-memory no longer stores a fact the MODEL asserted as "what you told me" ‚Äî the provenance gate now covers the conversational surface (P38-21). P38-20 closed this on one-shot `muse ask` (by skipping extraction), and flagged the residual: the SAME leak lives on `muse chat`, through a SEPARATE extractor (`extractMemoryFromTurn` in apps/cli/src/chat-auto-memory.ts) that also mines the assistant reply ‚Äî so a user who ASKS "what's WireGuard's default MTU?" and gets "1420" would have `wireguard_default_mtu: 1420` silently saved as their OWN fact, which a later recall cites "üßÝ from what you told me" (a fabricated provenance the user never stated). Fixed with a deterministic provenance gate (the same code-not-prompt shape as the citation gate): a new pure, exported `dropModelAssertedValues(record, userTurn, assistantOutput)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts drops a fact/preference iff ALL of its DISTINCTIVE value tokens appear in the assistant's reply and NONE appear in the user's own turn ‚Äî i.e. the value was demonstrably the model's assertion, not the user's words. A value the user actually stated (its token is in their turn) survives; an inferred boolean like `allergy_penicillin: yes` survives because "yes" carries no distinctive token (fail-open ‚Äî un-attributable values are kept, not dropped); a malformed array-shaped payload is left untouched for the existing sanitizer. - [Perception/Grounding edge] `muse ask --file` refuses a BINARY file instead of hallucinating content from its garbled bytes (P37-14). Probing the ad-hoc `--file` perception source with a real-shaped binary PDF: `muse ask --file resume.pdf "what is this person's job title?"` read the PDF's raw bytes as UTF-8 (the handler did `readFile(path, "utf8")`), injected the garbage as note-class grounding, and the local model HALLUCINATED a confident answer ‚Äî "The resume file mentions 'Senior Software Engineer' [from resume.pdf]" ‚Äî citing a value that appears NOWHERE in the file (it was pure binary stream bytes). A sourced fabrication on the perception surface, exactly what the "shows its work" edge forbids. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: a new pure, exported `looksLikeBinaryContent(bytes)` (deterministic, zero deps ‚Äî a NUL byte is the canonical text-vs-binary signal; failing that, a >10% U+FFFD replacement-char ratio from a lossy UTF-8 decode of the first 8 KB) classifies the `--file` payload BEFORE it is grounded. A binary file is NOT injected as evidence; instead the user gets a clear "--file <path> looks like a binary file (PDF, image, office doc, ‚Ä¶), not text ‚Äî I won't ground on it ‚Ä¶ extract the text first" message, and the answer honestly refuses rather than fabricating. A real text file is unaffected and still grounds + cites normally. Proof: 6 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-file.test.ts (a NUL byte, a PDF magic header + stream bytes, and an invalid-UTF-8 run all classify as binary; ASCII, valid UTF-8 Korean+emoji, and an empty file classify as text) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the identical binary-PDF probe now prints the refusal message and answers "I don't have enough information to determine this person's job title" (the fabricated "Senior Software Engineer" is GONE), while `muse ask --file resume.txt` still cites `[from resume.txt]` with the real value. cli 166 files / 1767 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who points `--file` at a PDF/image/doc now gets an honest "I can't read that as text" instead of a confidently fabricated answer attributed to their file ‚Äî P37-14 bullet
- [Perception/Knowledge] `muse ask --file <pdf>` now READS the PDF and answers from its real text ‚Äî a user can ask Muse about a PDF directly, grounded + cited (P37-15). P37-14 made a binary `--file` refuse rather than hallucinate; this upgrades the most common "binary" case ‚Äî a PDF ‚Äî into a real capability. The `--file` handler now detects a PDF (`isPdfDocument`: a `.pdf` extension OR the `%PDF-` magic header) and extracts its text via `pdf-parse` (the SAME MIT, pure-JS reader `muse read` already ships ‚Äî no new dependency, and it's dynamically imported so it loads only when a PDF is actually read), then grounds + cites it `[from <file>.pdf]` like any note. A non-PDF binary (image, archive, office doc) still hits the P37-14 binary refusal; a scanned/empty-text PDF or a malformed PDF refuses honestly (no fabrication from garbage bytes); a plain text/markdown file is unchanged. To avoid an import cycle (`commands-read.ts` already imports `consumeAskStream` from `commands-ask.ts`), the shared document extractor was moved to a new leaf module `apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts` (`parsePdfBuffer` / `isPdfDocument` / `isLikelyBinary` / `extractDocumentText` / `PdfParsed`) and re-exported from `commands-read.ts` so its existing consumers (notes-rag, watch-folder, their tests) are untouched. - [Grounding edge/Perception] A contact recall is no longer false-flagged "treat as unverified" when the model cites the raw `contact_<uuid>` id (P38-22). - [Actuation] `muse remind`/`tasks`/`calendar` understand an English day-part word + a specific hour ‚Äî "tonight at 8", "tomorrow morning at 9", "this evening at 7" (P40-9). The English counterpart of P40-8 (which fixed the Korean ÏïÑÏπ®/ÏÝÄÎÖÅ/Î∞§): a colloquial day-part word combined with an explicit hour was REJECTED. `muse remind add "tonight at 8"`, `"this evening at 7"`, `"tomorrow morning at 9"`, `"tomorrow evening at 6"`, `"tomorrow night at 10"`, and `"this morning at 8"` ALL failed with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase" ‚Äî everyday phrasings rejected ‚Äî even though the bare `"tomorrow morning"` resolved to 09:00. Root cause: three gaps in `resolveRelativeTimePhrase` (packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts) ‚Äî the standalone day-part path matched only a BARE word ("tonight" alone), the `dayPattern` mis-routed "tonight at 8" into the weekday branch (where "tonight" is not a weekday ‚Üí undefined), and `parseTimeOfDay` had no case for a "<day-part> at <hour>" spec like "morning at 9". Fixed with a new `dayPartBiasedTime(part, spec)` that lets the day-part word supply the AM/PM for a bare 1-12 hour (morning/this-morning ‚Üí AM; afternoon/evening/night/tonight ‚Üí PM), with the night edge handled (`tonight at 12` ‚Üí 00:00 midnight, vs afternoon/evening at 12 ‚Üí noon); it is wired through a new `standaloneDayPartTime` for the today-anchored forms ("this morning at 8" ‚Üí 08:00, "tonight at 8" ‚Üí 20:00) and a new day-part branch inside `parseTimeOfDay` for the day-headed forms ("tomorrow morning at 9", "monday evening at 6"). - [Perception/Knowledge] An HTML file is grounded on its readable TEXT (tags + script/style stripped, entities decoded), not raw tag-soup ‚Äî so `muse ask --file resume.html` / `muse read article.html` / `--file <folder-of-html>` work on HTML the way they do on text and PDFs (P37-17). Probing `--file` with an `.html` file exposed a real correctness defect: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` returned "jane&#64;globex.com" ‚Äî the HTML numeric entity `&#64;` (which is `@`) was never decoded, so the user got a MANGLED email ‚Äî and the üìé receipt showed raw `<html><head><style>‚Ä¶</style><script>‚Ä¶</script>` markup as the "source" (noisy, and it wastes the small model's context on tags/scripts). Root cause: every non-PDF `--file`/ingest path read the file bytes as UTF-8 verbatim, markup and all ‚Äî qwen coped with simple cases but the entities stayed mangled and large pages would bury the real content under markup. Fixed in apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts with a new pure, exported `htmlToText(html)` (regex-based, no DOM/parser dependency): it removes `<script>`/`<style>` blocks and HTML comments, strips the remaining tags, decodes the entities that actually corrupt grounded values (numeric `&#64;`, hex `&#x26;`, and the common named ones ‚Äî `&amp;`/`&lt;`/`&gt;`/`&quot;`/`&nbsp;`/`&mdash;`‚Ä¶), and collapses whitespace. `extractDocumentText` now routes `.html`/`.htm` through it, `.html`/`.htm` were added to `SUPPORTED_DOC_EXT` (so the directory walk for `muse read <dir>` / `muse ask --file <dir>` / `watch-folder --ingest` picks them up), and the single-`--file` path in commands-ask got the same branch (it has its own inline reader, applied AFTER the robust binary-refusal so a non-text binary is still refused). Proof: 4 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts (`isHtmlDocument` matches .html/.htm not .txt; tags + `<script>`/`<style>` bodies stripped and whitespace collapsed; numeric/hex/named entities decoded ‚Äî `jane&#64;globex.com` ‚Üí `jane@globex.com`, `a&#x26;b` ‚Üí `a&b`, `Globex &amp; Co &mdash; 2026` ‚Üí `Globex & Co ‚Äî 2026`; `extractDocumentText` reads an `.html` buffer as decoded text with no `<`) + the existing document-reader / read / notes-rag suites green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` now ‚Üí "jane@globex.com" with a CLEAN text receipt ("Jane Doe Email: jane@globex.com Job title: Principal Engineer at Globex & Co."), `muse read article.html --save-to-notes` saves "VPN Setup The MTU should be set to 1380 for WireGuard." (clean, no tags), and `muse ask --file <dir>` over a folder containing the HTML grounds on it and cites `[from article.html]`. cli 167 files / 1782 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now point Muse at an HTML file or a folder of them (a saved web article, an exported resume) and get a cited answer from its actual readable text with values intact, instead of a markup-polluted, entity-mangled one ‚Äî P37-17 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] A `[from <class>: ‚Ä¶]` structured citation (commit / task / event / reminder / ‚Ä¶) is no longer false-stripped ‚Äî the model's "from "-prefixed citation now survives the gate (P38-23). Probing the git-perception source (P37-11): `muse ask --git "what have I been working on recently?"` grounded on the user's real commits and answered correctly, citing a commit as `[from commit: feat(perception): muse ask grounds on the action log ‚Ä¶]` ‚Äî but the citation gate then STRIPPED it with "‚öÝÔ∏è Removed 1 citation(s) to source(s) you don't have (commit: ‚Ä¶) ‚Äî treat those claims as unverified" on a TRUE recall, making a correct git answer look unverified. Root cause: the local model frequently prepends the NOTE verb "from " to a STRUCTURED citation, but `enforceAnswerCitations`'s class regexes anchor on `[commit:` / `[task:` / `[event:` (with no "from "), and the note regex `[from <X>]` runs FIRST and mis-catches `[from commit: ‚Ä¶]` as a non-existent note, stripping it before the commit handler ever sees it. Same defect class as P38-22 (contacts) and P38-17 (memory), now generalised across every structured citation class. Fixed with a new pure, exported `normalizeFromPrefixedCitations(answer)` in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts that drops the redundant "from " before any known class keyword ‚Äî task / event / reminder / session / feed / contact / command / commit / memory / action ‚Äî rewriting `[from commit: X]` ‚Üí `[commit: X]` etc.; it is applied in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts BEFORE the contact/memory normalizers (so they see the de-prefixed form) and a real `[from note.md]` (no class keyword + ":") is never touched. - [Grounding edge/Perception] A past-SESSION recall cited by SLOT number ("[from session 1]") is no longer false-stripped ‚Äî the continuous-companion's "what did we discuss?" answers survive the gate (P38-24). - [Perception/Reach] `muse ask --url <url>` ‚Äî a user can now ask Muse about a public WEB PAGE, grounded on its readable text and cited, without ingesting it (P37-18). This is a NEW capability (Reach growth), the web counterpart of `--file`: `muse ask --url https://example.com "what is this domain for?"` fetches the page, extracts its readable text, grounds the answer on it cited `[from <host>]`, and an off-topic question honestly refuses rather than inventing page content. It reuses the existing SSRF-guarded `fetchReadableUrl` helper from @muse/mcp (the same one `muse notes ingest --url` already uses) ‚Äî it permits PUBLIC hosts only, re-checks the host after any redirect (so a redirect can't smuggle in a private/internal address), enforces a 15s timeout, and extracts readable text from HTML ‚Äî so there is no new fetch or egress machinery and the local-first posture is unchanged (the MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY gate governs LLM/voice egress, not reading a public web page the user explicitly asked about, which `outbound-safety.md` permits as "Muse may read the world freely"). - [Felt] The "empty notes" on-ramp stays silent when the query SUPPLIES its own grounding (`--file`/`--url`/`--git`/`--shell`) or the user has past sessions ‚Äî completing P35-9 (P35-10). - [Actuation] A BARE duration ‚Äî "2 hours", "30 minutes", "3 days", "2h", "a week" ‚Äî now parses as an offset from now across `remind`/`tasks`/`calendar`/`snooze`; the literal "in" is optional (P40-10). Probing the actuators surfaced a broad gap: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"`, `muse remind add "30 minutes" "call mom"`, and `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` ALL failed with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase" ‚Äî every bare duration was rejected, and ONLY the form WITH the literal word "in" ("in 2 hours") parsed. This is especially awkward for `--in "2 hours"`, where the word "in" is already in the flag name so repeating it ("--in 'in 2 hours'") reads wrong, and "in 2 hours" is one of the most natural ways a person states a reminder time. Root cause: the two duration handlers in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts ‚Äî the full-word "in N <unit>" form and the compact "in Nh/Nm/Nd/Nw" form ‚Äî both hard-required a leading `in\s+`. Fixed by making that prefix optional (`(?:in\s+)?`) in both regexes, so a bare "2 hours" / "30 minutes" / "3 days" / "a week" / "2h" / "90 mins" / "2w" now reads as that offset from the current time. The change is purely additive ‚Äî a bare duration was previously unrecognised, so nothing that parsed before changes ‚Äî and it preserves the existing disambiguation: a bare number with NO unit ("5") still means a 24-hour clock hour (today 05:00, not "5 of something"), and an unknown unit ("3 horses") still rejects, so there are no false positives. Proof: 4 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (bare full-word durations 2 hours/30 minutes/3 days/a week and bare compact 2h/90m/2d/2w each equal their explicit "in ‚Ä¶" form; "5" stays a clock hour; "3 horses" rejected) + the single mcp.test.ts assertion that had codified the OLD "a bare 1h is rejected" behavior updated to the new intended parse + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1330 tests) + the cli remind/tasks suites green (38) + LIVE on the loop PC: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"` ‚Üí +2h, `muse remind add "30 minutes" t` ‚Üí +30m, `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` ‚Üí +3 days, while "in 2 hours" and "5" (clock hour) are unregressed. mcp 167 files / 1330 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now write a reminder/task time the way they actually say it ("remind me in 2 hours" ‚Üí just "2 hours", or `--in "2 hours"`) instead of being forced to include the literal word "in" ‚Äî P40-10 bullet

- [Grounding edge/Perception] The feed and contact grounding markers now embed the canonical `[feed: ‚Ä¶]` / `[contact: ‚Ä¶]` citation, so the local model cites them correctly INLINE ‚Äî fixing the root cause that the P38-22 (contact) and P38-25 (feed) post-hoc normalizers had only patched on the buffered copy (P38-28). Tracing WHY the model kept citing feeds and contacts in non-canonical forms (`[feed 1]` by slot, `[from contact_<uuid>]` by raw id) revealed an inconsistency in how the grounding context is built: the task, event, reminder, memory, and commit markers each embed the exact canonical citation inside the marker (`<<event N ‚Äî provider>>\n<title>\n[event: <title>]\n<<end>>`), which the small local model then copies verbatim ‚Äî but the feed marker (`<<feed N ‚Äî name (date)>>\n<title>‚Ä¶`) and the contact marker (`<<contact N ‚Äî id>>\n<name> ‚Äî <fields>`) did NOT include the `[feed: ‚Ä¶]` / `[contact: ‚Ä¶]` line, so the model improvised a slot number or the raw id. Because the default `muse ask` (chat-only) path STREAMS the model's raw output token-by-token and only normalizes the BUFFERED copy afterward (for the gate + receipt), the user saw the ugly `[feed 1]` / `[from contact_<uuid>]` inline even though the receipts were correct ‚Äî the prior fixes never touched the streamed text. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts by adding `[feed: ${h.feedName}]` to the feed marker and `[contact: ${c.name}]` to the contact marker, matching the five markers that already embed their canonical citation; the P38-22/P38-24/P38-25 post-hoc normalizers remain as a safety net for the cases where the model still strays. - [Proactivity/Felt] Muse now notices the most common way you voice a commitment in passing ‚Äî "I'll ‚Ä¶" / "I will ‚Ä¶" / "I'm going to ‚Ä¶" / "I'm gonna ‚Ä¶" ‚Äî not just "I need to / have to / should" (P35-11). The SF-confidant "anticipates what you said you'd do" quality runs on the deterministic rule engine `detectUserCommitments` in packages/agent-core/src/commitment-detector.ts, which both `muse commitments scan` and `muse checkins scan` use to read recent chat (`~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl`) for things the user said they'd do and offer to track them / schedule a check-in. Its rules caught "I need to ‚Ä¶", "I have/got to ‚Ä¶", "I should ‚Ä¶", and the Korean Ìï¥Ïïº/ÌïòÍ∏∞Î°ú Ìñà forms ‚Äî but MISSED the single most common English way people state an intent: the future promise. A chat containing "I'll call the dentist tomorrow" or "I'm going to review the PR this afternoon" produced "No open commitments detected" ‚Äî Muse simply didn't see them. Fixed by adding two rules to the detector: `\bI(?:'ll|\s+will)\s+(‚Ä¶)` and `\bI(?:'m|\s+am)\s+(?:going\s+to|gonna)\s+(‚Ä¶)`, both mapped to a new `"will"` commitment kind at high confidence, with a small precision guard ‚Äî a `WILL_STATIVE_STARTERS` stoplist ({be, see, bet, say}) so a stative remark ("I'll be late", "I'll see", "I'll bet") is NOT mistaken for a task, and the existing interrogative filter still drops "Will I make it on time?" as a question. Proof: 2 new unit tests in packages/agent-core/test/commitment-detector.test.ts (all four intent forms ‚Äî I'll / I will / I'm going to / gonna ‚Äî detected as kind `will`/high; the stative and question forms detected as nothing) + the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1399 tests, so the new kind broke no exhaustive consumer) + the cli build green + LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: after seeding `~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl` with a user turn "Hey, I'll call the dentist tomorrow about the appointment", `muse commitments scan` now prints "Open commitments you mentioned (1): ‚Ä¢ call the dentist tomorrow about the appointment" (before this fix it reported "No open commitments detected in recent chat"). agent-core 112 files / 1399 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who says "I'll do X" (the way most people actually phrase a commitment) now has Muse notice it and offer to track it, instead of it slipping by ‚Äî P35-11 bullet
- [Proactivity/Actuation] A commitment's follow-up check-in now fires AFTER the timeframe you stated, instead of always tomorrow at 10:00 (P35-12). P35-11 made Muse NOTICE a commitment voiced in passing; this hardens the next stage ‚Äî the proactive follow-up that actually arrives in the user's channel. `muse checkins scan` reads recent chat for things the user said they'd do (via `detectUserCommitments`) and schedules a warm "how did it go?" nudge for each (delivered at its due time by `runDueCheckins`). The defect: `scheduleCheckins` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts hardcoded EVERY check-in's due time to `now.getDate() + 1` at `slotHour` (tomorrow 10:00) ‚Äî so "submit the tax forms THIS WEEK" and "renew my passport NEXT WEEK" both got a follow-up the very next morning, a premature nag days before the user would plausibly have acted. This is exactly the real-world failure mode the human-directed focus calls a USER-FACING reliability defect (a proven-once actuator that misbehaves on a natural input), not inward churn. Fixed with a new pure exported `followupDayOffset(commitment)` that reads the timeframe the user voiced in the commitment text ‚Äî EN + KO ‚Äî and returns the day offset to fire the check-in PAST it: "next week" / "Îã§Ïùå Ï£º" ‚Üí 8, "this week" / "Ïù¥Î≤à Ï£º" / "by <weekday>" ‚Üí 5, "tomorrow" / "ÎÇ¥Ïùº" / "next <weekday>" ‚Üí 2, and a same-day ("later today") or timeframe-less commitment ‚Üí 1 (the previous next-day default, so nothing that worked before changes). The `due` Date is now computed per-commitment inside the schedule loop (it was a single value hoisted above the loop), and the default id factory switched from a `due`-derived suffix to the batch index so it no longer depends on the hoisted value. The follow-up timing is deterministic code (no model call ‚Äî the commitment detection is rule-only too), fail-safe (an unrecognised timeframe simply defaults to next-day, never drops the check-in). - [Grounding edge] The recall verdict's wrong-value escalation now catches a drifted EMAIL ADDRESS, not just a wrong number or named entity ‚Äî closing the most dangerous contact-data drift (P38-29). P38-2 made `verifyGroundingWithReverify` escalate a `grounded`-scoring answer that asserts a NUMBER ("MTU 9000" vs the note's 1380) or a capitalized NAMED ENTITY ("Dr. Lee" vs "Dr. Park") absent from the evidence to one fail-OPEN judge pass (claim-level grounding, since whole-answer coverage can't see a single wrong token). But an EMAIL ADDRESS escaped BOTH checks: the lexical tokenizer splits "jane@acme.com" into lowercase parts (jane/acme/com), so a drifted DOMAIN ("acme" where the note says "globex") is neither a pure digit nor a capitalized entity ‚Äî meaning a confident, high-coverage, fully-cited answer asserting a WRONG contact email read `grounded` and was handed to the user as fact (verified live: the wrong-email answer scores base verdict grounded at confidence 1.00 with NO gate). For a contact / outbound surface that is the single most dangerous fabrication ‚Äî Muse confidently gives you a wrong address you might then email. Fixed in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts: `answerAssertsUnsupportedValue` now also extracts whole email addresses from the (citation-stripped) answer via `/[a-z0-9._%+-]+@[a-z0-9.-]+\.[a-z]{2,}/giu` and flags any not present VERBATIM in the joined raw evidence text (case-insensitive ‚Äî a real email is copied from a note, never reformatted), so a drifted email triggers the SAME fail-OPEN judge pass as a wrong number and is demoted to "I'm not sure" on an unsupported verdict. Scoped to emails (the clean, unambiguous, highest-value identifier; @handles/URLs deferred as noisier). Fail-open and zero-cost on the common path: a CORRECT email is present in evidence, so `emails.some(not-in-evidence)` is false and no extra judge pass fires ‚Äî only a genuinely drifted email pays for re-verification, and a judge error never demotes a correct answer. Proof: 2 new unit tests in packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-reverify.test.ts (a wrong-domain email "jane@acme.com" over evidence "jane@globex.com" demotes grounded‚Üíungrounded with the "value the evidence does not support" reason ‚Äî the value-escalation branch, confirmed by the base verdict being grounded@1.00; a verbatim-matching email never escalates, asserted with the `never` reverifier that throws if called) + the existing wrong-number / named-entity / cross-lingual escalation tests all still green + the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1401 tests) + cli build green (the ask wedge consumes the unchanged `verifyGroundingWithReverify` signature) + a real-LLM round-trip on qwen3:8b: `muse ask "what is Jane Park's email address?"` over a note holding "jane@globex.com" answers "Jane Park's email address is jane@globex.com [from contacts.md]" ‚Äî correct, cited, grounded, with its receipt and NO spurious grounding warning (the correct-email path is unbroken end-to-end). agent-core 112 files / 1401 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who asks Muse for a contact's email is now protected from a confidently-wrong address: if the local 8B drifts the domain, the answer is escalated and demoted to an honest "I'm not sure" instead of passing as grounded ‚Äî P38-29 bullet
- [Perception] A user can now ground Muse on whatever text they just COPIED ‚Äî `muse ask --clipboard "<question>"` answers from the clipboard, cited `[from clipboard]`, with an honest refusal off-topic (P37-19). This is a NEW read-only local perception source, the ephemeral sibling of `--file` (a saved file) and `--url` (a web page): you copy an article, an error message, a code snippet, or an email, then ask Muse about it immediately ‚Äî no file to save first. It routes through the SAME cited-recall + grounding gate as `--file`/`--url` rather than bypassing it: the clipboard text is chunked by the existing `selectFilePassages` ranking into `scored`, so the answer passes `enforceAnswerCitations` (only real sources cited) and the `groundingVerdictNotice` rubric, and an off-topic question gets the honest "I don't have that" refusal ‚Äî a NEW surface that is gated by construction (the user-locked "gate a new surface" done as perception growth, not another citation tweak).
