- [Grounding edge] The "shows its work" source receipt is now suppressed when the answer FAILS the grounding verdict, so the edge never vouches for a fabrication (P38-30). Falsifying P37-19 (`muse ask --clipboard`) surfaced a general edge-integrity hole on the chat-only ask path: the source receipt ("üìé From your notes (open to verify): ‚Ä¢ from clipboard ‚Äî '<chunk>'") was printed UNCONDITIONALLY and BEFORE the grounding verdict ran. So an off-topic question that the local model answered from its own parametric knowledge and cited to the grounded source ‚Äî e.g. over a clipboard holding a printer IP, "who won the 2018 world cup?" ‚Üí "The 2018 World Cup was won by France [from clipboard]" ‚Äî got BOTH a receipt that appeared to vouch for it AND a contradictory "‚öÝÔ∏è Grounding check: ‚Ä¶ treat as unverified" warning beneath. The receipt is the edge's flagship "shows its work" artifact; rendering it on an answer that failed its OWN grounding check lends false authority to precisely the un-groundable claim the edge promises to drop, and the two outputs (receipt says "grounded on clipboard", warning says "not backed") directly contradict. An ungrounded answer shows the warning (and `--repair` suggestion) ALONE, with no misleading receipt; a genuinely grounded answer keeps its full followable receipt unchanged. This affects EVERY grounding source (notes / `--file` / `--url` / `--clipboard` / contacts / tasks / events / reminders / sessions / feeds / memory / commands / commits / actions), not just the clipboard case that surfaced it. The change is a pure reorder + one guard ‚Äî no new machinery, no second model call, deterministic. - [Grounding edge] A source receipt's "open to verify" target is now REAL for an ad-hoc grounding source ‚Äî the actual page URL for a `--url` answer, and no fabricated path for a `--clipboard` answer (P38-31). Falsifying P38-30 surfaced the next integrity gap in the same flagship "shows its work" receipt: for an ad-hoc source (a fetched web page, the clipboard) the receipt's verify line was a FABRICATED local path. A `--url` answer's receipt pointed at `.muse/notes/example.com` and a `--clipboard` answer's at `.muse/notes/clipboard` ‚Äî neither file exists on disk (confirmed live: `ls` of the shown path returns "No such file or directory"), so the receipt's "(open to verify)" was a broken promise: it told the user to open a path that isn't there. Root cause: `formatSourceReceipts` computed the verify path as `join(notesDir, <cited-source-label>)` for any non-absolute source, blind to the fact that a URL host or the literal "clipboard" isn't a note under the notes directory. The fix can't key on `existsSync` (the existing unit tests legitimately assert path lines for synthetic paths that don't exist in the test sandbox), so the handler ‚Äî which KNOWS each source's type ‚Äî now records an `adHocVerifyTargets` map: the REAL `fetched.finalUrl` for a `--url` source (a link the user can actually open in a browser to verify the page the answer came from) and `null` for the ephemeral `--clipboard` source (nothing to open). `formatSourceReceipts` takes an optional `verifyTargets: ReadonlyMap<string, string | null>`: a present non-null value is rendered as the verify line (the URL), a present `null` renders the labelled snippet with NO path line, and an ABSENT entry ‚Äî every note and every `--file` ‚Äî falls through to the exact prior local-path logic (preferring the matched chunk's real absolute path), so notes and files are completely unchanged and no existing receipt test regresses. Proof: 2 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-receipts.test.ts (a `--url` source with a verify target renders the real `https://example.com/about` and NOT a `/home/u/.muse/notes/example.com` path; a `--clipboard` source with `null` renders the verbatim snippet with no fabricated `.muse/notes/clipboard` path) + all 28 existing receipt tests still green (notes / `--file` absolute-path behaviour unchanged) + the full @muse/cli suite green (168 files / 1808 tests) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): `muse ask --url https://example.com "what is this domain for?"` now prints the verify target "https://example.com/" (the real page, openable ‚Äî it was the un-openable ".muse/notes/example.com" before), and `muse ask --clipboard "where is the spare key?"` prints "‚Ä¢ from clipboard ‚Äî '<snippet>'" with NO path line. cli 168 files / 1808 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who gets a web- or clipboard-grounded answer can now actually FOLLOW the "open to verify" link (it's the real page URL) instead of being pointed at a local file that was never there ‚Äî P38-31 bullet
- [Actuation] A user can now set a reminder / task / event for a bare DAY-OF-MONTH ‚Äî "remind me on the 25th to pay rent", "add a task due the 15th", "rent is due the 1st" ‚Äî across `muse remind` / `tasks` / `calendar` / `snooze` (P40-11). Probing the natural-language date parser (`resolveRelativeTimePhrase` in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts) showed that "the 25th" / "on the 25th" / "the 1st" / "on the 15th at 3pm" ALL returned undefined and were rejected at the actuator with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase", even though "next monday" / "end of the month" / "in 2 weeks" worked ‚Äî yet a bare ordinal day-of-month is one of the most common ways people state a date ("rent is due on the 1st", "the meeting is the 15th"). The month-NAME date parser (`resolveAbsoluteMonthDate`) only handles "June 25" / "25 June"; a bare ordinal had no handler and fell through to undefined. Added a day-of-month handler: the regex `^(?:on\s+)?the\s+(\d{1,2})(?:st|nd|rd|th)(?:\s+(?:at\s+)?(.+))?$` resolves the phrase to the NEXT occurrence of that day-of-month ‚Äî this month if it hasn't passed yet (time-aware, so "the 25th at 9am" when 9am already passed today rolls to next month, never schedules in the past), otherwise next month; a day that doesn't exist in the current month (e.g. "the 31st" in a 30-day month) rolls onto the next month that has it via a getDate() guard; an impossible day ("the 99th" / "the 0th") is rejected outright rather than producing a silently rolled-over date; the time defaults to the same 9am bare-day hour every other date phrase uses, and an explicit "at 3pm" / "at 9am" is parsed via the shared `parseTimeOfDay`. The change is purely additive ‚Äî a bare ordinal was previously unrecognised, so nothing that parsed before changes (verified: "next monday" still lands on a Monday, "in 2 weeks" still +14 days, "next mango" still undefined). Proof: 6 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (a still-ahead day ‚Üí this month with getDate/getMonth/future assertions; a past day ‚Üí next month; an explicit "at 3pm" ‚Üí 15:00; the 9am default; "the 99th"/"the 0th" ‚Üí undefined; and weekday/duration non-regression) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1338 tests, including mcp.test.ts's 357 ‚Äî the other consumer of the parser, unregressed) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC: `muse remind add "on the 25th" "pay rent"` ‚Üí "Added [rem_‚Ä¶] pay rent ‚Äî due 2026-06-25 09:00" and `muse tasks add "submit report" --due "the 15th"` ‚Üí "due 2026-06-15 09:00", with `muse remind list` confirming the reminder landed at 2026-06-25 09:00 (both phrasings were REJECTED before this slice). mcp 167 files / 1338 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now schedule against the way they actually say a monthly date ("on the 25th") instead of being forced to write a full ISO timestamp or name the month ‚Äî P40-11 bullet
- [Actuation] A user can now schedule against a MONTH-QUALIFIED date ‚Äî "remind me on the 15th of next month", "task due the 1st of next month", "file taxes by end of next month" ‚Äî across `muse remind` / `tasks` / `calendar` / `snooze` (P40-12). P40-11 taught the parser the bare "the 25th" (the next occurrence of that day-of-month), but the natural way to pin a SPECIFIC relative month ‚Äî "the 15th of next month", "the 1st of this month", "end of next month" ‚Äî still returned undefined and was rejected at the actuator with "dueAt must be ‚Ä¶ a supported relative phrase". Unlike a bare day, this form has NO offset alternative: you cannot say "in N days" for "the 15th of next month" without knowing today's date and counting, so it is the higher-value half of the day-of-month story. Added two handlers in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts: (1) `^(?:on\s+)?the\s+(\d{1,2})(?:st|nd|rd|th)\s+of\s+(this|next)\s+month(?:\s+(?:at\s+)?(.+))?$` resolves the ordinal day within the named relative month (offset 0 for "this", +1 for "next"); it is placed BEFORE P40-11's bare "the Nth" handler because that handler's trailing `(.+)` time slot would otherwise greedily swallow "of next month", parse it as an invalid time, and fail the whole phrase ‚Äî ordering is load-bearing. An explicit month is honoured literally (so "the 1st of this month" returns this month's 1st even though it has passed ‚Äî the user named the month deliberately), and a getDate() guard rejects a day that doesn't exist in the target month (e.g. "the 31st of a 30-day month") rather than silently rolling it into the following month. (2) The existing "end of [the|this] month" handler was extended to also accept "next" (capturing the qualifier and applying a +1 month offset), so "end of next month" lands on the following month's last calendar day. Both default the time to the same 9am bare-day hour and honour an explicit "at 3pm". The change is purely additive ‚Äî these phrasings were previously unrecognised ‚Äî and the bare "the 25th", "end of the month", weekday, and duration phrases are all unregressed (verified). Proof: 6 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (a next-month pin ‚Üí July with getDate/getMonth assertions; a this-month literal even when past; an explicit "at 3pm" ‚Üí 15:00; "end of next month" ‚Üí July 31; "the 99th of next month" ‚Üí undefined; and bare-day-of-month / "end of the month" non-regression) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1344 tests, including mcp.test.ts's 357 ‚Äî the parser's other consumer, unregressed) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC (reference 2026-06-03): `muse remind add "the 15th of next month" "quarterly review"` ‚Üí "Added [rem_‚Ä¶] quarterly review ‚Äî due 2026-07-15 09:00" and `muse tasks add "file taxes" --due "end of next month"` ‚Üí "due 2026-07-31 09:00" (both REJECTED before this slice). mcp 167 files / 1344 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now name the month a date falls in ("the 15th of next month", "end of next month"), the one common date phrasing that has no relative-offset shortcut ‚Äî P40-12 bullet
- [Proactivity/Felt] A user can now CANCEL a proactive check-in ‚Äî `muse checkins cancel <id>` ‚Äî so the daemon stops asking "how did it go?" about something already done or unwanted (P35-13). P35-11/12 taught Muse to notice a commitment the user voiced in passing and schedule a warm follow-up nudge (`muse checkins scan` ‚Üí a due-windowed "Following up ‚Äî you mentioned you'd '‚Ä¶'. How did it go?" the daemon later delivers). But there was NO way to SILENCE one: if you'd already called the dentist, or never wanted the nudge, the check-in would still fire ‚Äî and a proactive system you can't opt out of is a nag, not a confidant. The `"cancelled"` status already existed in `CheckinStatus` and was honoured by `runDueCheckins` (it fires only `status === "scheduled"`) and `scheduleCheckins` (a cancelled source doesn't block a future re-mention), but nothing could SET a check-in to cancelled from the CLI, and `muse checkins list` didn't even display the id you'd reference. Added a pure exported `cancelCheckin(checkins, idOrPrefix)` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts: it matches by exact id OR a UNIQUE id prefix (the convenience, since list now shows the full id), refuses an AMBIGUOUS prefix rather than cancelling the wrong check-in, and returns a structured reason (not-found / ambiguous / already-fired / already-cancelled) instead of silently pretending to succeed; on success it returns the updated list with that one check-in flipped to `cancelled`. Wired as `muse checkins cancel <id>` (reads the store, calls the helper, writes back only on a real change, with a clear success/explanatory message and a `--json` form), and `muse checkins list` now prints `  ‚Ä¢ [<id>] <question> (<when>)` so the id is visible to cancel by. Because `runDueCheckins` already fires only scheduled check-ins, a cancelled one is deterministically excluded from delivery ‚Äî the daemon will not ask about it. Proof: 4 new unit tests in packages/mcp/test/commitment-checkin.test.ts (cancel by exact id flips only that one, leaving a sibling scheduled; cancel by a unique prefix resolves to the right id; an ambiguous prefix returns reason "ambiguous" with the match count and mutates nothing; not-found / already-fired / already-cancelled each report without mutating, and an empty needle is not-found) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1348 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite green (168 files / 1808 tests) + a LIVE end-to-end round-trip on the loop PC: seeding `~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl` with "I need to call the dentist" + "I have to renew my passport", `muse checkins scan` schedules both, `muse checkins list` shows each with its `[chk_‚Ä¶]` id, `muse checkins cancel <dentist-id>` prints "Cancelled check-in [chk_‚Ä¶] ‚Äî '‚Ä¶' won't fire.", the scheduled list afterward shows ONLY the passport check-in (the dentist one is gone from scheduled), and `muse checkins cancel chk_nope` prints "No scheduled check-in matches 'chk_nope'. Run `muse checkins list` to see ids." mcp 167 files / 1348 tests + cli 168 files / 1808 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now dismiss a proactive nudge for something they already handled instead of being asked about it, which is the opt-out that makes Muse's proactivity calm rather than naggy ‚Äî P35-13 bullet
- [Proactivity/Felt] A user can now SNOOZE a proactive check-in ‚Äî `muse checkins snooze <id> <when>` ‚Äî deferring "how did it go?" to a later time instead of only cancelling it (P35-14). - [Proactivity/Felt] A user's morning brief (`muse brief`) now surfaces the follow-ups they're DUE on ‚Äî things they said they'd do whose check-in has come due ‚Äî so the proactivity payoff reaches the pull surface, not only the background daemon (P35-15). P35-11..14 built the full commitment ‚Üí check-in arc: detect what the user voiced in passing ("I need to call the dentist"), schedule a warm "how did it go?" follow-up, and cancel/snooze it. But the ONLY thing that delivered a due check-in to the user was the background daemon's `runDueCheckins`. A user who runs `muse brief` each morning (the JARVIS-style summary) but doesn't run the daemon would never see the follow-up ‚Äî the entire flow's payoff was invisible in the surface they actually use, making P35-11..14 dead weight for the common pull-surface user. Fixed by adding a pure exported `selectDueCheckins(checkins, nowMs, max=10)` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts ‚Äî the SCHEDULED check-ins whose dueAt has passed, sorted soonest-due-first and capped ‚Äî and refactoring the daemon's `runDueCheckins` to use it (so the daemon's push and the brief's pull resolve the EXACT same due set; the refactor also gives the daemon a soonest-first ordering it lacked). `muse brief` (apps/cli/src/commands-brief.ts) now reads the check-ins store via `checkinsFile()` and `selectDueCheckins`, adds a "Follow-ups you're due on (things the user said they'd do): N" section to the deterministic fact sheet it hands the model ‚Äî each as "¬∑ <commitment> (mentioned <date>)" ‚Äî and a new system-prompt line instructs the JARVIS summary to gently surface a time-sensitive personal commitment over a routine task; the read is fail-soft (a missing/unreadable checkins file leaves the brief working on tasks/events/reminders as before). The user can then act on a surfaced follow-up with `muse checkins cancel/snooze <id>` (P35-13/14), so the pieces compose: the brief shows what's due, the management commands let you dismiss or defer it. Proof: 2 new unit tests in packages/mcp/test/commitment-checkin.test.ts (`selectDueCheckins` returns only scheduled-and-past-due check-ins soonest-first, excluding a future one, a fired one, and a cancelled one; respects the cap and an empty list) + the existing `runDueCheckins` tests still green (the shared-selector refactor preserved its behaviour) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1353 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite green (168 files / 1808 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): seeding `~/.muse/checkins.json` with a check-in whose dueAtIso is yesterday for "call the dentist", `muse brief` opens "Good afternoon. You're due to call the dentist, which you mentioned on May 31st. It's time to follow through with that commitment." (before this slice the brief never mentioned check-ins ‚Äî they lived only in the daemon). mcp 167 files / 1353 tests + cli 168 files / 1808 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who reads their morning brief now sees the commitments they're overdue on, instead of that follow-up reaching them only through a daemon they may never run ‚Äî P35-15 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Reach] `muse ask --url` (and `muse notes ingest --url`) now REFUSE to ground on a non-text resource ‚Äî a PDF / image / binary URL ‚Äî instead of reading its garbled bytes and hallucinating a confident, cited answer from them (P38-32). The shared web-read core `fetchReadableUrl` in packages/mcp/src/fetch-readable-url.ts (behind both the `--url` ask grounding and the `--url` notes ingest) read EVERY response body via `response.text()` with NO content-type check, then ran HTML tag-stripping over it. So a URL pointing at a PDF, an image, or an application/octet-stream decoded its binary bytes to garbled text, which the local model would then ground on, invent plausible-sounding content from, and cite to the URL ‚Äî exactly the fabrication the edge exists to prevent, and for the ingest path a way to poison the notes corpus with garbage. Fixed by adding a pure exported `isReadableContentType(contentType)` that gates on the response's declared `content-type`: text/* , application/xhtml+xml, application/xml, anything ending `+xml` (RSS/Atom/XHTML), and application/json (incl. ld+json) are groundable text; a declared binary type (application/pdf, image/*, application/octet-stream, audio/*, video/*, font/*, application/zip) makes `fetchReadableUrl` return `{ ok: false, error: "not a readable text page (content-type: <type>)" }`. A MISSING content-type is not trusted blindly ‚Äî it falls through to a binary-content sniff backstop (a NUL byte, or >10% U+FFFD replacement chars in the first 4KB of the decoded body, mirrors the `--file` binary refusal) so a binary body served under a wrong/absent content-type is still refused. No CLI change was needed: the `muse ask --url` branch already renders an `!ok` fetch result as "muse: could not fetch --url ‚Ä¶ (<error>) ‚Äî I won't ground on it", so the new refusal flows straight to the user. Proof: 6 new tests in packages/mcp/test/fetch-readable-url.test.ts exercising the REAL fetchReadableUrl path with only the network faked (contract-faithful per outbound-safety.md): a PDF content-type refuses with "application/pdf" in the message; an image/png refuses; an application/json and a text/plain response are allowed and their text grounded; a binary body (NUL bytes) served as text/html is caught by the sniff with "binary content"; and `isReadableContentType` allows the whole text family plus an empty type while refusing 8 distinct binary types ‚Äî plus the existing SSRF / redirect / retry tests all still green + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1359 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC against a REAL URL: `muse ask --url https://arxiv.org/pdf/2310.11511 "what is this paper about?"` now prints "could not fetch --url https://arxiv.org/pdf/2310.11511 (not a readable text page (content-type: application/pdf)) ‚Äî I won't ground on it", whereas `muse ask --url https://example.com` still fetches and grounds on the HTML page. mcp 167 files / 1359 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user who points Muse at a PDF, image, or other binary URL now gets an honest "I won't ground on it" instead of a confident answer fabricated from binary garbage, and the same protection keeps a binary URL from poisoning the corpus on ingest ‚Äî P38-32 bullet
- [Actuation/Reliability] A rate-limited outbound reminder/notice (HTTP 429 + Retry-After) is now actually DELIVERED instead of silently dropped ‚Äî the send-retry layer waits the server-mandated Retry-After rather than burning its 3 fixed attempts in ~1 second (P41-1). `sendWithRetry` in packages/mcp/src/messaging-retry.ts is the single retry path behind EVERY outbound firing loop ‚Äî reminders, follow-ups, pattern notices, proactive notices, situational briefings, standing-objective sends, ambient nudges, and web-watch alerts (one helper, eight surfaces). It used a fixed `[0, 200, 800]ms` backoff ladder, and its catch only inspected `cause.retryable` ‚Äî it NEVER read the server's `Retry-After`. So when Telegram/Slack/Discord/LINE answered a send with `429 + Retry-After: 30`, the retry fired again at 200ms then 800ms, was throttled all three times, and the message was DROPPED ‚Äî the user simply never received their 9am reminder, with no error they'd see. `MessagingProviderError` (packages/messaging/src/errors.ts) carried `status` but had no retry-after field, and its own doc-comment acknowledged "429 + Retry-After ‚Ä¶ retry-with-backoff is the right response" even as the send path ignored the hint. Fixed end-to-end: (1) a new `retryAfterMs?` field on `MessagingProviderError` (validated finite & non-negative); (2) populated at all four HTTP providers' send-failure throws ‚Äî telegram/slack/discord/line ‚Äî via a new exported `retryAfterMsFromResponse(response, bodyRetryAfterSeconds?)` that prefers a provider's body `retry_after` (Telegram returns the wait in the body `parameters.retry_after`, in seconds) and otherwise parses the `Retry-After` response header through a renamed/clarified `parseRetryAfterMs` (the old `parseRetryAfterSeconds` already returned ms despite its name); (3) `sendWithRetry` now, on a caught retryable `MessagingProviderError` carrying `retryAfterMs`, sleeps that server-mandated delay ‚Äî capped at 30s so a hostile or absurd hint can't hang a firing loop ‚Äî instead of the ladder value, and falls back to the unchanged `[0,200,800]` ladder when no hint is present so a plain transient 5xx is completely unregressed; the `sleep` is injectable so the test asserts the delay with no real wall-clock wait. This is the human-directed "harden the one-of-each actuators into daily-reliable integrations against rate-limit / transient-5xx" mandate, classified as outward reliability work, not churn. Proof (fully deterministic ‚Äî contract-faithful HTTP fakes + injected sleep spy per outbound-safety.md, ZERO dependence on the local model): 4 new tests in packages/mcp/test/messaging-retry.test.ts (a 429 carrying retryAfterMs=3000 makes sendWithRetry sleep 3000 ‚Äî not BACKOFFS_MS[1]=200 ‚Äî then deliver on the next attempt; a 1-hour hint is capped to 30000; a hint-less 503 still uses the [200,800] ladder unchanged; a non-retryable 400 still short-circuits with no sleep) + a Discord provider test (a 429 response with `Retry-After: 7` header ‚Üí the thrown MessagingProviderError carries retryAfterMs===7000 and retryable===true) + a Telegram provider test (a 429 with body `parameters.retry_after: 12` ‚Üí retryAfterMs===12000) + 2 helper tests for parseRetryAfterMs (numeric seconds ‚Üí ms, garbage/missing ‚Üí undefined) and retryAfterMsFromResponse (body wins over header, header fallback, neither ‚Üí undefined) + the existing send/retry/runDueReminders tests all still green + the full @muse/messaging suite (368 tests) and @muse/mcp suite (168 files / 1363 tests) green + cli build green. mcp 168 files / 1363 tests + messaging 368 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user whose reminder or proactive notice hits a provider rate limit now receives it a tick or two later, on every outbound surface, instead of silently losing it ‚Äî P41-1 bullet
- [Actuation/Safety] `muse messaging send` is now draft-first, fail-closed, and action-logged ‚Äî an ungated autonomous third-party send is closed (P41-2). The CLI's `messaging send --local <provider> <destination> <text>` (Telegram / Discord / Slack / LINE) called `registry.send(...)` DIRECTLY ‚Äî no draft-first confirmation, no approval gate, no action-log entry ‚Äî even though the sibling `muse email send` was fully draft-first/confirm-gated/logged. That is precisely the autonomous send to a third party that `.claude/rules/outbound-safety.md` and CLAUDE.md classify as never-allowed ("Outbound to a third party ‚Ä¶ is fail-close & draft-first ‚Ä¶ never an autonomous send"); the gap was that the already-built and already-tested `sendMessageWithApproval` helper (packages/mcp/src/message-send.ts ‚Äî draft-first, fail-closed gate, mandatory action-log of sent OR refused) had been wired into the agent tool (loopback-messaging.ts) but NEVER into the human CLI surface. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-messaging.ts: the `--local` send now routes through `sendMessageWithApproval` with a default terminal approval gate that prints the EXACT draft ("Send via <provider> ‚Üí <destination>: <text>") and proceeds only on an explicit confirm; every outcome is appended to the personal action log (a `refused` entry on denial, a `performed` entry on send) so the send is on the record and subject to undo/veto like any other action; a new `--user <id>` option tags the log entry; and the default gate FAIL-CLOSES when no interactive terminal is present (a non-TTY / piped / scripted / CI context returns "no interactive terminal to confirm the send" and refuses, rather than hanging on stdin waiting for input or ‚Äî worse ‚Äî sending unconfirmed). A `deps` seam (approvalGate / registry / actionLogFile) injects the gate and a fake registry for deterministic testing. The API (non-`--local`) path is unchanged ‚Äî it is gated server-side by the runtime tool-approval gate. Also exported `sendMessageWithApproval` (+ its types) from the @muse/mcp index, which had been import-only. Proof: 3 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-messaging-send.test.ts driving the REAL CLI command over a recording fake registry + an injected gate (a contract-faithful fake, never a stubbed registry, per outbound-safety.md; zero model or network dependence): a DENIED gate leaves the recording registry untouched (NOTHING sent), prints "Not sent (denied)", exits non-zero, and appends a `refused` action-log entry with `what: "message via telegram to chat123"`; a gate that THROWS is treated as a denial (still no send ‚Äî fail-closed); an APPROVED gate sends exactly `{ destination, text }` and appends a `performed` entry ‚Äî plus the existing program.test.ts `--local` round-trip updated to assert that a non-TTY send now fail-closes ("Not sent", zero provider API calls) instead of sending unconfirmed. cli 169 files / 1811 tests + mcp 168 files / 1363 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user (or a stray script) can no longer fire a message to a third party from the Muse CLI without seeing and confirming the exact content first, and every send or refusal is recorded ‚Äî P41-2 bullet
- [Knowledge] A user can now `muse notes rename <from> <to>` and have every `[[wiki-link]]` pointing at that note automatically rewritten across the whole corpus ‚Äî renaming a note no longer silently breaks its backlinks (P42-1). `muse notes` had list / read / search / save / append / delete but NO rename or move, while Muse already builds a note link graph (`buildNoteLinkGraph`), surfaces backlinks, and AUDITS for broken links (`auditNoteGraph`) ‚Äî yet offered no remedy, so moving or renaming a note orphaned every `[[link]]` pointing at it (and `auditNoteGraph` would then just report them as broken). Added a pure exported `rewriteWikiLinkReferences(body, oldTarget, newTarget)` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that rewrites the TARGET portion of each `[[‚Ä¶]]` reference, preserving any `|alias` and `#section` suffix, matching the target case-insensitively (the same key rule `extractWikiLinks` uses), and never on a partial match (`[[ideabank]]` is left alone when renaming `ideas`); plus a `renameNoteWithLinkRewrite(notesDir, fromPath, toPath, dryRun)` orchestration and a `muse notes rename <from> <to> [--dry-run] [--json]` command. The command renames the file, walks the entire notes tree rewriting `[[<basename>]]` references to it, refuses a missing source or an existing destination (no silent clobber) and any path that escapes the notes directory (a `..` traversal guard), counts how many links across how many notes were rewritten, and `--dry-run` reports exactly what WOULD change without touching anything. The link target is the renamed note's basename without `.md` (the bare `[[note]]` convention); the operation is local-only (a direct corpus mutation, no API/model). - [Grounding edge/Felt] The morning brief (`muse brief`) is now grounded against your schedule ‚Äî it can't tell you about a meeting TIME that isn't on your calendar without flagging it, extending the fabrication=0 gate to the one surface that lacked it (P38-33). The brief was the only `muse ask`-style surface with NO grounding gate: its JARVIS-style summary is model-composed prose streamed straight to stdout from a deterministic fact sheet (tasks / events / reminders / due check-ins), so the local model drifting or inventing an appointment time ‚Äî "don't forget your dentist at 5pm" when nothing is at 5pm ‚Äî would pass as fact on the flagship felt surface a user reads first thing each morning. Added a pure exported `unscheduledTimesInBrief(briefProse, factSheet, nowMinutes)` in apps/cli/src/commands-brief.ts that extracts clock times from BOTH the composed brief and the fact sheet and returns any time the brief asserts that appears on neither the schedule nor the current clock. It is format-robust: an internal `clockTimesToMinutes` normalises 12-hour ("3pm", "3:30 p.m.", "7:45am") and 24-hour ("15:00", "09:30") forms to minutes-since-midnight (with a negative lookahead so "3:30 pm" isn't double-counted as a bare 03:30), so a faithful time the model rendered in EITHER format matches the fact sheet's 24-hour times ‚Äî the property that makes the check safe to run on the flagship surface. The allowed set is the fact sheet's times plus the current clock (so an "it's 9:30am" greeting is never flagged). The brief action runs the gate on the streamed-then-collected answer and, if any unscheduled time is found, appends a stderr warning ("‚öÝÔ∏è This summary mentions a time not on your schedule (‚Ä¶) ‚Äî double-check it against your calendar before relying on it"); the gate is FAIL-OPEN (it warns, never blocks or regenerates the brief) and deliberately ZERO-false-positive ‚Äî a time it can't parse, a relative phrase ("in 2 hours"), a scheduled time in any format, and the current clock are all allowed, because a false warning on the morning briefing would erode trust worse than the original gap. It catches a wholly-fabricated time (one nowhere on the schedule); a drift to a time that happens to be elsewhere on the schedule (e.g. an event's end time) is the accepted precision trade for the zero-false-positive guarantee. Proof: 5 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-brief.test.ts (a brief echoing scheduled 12h/24h times + the current clock + a relative "in 2 hours; 3 tasks open" flags NOTHING; "dentist at 5pm" and "standup at 7:45am" ‚Äî neither on the schedule ‚Äî are flagged; an invented "call at 2pm" on an EMPTY schedule is flagged while "it's 9:30, nothing scheduled" is not; repeated "5pm ‚Ä¶ 5 pm" dedupes to one) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1821 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): seeding a reminder due at 17:42, `muse brief` opened "Good afternoon. You have a dentist appointment scheduled for 17:42." with NO time warning ‚Äî the model echoed the real 17:42 and the gate correctly stayed silent (zero false positive end-to-end on a real faithful brief). cli 169 files / 1821 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî Muse's morning briefing now plugs into the same fabrication=0 grounding edge as recall, reflection, and council, so it can't quietly tell you about a meeting you don't actually have ‚Äî P38-33 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The end-of-session episode summary is now gated against its own transcript ‚Äî a fabricated "decision" the conversation never contained is DROPPED instead of persisted as a citable memory, closing the edge's last ungated surface and its first INGEST one (P38-34). Every OUTPUT surface that emits a claim about the user's world ‚Äî recall (`muse ask`), reflection, swarm council, and the morning brief ‚Äî already passes through the deterministic grounding+citation gate, but the one INGEST surface did not: when a chat session ends, `captureEndOfSessionEpisode` (apps/cli/src/chat-end-session.ts) calls `summariseSession` ‚Äî whose `SUMMARISER_SYSTEM_PROMPT` explicitly asks the local model for "WHAT the user decided or where the matter stands" and "ANY explicit follow-up the user asked for" ‚Äî and then persisted that model-written free text via `upsertEpisode` after ONLY re-scrubbing credential shapes, with NO faithfulness check against the transcript. That summary later becomes a citable `[session: ‚Ä¶]` source that `enforceAnswerCitations` and the recall stack trust as ground truth, so a hallucinated decision in the summary (e.g. the model writing "the user decided to book a flight to Tokyo on Friday" for a session that only discussed a Q3 budget memo) would later be served back to the user as a CITED fact ‚Äî a fabrication entering through the back door, behind every output gate. Fixed with a pure exported `summaryGroundedInTranscript(summary, turns, floor)` in packages/agent-core/src/episodic-summariser.ts that measures the fraction of the summary's content tokens ‚Äî via `lexicalTokens`, the exact tokeniser the recall gate uses ‚Äî that occur anywhere in the transcript turns, returning false when it falls below the floor (i.e. the summary talks about things the session never did); `captureEndOfSessionEpisode` now calls it after summarising and DROPS the episode ("summary not grounded in the session transcript ‚Äî dropped to avoid persisting a fabricated memory", status skipped) rather than writing it. The floor (`DEFAULT_EPISODE_GROUNDING_FLOOR = 0.25`) is deliberately LENIENT: a faithful paraphrase adds framing words ("decided", "discussed") absent from the transcript so its coverage sits well below 1, and silently dropping a real memory is worse than keeping a borderline one (the recall gate still applies downstream when it is recalled), so the floor only has to be high enough to reject a WHOLESALE fabrication (which scores ~0 coverage) and low enough never to drop a real but terse summary. This is the edge's FIRST gate on ingest rather than output ‚Äî extending "one deterministic grounding gate under EVERY surface" to the memory-write path. Proof (fully DETERMINISTIC ‚Äî no live model is involved in the check, the model's summary is the INPUT being gated): 4 new unit tests in packages/agent-core/test/episodic-summariser.test.ts (a faithful Q3-budget-memo/Notion summary whose content is drawn from the transcript ‚Üí grounded=true; the "book a flight to Tokyo" fabrication over that same transcript ‚Üí false; an empty transcript is un-groundable ‚Üí false and an empty summary asserts nothing ‚Üí true; an explicit stricter/looser floor is honoured) + a new surface assertion on the EXISTING captureEndOfSessionEpisode harness in apps/cli/test/program.test.ts (a stub provider returning a fabricated Tokyo-travel summary over a Q3-memo transcript is DROPPED with status "skipped" and reason containing "not grounded", and the on-disk episodes.json stays at exactly one entry ‚Äî the fabricated episode never lands), while the existing happy-path capture and the secret-scrub test both stay green (the scrub test's seeded transcript enriched so its summary remains grounded, since that test is about scrubbing not grounding) + the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1405 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1821 tests). agent-core 112 files / 1405 tests + cli 169 files / 1821 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî Muse can no longer quietly remember, and then cite back to you, a decision or follow-up you never actually made ‚Äî P38-34 bullet
- [Perception] A user can now `muse ask --file <message>.eml` (or `muse read` it, or include it in a folder ingest) and ground on the saved email's DECODED subject + readable body, instead of raw RFC822/MIME (P37-20). `muse read` / `muse ask --file` already handled PDFs (parsed), HTML (readable text), and plain text, but a saved email file (`.eml`) fell through to `bytes.toString("utf8")` ‚Äî so the local model was handed the raw message: RFC822 headers, `multipart/alternative` boundaries, and a `quoted-printable` or `base64` body (`Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable` ‚Ä¶ `drop by 5=25 before Friday`), which buries the actual content under transport encoding and makes a grounded answer cite mangled text. A full RFC822/MIME parser already existed in the codebase ‚Äî `parseHeaders`, `extractBody` (multipart ‚Üí first text/plain part, quoted-printable/base64 decoded, HTML stripped), and `decodeHeaderValue` (RFC2047 encoded-word `=?UTF-8?B?‚Ä¶?=` subjects) in apps/cli/src/mbox-ingest.ts ‚Äî but it was wired only into the `--mbox` chat ingest, never the `--file` grounding path. Added two small functions to apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts that REUSE that parser: `isEmlDocument(filePath)` (extension-based, `.eml`) and `emlToText(rawEml)`, which emits the decoded `Subject:` / `From:` / `Date:` header lines followed by the decoded readable body. `extractDocumentText` (the shared `muse read` / `--file` extractor) now routes a `.eml` through `emlToText` right after the PDF check and BEFORE the binary-refusal check (an .eml's text headers never trip the binary heuristic, and a base64 part inside is exactly what the parser decodes), the `muse ask --file` branch in commands-ask.ts does the same, and `.eml` was added to `SUPPORTED_DOC_EXT` so a directory of saved emails ingests too. Nothing else changed ‚Äî PDF/HTML/text/binary handling is untouched. Proof: 3 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts (`isEmlDocument` matches only `.eml` case-insensitively; `emlToText` on a multipart message decodes the `=?UTF-8?B?UTMgYnVkZ2V0IOKAlCByZXZpZXc=?=` subject to "Q3 budget ‚Äî review", picks the text/plain part over the text/html part, unwinds `5=25`‚Üí`5%`, joins a soft line break, and turns `headcount=3F`‚Üí`headcount?` with no raw `=3F` or HTML left; `extractDocumentText` returns one page of clean text carrying "Q3 budget" and no "Content-Transfer-Encoding") + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1824 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): a `.eml` whose quoted-printable body says "The Q3 budget must drop by 5=25 before Friday. Confirm the headcount of 47.", `muse ask --file msg.eml "by how much must the Q3 budget drop?"` answers "The Q3 budget must drop by 5% [from msg.eml]." with the receipt showing the DECODED body (raw-text grounding would have shown "5=25" and the MIME headers). cli 169 files / 1824 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now point Muse at a saved email and ask about it, grounded on the message itself, the same way `--file` already works for a PDF or `--url` for a web page ‚Äî P37-20 bullet
- [Knowledge] A user can now run `muse notes fix-links` to repair broken `[[wiki-links]]` across their notes ‚Äî each broken/typo'd link is snapped to its unique closest existing note, while ambiguous or genuinely-missing ones are safely left alone (P42-2). Muse's note link graph already DETECTS broken links (`auditNoteGraph` returns a `brokenLinks` list of `[[target]]` references that resolve to no note) but only ever PRINTED them ‚Äî there was no remediation, so a typo'd `[[concpets]]` or a link left dangling after a manual edit / import stayed broken and the user had to hunt and fix each by hand. Added a pure exported `planLinkFixes(brokenTargets, existingIds, maxDistance)` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that, for each broken target, finds existing note ids within `maxDistance` edits (reusing the existing `levenshteinDistance`) and snaps it to the match ‚Äî but ONLY when there is EXACTLY ONE candidate at the closest distance; a target with two equally-close notes (an ambiguous typo) or no near match is returned as `unresolved` rather than silently mis-linked to the wrong note (the wrong-snap is the one real risk of a fuzzy repair, so it is fenced off by construction). The default `maxDistance` is 2 (catches a transposition or a one/two-character slip), case-insensitive, with deduped targets. A `fixBrokenLinks(notesDir, dryRun, maxDistance)` orchestration builds the corpus link graph, audits it, plans the fixes, and applies them via the P42-1 `rewriteWikiLinkReferences` (which preserves any `|alias` / `#section`); and a `muse notes fix-links [--dry-run] [--max-distance N] [--json]` command lists each applied fix as `[[from]] ‚Üí [[to]]` and separately reports the links it left unresolved so the user knows what still needs a human. `--dry-run` plans and previews without writing a single note. The operation is local-only and fully deterministic (no model). Proof: 4 new `planLinkFixes` unit tests in apps/cli/src/notes-links.test.ts (a unique typo "concpets" at distance 2 ‚Üí fixed to "concepts"; an ambiguous "foop" with both "food" and "fool" at distance 1 ‚Üí left unresolved with NO fix; a no-match target unresolved + a case-insensitive dedupe of repeated targets; a tighter `maxDistance` 1 correctly refuses the distance-2 snap) + 3 new `fixBrokenLinks` tests in apps/cli/src/commands-notes.test.ts over a real temp corpus (a journal linking `[[concpets]]` and `[[totallymissing]]` against a `concepts.md` note ‚Üí the typo is rewritten to `[[concepts]]` and the genuinely-missing link is left untouched; `--dry-run` returns the same plan but edits nothing on disk; an all-resolving corpus reports no fixes and no unresolved) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1831 tests) + a LIVE end-to-end round-trip on the loop PC: `muse notes fix-links --dry-run` then `muse notes fix-links` over that corpus print "Fixed 1 broken link(s) across 1 note(s): ‚Ä¢ [[concpets]] ‚Üí [[concepts]]" and "1 link(s) left unresolved (no unique close match): [[totallymissing]]", with journal.md afterward reading "See [[concepts]] for the idea, and [[totallymissing]] too." ‚Äî the typo repaired, the missing link deliberately untouched. cli 169 files / 1831 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a user can now repair a whole corpus of broken wiki-links in one command (completing the link-maintenance toolkit alongside `muse notes rename`), with the only real hazard ‚Äî snapping to the wrong note ‚Äî eliminated by the unique-match guard ‚Äî P42-2 bullet
- [Autonomy] A user running `muse daemon` now has the corrections they made in past chat sessions distilled into learned strategies UNATTENDED ‚Äî on the daemon's idle tick, with NO manual `muse playbook distill` ‚Äî closing the first slice of the autonomous self-development loop (P43-1 slice 1). The self-development mechanisms already existed but only as manual CLI (`muse playbook distill` / `consolidate`, `skills consolidate`) and the `apps/api` server tick (`tick-daemons.ts` wires `startConsolidateTick` + `distillQueuedCorrections`); the process the user actually runs on their Mac ‚Äî `muse daemon` (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) ‚Äî drove proactive / reminder / followup / ambient / web-watch / objectives / briefing / reflection ticks but NO learning-from-corrections tick, so a correction enqueued (`enqueueLearnEvent`) at correction time sat untouched until the user manually distilled it: the self-improvement loop was open exactly where it matters. Fixed WITHOUT forking the grounding-fenced drain: moved `distillQueuedCorrections` (+ `DistillQueuedDeps`) from apps/api into `@muse/autoconfigure` (the one package that depends on BOTH `@muse/agent-core` ‚Äî the distiller ‚Äî and `@muse/mcp` ‚Äî the learn-queue + playbook ops), with apps/api/src/distill-queue.ts now a byte-identical re-export so the server tick + its tests are unchanged, and the CLI daemon importing the SAME implementation (one source of truth, no duplicated grounding fence). Wired a `selfLearnTick` into `muse daemon`'s `runTick`, mirroring the existing reflection ("dreaming") tick: gated by `MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED` (off by default) AND a resolved model, interval-throttled (`MUSE_SELFLEARN_INTERVAL_MS`, default 5 min), and BRAKE-FIRST ‚Äî the learning-pause kill switch (`isLearningPaused`) is checked inside the drain so a paused user gets zero writes and the queue is left intact for a later resume; at most one distill per tick (the LLM call is the cost); every unattended write lands on PROBATION (recorded + visible via `muse learned` but NOT injected into prompts until a real reinforce graduates it ‚Äî the self-confirmation guard) with `origin: "grounded"` carrying the real correction as its source; fail-soft (a throwing distiller/embedder never breaks the daemon); a new `--status` line reports `self-learn: enabled/disabled`. The grounding floor is preserved end-to-end ‚Äî a queued event with no real correction text, or a distiller that returns nothing, writes ZERO strategies (a non-corrective signal never fabricates a lesson). Proof: 4 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts driving the REAL `muse daemon --once`/`--status` over the real learn-queue + a deterministic injected distiller seam (`selfLearnDistill`, zero live-LLM dependence): with `MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED` + a queued correction the tick distills it ("learned: +1 strategy from your corrections") and DRAINS the queue with no manual command; the BRAKE (`setLearningPaused`) leaves the queue intact and learns nothing; the gate is real (unset ‚áí nothing distilled, queue untouched); `--status` reports enabled only with the flag AND a model ‚Äî plus the @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1835 tests), the api `distill-queue` suite green against the re-export (849 tests), autoconfigure + api + cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (the moved module rebuilt clean and the grounding/self-improve machinery ‚Äî cited-recall, rubric gate, faithfulness, skill/playbook merge ‚Äî all still pass, so the floor held). cli 169 files / 1835 tests + api 849 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî the autonomous self-development loop is closed for its first surface (distill-from-corrections runs in the daemon you actually launch); the P43-1 bullet stays `[ ]` until consolidate/reinforce + a 2-session live battery prove an unattended correction changes a LATER session ‚Äî P43-1 slice 1 (decomposition: docs/goals/P43-close-the-loop.md)
- [Autonomy] A user running `muse daemon` now has stale, unused learned strategies automatically FADE toward neutral on the daemon's idle tick ‚Äî the forgetting half of continuous RL over the memory bank, so a one-off thumbs-up can't keep steering the agent forever (P43-1 slice 2). Slice 1 gave the daemon the ADDING half (distill corrections ‚Üí probation strategies unattended); but the user's actual runtime had no FORGETTING ‚Äî `decayStalePlaybookRewards` (every positive-reward, non-probation strategy not reinforced within the 30-day stale window loses a step toward NEUTRAL 0, never below ‚Äî disuse fades trust, it does not punish) ran ONLY in the `apps/api` server tick (`tick-daemons.ts`), never in `muse daemon` (the process the user launches on their Mac), so a strategy they thumbs-upped once and stopped using stayed at its old reward forever and kept being injected into every relevant prompt as stale advice. Wired a `selfLearnDecayTick` into the daemon's `runTick` (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) under the SAME `MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED` switch as distill (one switch = "autonomous self-development on": the bank both grows from corrections and fades from disuse), BRAKE-FIRST ‚Äî it checks the learning-pause kill switch (`isLearningPaused`) before touching anything, so a paused user's bank is frozen and a later resume catches up ‚Äî model-free (pure time+file, so it runs without a resolved model) on a slow daily cadence (`MUSE_SELFLEARN_DECAY_INTERVAL_MS`, default 24h), fail-soft, logging `decay: N stale strateg‚Ä¶ faded toward neutral` only when it actually fades something. Probation, neutral, and already-negative entries are untouched (decay only sinks earned-positive-but-now-stale strategies; a real correction is still what drives a strategy negative). Proof: 3 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts driving the REAL `muse daemon --once` over a real playbook file (NO model, NO network): a 60-day-stale reward-2 strategy fades to reward 1 on the tick ("decay: 1 stale strategy faded toward neutral"); the BRAKE (`setLearningPaused`) freezes the bank ‚Äî reward stays 2, nothing logged; the gate is real (MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED unset ‚áí no decay, reward stays 2) ‚Äî plus the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1838 tests) + apps/cli tsc clean + pnpm lint 0/0. This slice is model-free so no request/response live battery applies; the surface check drives the real daemon command end-to-end. cli 169 files / 1838 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî distill ADDS, decay FADES: the user's actual runtime (`muse daemon`) now runs continuous RL over its learned bank unattended (P43-1 stays `[ ]` ‚Äî the FLIP awaits consolidate/graduation + a 2-session live battery proving an unattended correction changes a later session) ‚Äî P43-1 slice 2 (decomposition: docs/goals/P43-close-the-loop.md)
- [Reliability/Actuation] `muse calendar add` (and the agent's calendar-create/move/cancel tool) against Google Calendar now SURVIVES a 429 rate-limit on the write ‚Äî it retries honouring the server's Retry-After instead of dropping the event ‚Äî closing the calendar actuator's transient-failure gap toward all-actuator reliability (P43-2 slice 1). Messaging dispatch already retried transient failures (`sendWithRetry`: 3 attempts, honours `MessagingProviderError.retryAfterMs`, short-circuits permanent errors), but the calendar actuator did NOT: `GoogleCalendarProvider.request` retried ONLY idempotent GETs (`maxRetries = method === "GET" ? this.retries : 0`) ‚Äî every write (POST createEvent / PATCH updateEvent / DELETE deleteEvent) failed outright on a transient status, so a Google burst-quota 429 (the most common transient failure for Calendar writes) silently dropped the user's event when created via `muse calendar add` or the agent calendar tool (loopback-calendar.ts). Fixed SAFELY ‚Äî the hard part of retrying a state-changing send: a WRITE now retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit, honouring `Retry-After` (parsed per RFC 7231 ‚Äî delta-seconds or HTTP-date, junk rejected ‚Äî clamped to CALENDAR_RETRY_AFTER_CAP_MS=30s, else exponential backoff), because a 429 is rejected by Google BEFORE the mutation is applied (no event created) so retrying can't double-create; a write 5xx OR a mid-flight network reject is AMBIGUOUS (the insert may have committed) and is NEVER retried (the existing "no double-create" guarantee is preserved). GET reads keep retrying 429/5xx + network rejects as before. Added `parseRetryAfterMs` + `CALENDAR_RETRY_AFTER_CAP_MS` to packages/calendar/src/errors.ts (mirroring the messaging/model Retry-After contract; calendar can't import @muse/mcp's copy ‚Äî wrong dependency direction) and exported them from the calendar barrel. Proof: contract-faithful HTTP fake (never a stubbed provider) in packages/calendar/test/google-provider.test.ts ‚Äî a write that returns 429+`Retry-After: 2` then 200 retries once and succeeds, sleeping exactly 2000ms (honoured the server hint, NOT the 250ms backoff); a 429 with no Retry-After falls back to 250ms exponential backoff; the 429 retry budget exhausts to a thrown HTTP_429 after initial+2 retries (no infinite loop); a 500 on a write is STILL never retried (single attempt, no double-create) ‚Äî plus 6 new `parseRetryAfterMs`/`isRetryableCalendarStatus` unit tests in packages/calendar/test/errors.test.ts (delta-seconds, HTTP-date relative-to-now clamped at 0, junk/decimal/negative rejected) + the full @muse/calendar suite green (12 files / 135 tests) + calendar tsc clean + `pnpm check` green across all workspaces (after restoring the goal-227 byte-hygiene gate in a separate fix) + pnpm lint 0/0. - [Self-improve/Retrieval] A user can now enable `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_RANK=true` so `muse ask` ranks the learned-strategy playbook (ACE / ReasoningBank) by SEMANTIC similarity to the question instead of pure lexical token-overlap ‚Äî a strategy the user phrased DIFFERENTLY from the current query now surfaces and gets applied, where token-overlap ranking surfaced the wrong (merely word-sharing) one (a research-validated small-model lever: for a FROZEN local model, retrieval quality dominates output ‚Äî "experience-following"). The playbook ranker (`scoreStrategy`/`rankPlaybookStrategies`, packages/agent-core/src/playbook.ts) was pure lexical ‚Äî `rankOverlap(query tokens, strategy tokens)` + reward + reflected-penalty ‚Äî with nomic embeddings used only in the merge/distill gates, never in per-query strategy surfacing; its own comment even flagged the scorer as "the swap-point for an embedding ranker later". Added a model-agnostic `rankPlaybookStrategiesByRelevance(strategies, queryText, embed, options)` that blends `EMBED_RANK_WEIGHT(5) * cosine(query, strategy)` into the existing score: `embed` is a duck-typed `(text) => Promise<number[]>` param (agent-core stays vendor-free ‚Äî the caller passes a local embedder), only eligible (non-avoided, non-probation) strategies are embedded, and any strategy whose embedding throws degrades to its pure-lexical score (a flaky embedder never drops a strategy). The sync `rankPlaybookStrategies` and the new async path now share one `rankEligible` helper, so the top-K + recency-floor + avoidance/probation exclusions are identical across both (behaviour-preserving for the lexical path ‚Äî all existing ranking tests unchanged). Wired into the `muse ask` chat-fast-path (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts, where a nomic embedder + cosine are already in scope) behind `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_RANK` (OFF by default ‚Äî it adds one local nomic pass per strategy, so it stays opt-in with no latency regression to the default ask; `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_MODEL` overrides the embed model), fail-soft back to the lexical ranker. Proof: 3 new deterministic tests in packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts with hand-built vectors (no live model) ‚Äî a SEMANTIC match ("keep replies warm and brief") ranks ABOVE a lexically-overlapping but off-topic decoy ("message the coworker about the server outage") for the query "how should I respond to a message from a coworker", exactly the case where lexical ranking INVERTS and picks the decoy; avoided (reward ‚â§ ‚àí4) AND probation strategies are still excluded even on a high cosine; a throwing embedder falls back to byte-identical lexical order ‚Äî plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1408 tests, the existing sync-ranking suite unchanged), apps/cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (the playbook-merge / skill-merge / background-review / all WEDGE+grounding batteries still pass, so the `rankEligible` refactor didn't regress the self-improve or grounding machinery). agent-core 112 files / 1408 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî Muse now applies the RIGHT learned strategy even when you phrase the request differently from when you taught it (the #2 research-backed small-model lever; the #1, deterministic arithmetic offload, was already delivered) ‚Äî small-model maximization lever (memory: project_small_model_maximization)
- [Grounding edge/Retrieval] A user can now enable `MUSE_RECALL_BM25=true` so personal-knowledge recall ranks the lexical half of its hybrid retrieval by Okapi BM25 (IDF-weighted, length-normalised) instead of raw token-overlap ‚Äî a query's RARE discriminative term (a name, an ID, an error code) now outranks a chunk that merely shares a corpus-common term, fewer/better passages being the single biggest precision lever for a weak local generator (research-backed). `rankKnowledgeChunks(hybrid:true)` (packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts) already fused a cosine ranking with a LEXICAL ranking via Reciprocal Rank Fusion (+ MMR), but the lexical signal was `lexicalOverlap` ‚Äî a raw COUNT of shared content tokens that weights every term equally and ignores chunk length, so a chunk sharing one common term ties (or beats) one sharing a rarer, more discriminative term. Added an exported `bm25Scores(queryTokens, chunks, key)` implementing Okapi BM25 ‚Äî IDF (`ln(1 + (N‚àídf+0.5)/(df+0.5))`) √ó saturating TF (k1=1.5) with document-length normalisation (b=0.75) over the candidate chunk set as the corpus ‚Äî and refactored the tokeniser so `lexicalTokens` (the de-duped Set) and BM25 (which needs the term-frequency multiset + document length) share one `lexicalTokenList` filter (behaviour-preserving: `lexicalTokens` now `new Set(lexicalTokenList(text))`, identical output). A new `bm25?: boolean` option on `RankKnowledgeOptions` (default OFF ‚Äî the raw-overlap behaviour is unchanged) swaps the fusion's lexical RANKING to BM25 when on, while the overlap-based citation FENCE (a passage earns a citation only with cosine ‚â• threshold OR any lexical overlap) is left exactly as-is ‚Äî BM25 > 0 iff overlap > 0, so the fabrication=0 guard is untouched and only the ORDER among already-eligible passages changes. Wired into the two production recall paths in autoconfigure (knowledge-corpus.ts: the ambient "Related:" lookup + the knowledge_search corpus) behind `MUSE_RECALL_BM25` (opt-in, no default-path latency/behaviour change). Proof: 2 new deterministic tests in knowledge-recall-agent.test.ts (no live model) ‚Äî `bm25Scores` ranks a chunk matching the rare "zephyr" (df=1, high IDF) strictly ABOVE one matching the corpus-common "report" (df=3, low IDF) where raw overlap ties both at 1; and `rankKnowledgeChunks(hybrid:true, bm25:true)` with a cosine-neutralising zero embed surfaces the rare-"zephyr" chunk at the top where the same call WITHOUT bm25 leaves a common-"report" chunk leading ‚Äî plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1410 tests, the existing hybrid/RRF/MMR + lexical-tokeniser tests unchanged by the refactor), @muse/autoconfigure tsc clean, apps/cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (the cited-recall / recall-citation-gate / rubric-gate / faithfulness / claim-grounding / proactive-recall-gate WEDGE + grounding batteries all still pass ‚Äî the default recall path is unchanged and the tokeniser refactor regressed nothing). agent-core 112 files / 1410 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî Muse's personal recall can now key on the discriminative rare term (a name / ID / code) a small model most needs grounded, where raw token-overlap drowned it under common-word matches ‚Äî small-model retrieval-precision lever (memory: project_small_model_maximization)
- [Grounding edge] A correctly WEB-grounded `muse ask --with-tools` answer is no longer false-flagged "not backed by your notes" ‚Äî the agent-path grounding verdict now scores the answer against the agent's OWN tool outputs (the evidence it was actually shown), not a notes-only set, closing a deterministic false-positive on the identity surface. The output-side rubric VERDICT (`groundingVerdictNotice` ‚Üí `verifyGrounding`/RGV) already ran under BOTH the chat-only AND the `--with-tools` agent path (so the backlog's "#1 --with-tools RGV" was already delivered ‚Äî verified, not rebuilt), and it scored against `scoredMatches` = notes + cited-note augmentation + structured data (contacts/tasks/events/episodes/memory/feeds). But it had NO access to what the AGENT retrieved via web_search / non-note tools, so a correct web answer ("The capital of France is Paris") scored ~zero coverage against the notes-only evidence and tripped the "‚öÝÔ∏è this answer's claims aren't fully backed by your notes ‚Äî treat as unverified" warning ‚Äî a deterministic false-positive on the exact surface where a spurious "I'm not sure" erodes trust worst. Surfaced the agent's read-tool outputs end-to-end: added `groundingSources?: { source, text }[]` to `AgentRunResult` (packages/agent-core/src/types.ts); `createRunResult` (runtime-internals.ts) now derives them from `execution.toolResults` (each tool's non-empty text output, capped at 4000 chars so a large web page can't bloat the reverify prompt; empty outputs like an actuator's "sent" are skipped) and `agent-runtime.ts` passes `execution.toolResults` through at the main call site; the `muse ask --with-tools` path (commands-ask.ts) captures `result.groundingSources` and adds them to the verdict's `scoredMatches` as `tool: <name>` evidence (cosine 1 ‚Äî the agent deliberately fetched them, so the verdict rests on COVERAGE). Still fabrication-safe: ONLY real tool outputs are added, so a claim backed by NEITHER the notes NOR any tool result stays uncovered ‚Üí ungrounded (the zero-fabrication property is preserved ‚Äî this only PREVENTS a false "ungrounded", never causes a false "grounded"). Proof: 3 new deterministic tests (no live model) ‚Äî `createRunResult` derives `groundingSources` from a web_search tool's text output and SKIPS an empty actuator output, and omits the field entirely on a chat-only / actuator-only run (packages/agent-core/test/runtime-internals.test.ts); and `groundingVerdictNotice` WARNS on "The capital of France is Paris" against notes-only evidence but is SILENT once the agent's web-tool output is in the evidence set (apps/cli/src/commands-ask-grounding-verdict.test.ts) ‚Äî plus the full @muse/agent-core suite (112 files / 1412 tests) + @muse/cli suite (169 files / 1839 tests) green, agent-core + cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (cited-recall / recall-citation-gate / rubric-gate / faithfulness / claim-grounding / reflection + council RGV all still pass ‚Äî the additive `groundingSources` field regressed nothing and the default chat path is unchanged). agent-core 112 files / 1412 tests + cli 169 files / 1839 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî the `--with-tools` agent answer is now verified against the evidence the agent actually used, completing "one grounding gate under EVERY surface" so a correct web answer no longer carries a spurious unverified warning ‚Äî grounding-edge false-positive fix (memory: project_small_model_maximization)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A rate-limited Gmail send via `muse email send` (and the agent's email tool) now SURVIVES a 429 ‚Äî it retries honouring the server's Retry-After instead of dropping the email ‚Äî extending the safe all-actuator transient-retry to the flagship OUTBOUND actuator (P43-2, ACT axis; messaging + calendar already retried, email did not). `GmailEmailProvider.sendEmail` (packages/mcp/src/email-provider.ts) did a single POST and threw on any non-2xx ‚Äî it DELIBERATELY did not retry, because a send is non-idempotent (Gmail has no client idempotency key) and a retried POST could deliver the message twice (the irreversible harm `outbound-safety.md` guards). Refined that to the SAFE subset: a SEND now retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit, honouring Retry-After (parsed per RFC 7231 via the shared `parseRetryAfterMs`, clamped to 30s, else exponential backoff), because Gmail rejects a 429 BEFORE queuing the message ‚Äî nothing was delivered, so retrying cannot double-send; a 5xx OR a mid-flight network reject is AMBIGUOUS (the message may have been accepted) and is STILL never retried (the no-double-send guarantee is preserved), and a 401/403 auth error still fails fast. Reuses the provider's existing `retryOptions` (retries/baseDelayMs/sleep/maxRetryAfterMs) ‚Äî the same seam the idempotent read path uses ‚Äî so the read retry is untouched. - [Reliability/Actuation] A Home Assistant action (lock the door, set the thermostat, turn off a light) via Muse now SURVIVES a transient 429 rate-limit ‚Äî the idempotent `call_service` retries honouring Retry-After instead of failing ‚Äî COMPLETING the all-actuator transient-retry the human focus named (messaging + calendar + email + home now retry; a non-idempotent web submit stays correctly single-shot), P43-2 ACT axis. The home WRITE path went through the shared `performWebActionWithApproval` executor (web-action.ts), which was deliberately single-shot ("No retry ‚Äî a retried POST can double-act") ‚Äî correct for a generic non-idempotent web submit (a booking/form), but it meant a Home Assistant `call_service` (which is IDEMPOTENT ‚Äî setting a state) also dropped on a transient 429. Added a `retryOn429?: boolean` option (default OFF) to the executor that, when set, retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit honouring Retry-After (parsed per RFC 7231, clamped 30s, else exponential backoff), wrapping ONLY the transmit ‚Äî the draft-first approval gate runs ONCE before the loop and a 429 retry NEVER re-approves; a 5xx OR a network/timeout reject is AMBIGUOUS (the action may have applied ‚Äî a toggle/script could have run) and is STILL never retried; the action log records the single FINAL outcome. `performHomeActionWithApproval` (smart-home.ts) sets `retryOn429: true` because a 429 is rejected by Home Assistant BEFORE the service executes (nothing happened, so a retry can't double-act) ‚Äî safe for every HA service including toggle/press. A generic web action leaves the flag off ‚Üí its single-shot non-idempotent-safe behaviour is byte-unchanged. Proof: 5 new contract-faithful tests (real Response sequences, counting transmits so a double-act shows as an extra call, never a fake registry) ‚Äî in web-action.test.ts: `retryOn429` retries a 429+`Retry-After:2` then performs (sleeping 2000ms, approving ONCE), a 5xx is NEVER retried (single attempt), and WITHOUT the flag a 429 is single-shot (a web submit never auto-retries); in smart-home-action.test.ts: `performHomeActionWithApproval` survives a 429 (retries honouring Retry-After, approves once, performs) and does NOT retry a 5xx ‚Äî plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (168 files / 1373 tests, the existing single-shot 500/403 web-action tests UNCHANGED), mcp tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. - [Self-improve/Autonomy] When you correct Muse about the SAME thing more than once, the unattended distiller now CONSOLIDATES it ‚Äî `muse learned` shows the lesson with a "raised N√ó" badge instead of cluttering the bank with paraphrase duplicates ‚Äî and (the safety fix) a repeated correction NEVER silently graduates a guessed strategy into the injected `[Learned Strategies]` block; promotion stays bound to your explicit approval (P43-1 slice 3a, the SAFE consolidation half; ACT/self-improve axis). The idle distill consumer (`distillQueuedCorrections`) checked the suppressed-lessons veto but NOT the playbook bank ‚Äî `recordPlaybookStrategy` only dedups by `id`, so every re-derived lesson from a repeated correction wrote a fresh probation entry (paraphrases of one lesson piling up), and worse, N independent probation entries could EACH later graduate, amplifying a single guess. A 10-voter reassessment panel found the originally-held "graduate a probation strategy when a repeated correction matches it" design UNSAFE ‚Äî a repeated correction is a NEGATIVE signal (the attended path scores a correction DECAY ‚àí1, only an APPROVAL REINFORCE +1; `adjustPlaybookReward` graduates only on net-positive reward) and `strategyTextSimilarity` is CJK-aware Jaccard TOPIC-overlap (can't tell "use a warm sign-off" from "STOP using a warm sign-off"), so graduating on a repeat would INVERT the user's signal and autonomously inject a contradicted directive ‚Äî a fabrication-class regression on the action surface. Shipped the SAFE slice the panel ratified instead: (1) `bumpPlaybookObservation(file, id)` (personal-playbook-store.ts) increments a new `timesObserved` counter ONLY ‚Äî it deliberately does NOT touch `reward`, `probation`, or `lastReinforcedAt` (pure observability, sign-safe); (2) `distillQueuedCorrections` (distill-queue.ts), before recording, queries the user's bank and if a freshly-distilled lesson's `strategyTextSimilarity` to an existing entry is ‚â• `dedupThreshold` (default 0.7) it bumps that entry's observation count and SKIPS the duplicate write (no graduation); (3) `muse learned` (commands-learned.ts) renders ` ¬∑ raised N√ó` on a probation strategy with `timesObserved ‚â• 2` so a repeatedly-raised point reads as worth reinforcing WITHOUT auto-promoting it. Graduation stays exactly where it was ‚Äî `adjustPlaybookReward` clearing probation on a POSITIVE user act (approval) ‚Äî untouched. Proof: 7 new deterministic tests (no live model) ‚Äî `bumpPlaybookObservation` increments (absent‚Üí2, +1, missing‚Üíundefined) AND the NEGATIVE ASSERTION that it never changes reward / clears probation / stamps lastReinforcedAt (playbook-store.test.ts); `distillQueuedCorrections` consolidates a re-derived near-duplicate (bumps timesObserved, records 0 new, keeps probation:true + reward:-1 ‚Äî no graduation) and STILL records a genuinely-distinct lesson as a new entry (distill-queue.test.ts, a new direct test for the previously-untested consumer); `muse learned` renders "raised 3√ó" and omits it for a once-observed entry (commands-learned.test.ts) ‚Äî plus the full @muse/mcp (168/1375) + @muse/autoconfigure (74/486) + @muse/cli (170/1860) suites green, mcp+autoconfigure+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE self-learning regression on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (skill-merge / playbook-merge / background-review + all WEDGE/grounding batteries still pass ‚Äî the additive consolidation regressed nothing). mcp 168/1375 + autoconfigure 74/486 + cli 170/1860 + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî repeated corrections are consolidated with a visible "raised N√ó" signal and can NEVER auto-bias Muse's answers, the sign-correct half of P43-1's held graduation slice; P43-1 stays `[ ]` until the 2-session live battery proves an unattended signal changes a later session ‚Äî P43-1 slice 3a (safe consolidation, sign-guarded, panel-ratified)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A multi-step `muse ask --with-tools` task no longer reports a confident answer built on a step that FAILED WITHOUT THROWING ‚Äî a plan step whose tool returned a failure (an MCP `isError` result, which surfaces as an "Error: ‚Ä¶" string with execution status "completed", or a `{ ok:false }`/`{ error }` JSON envelope) is now marked FAILED, so the synthesis is told not to use it as evidence and a sole failed-effect step refuses synthesis instead of fabricating a "done" (P43-2 verify-slice 1: per-step post-condition; the first leg of carry-to-done verification, the reassessment's #1 transformative gap). plan-execute-loop.ts determined step success as `toolResult.result.status === "completed"` ‚Äî i.e. purely "the tool didn't throw". But the executor sets status "completed" for ANY non-throwing RETURN (executor.ts:60), and an MCP tool that returns `isError: true` is rendered by the transport as `"Error: " + content` (transport.ts:278) WITHOUT throwing ‚Äî so a FAILED MCP tool call inside a plan was counted as a SUCCESSFUL step and the synthesis confidently built an answer on it: the exact fabrication failure mode the grounding edge kills on the RECALL surface, leaking onto the ACTION surface ("the grounding gate guards what Muse SAYS; nothing guarded that what Muse DID actually happened"). Added an exported pure `classifyStepEffect(output)` (plan-execute.ts) ‚Äî a per-step POST-CONDITION that first UNWRAPS the policy sanitizer's `--- BEGIN/END TOOL DATA ---` envelope (tool outputs reach the loop wrapped) and then flags an effect failure ONLY on an explicit signal: a leading `Error:`/`Failed:`/`Exception:` marker (the colon distinguishes it from ordinary content like "Error handling in Rust ‚Ä¶"), or a JSON envelope with a non-empty `error` / `ok:false` / `success:false`. EMPTY output stays VALID (the subtle empty-but-valid distinction the reassessment named ‚Äî an empty lookup is a legitimate result, rendered "[Îç∞Ïù¥ÌÑ∞ ÏóÜÏùå]", NOT a failure), and ordinary content (incl. "No results found") is never flagged. The loop now computes `success = completed && !classifyStepEffect(output).effectFailed`; a failed-effect step records `output: null` + the reason, feeds `renderPlanResultSummary`'s "[Ïã§Ìå®] ‚Ä¶ ÎãµÎ≥Ä Í∑ºÍ±∞Î°ú ÏÇ¨Ïö©ÌïòÏßÄ ÎßàÏÑ∏Ïöî" marker, and trips the existing `PLAN_ALL_STEPS_FAILED` refusal when it is the only step. Conservative by construction: only an explicit failure marker downgrades a step, so a normal plan (tools returning real content) is byte-unchanged. Proof: 9 new deterministic tests (no live model) ‚Äî `classifyStepEffect` flags a leading `Error:`/`Failed:` marker + a `{error}`/`{ok:false}`/`{success:false}` envelope, treats empty/whitespace/null as VALID, never flags "no results"/a success envelope/"Error handling in Rust" (no colon), AND classifies the PAYLOAD inside the real BEGIN/END TOOL DATA wrapper (so a wrapper-format change can't silently defeat it); plus 2 plan-execute-loop integration tests on the REAL assembly (ToolExecutor + sanitizer): a tool that RETURNS "Error: ‚Ä¶" with status "completed" is now marked `success:false` in its step-result span (where the old status check passed it), and a SOLE such step throws `PLAN_ALL_STEPS_FAILED` (refuses synthesis) instead of fabricating a done ‚Äî plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1425 tests, the existing thrown-failure + trajectory tests unchanged), agent-core tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (background-review-e2e exercises the agent runtime; the additive post-condition regressed nothing and the default content path is unchanged). agent-core 112/1425 + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a failed tool call inside a multi-step plan can no longer masquerade as a completed step, so `muse ask --with-tools` won't synthesize a confident answer on a failed effect; P43-2 stays `[ ]` until the REPLAN-on-failure recovery half + a 2-step carry-through through an injected failure lands ‚Äî P43-2 verify-slice 1 (plan-execute per-step post-condition, observed MCP-isError gap)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A multi-step `muse ask --with-tools` task now RECOVERS from a transient failure in an idempotent step instead of dying ‚Äî a read/lookup step that fails transiently (a 5xx/timeout that surfaces as an "Error: ‚Ä¶" result) is RETRIED once, and on recovery the 2-step task carries through to a verified done; a non-idempotent write/actuator step that fails is NEVER plan-retried (no double-act, per outbound-safety) and is surfaced honestly via the per-step post-condition. This FLIPS P43-2 "Reliable carry-to-done" (ACT axis, the reassessment's #1 transformative gap). Verify-slice 1 (prior commit) added the per-step post-condition (`classifyStepEffect`) that DETECTS a failed-effect step, but the plan-execute loop still ran once top-to-bottom with NO recovery ‚Äî a single transient blip in step 1 (a flaky lookup, a momentary 5xx) failed that step and, depending on the plan, killed the whole task or dropped it from the synthesis. Added bounded per-step retry GATED to read-risk tools: the loop reads `ModelTool.risk` (already carried on every projected tool) and, when a step FAILS, retries it up to `PLAN_STEP_MAX_ATTEMPTS=2` (one recovery retry) ONLY if the tool is `risk: "read"` (idempotent ‚Äî safe to re-execute); a `write`/`execute` step is pinned to ONE attempt because a retried send / booking / actuator call could double-act (the irreversible harm outbound-safety.md fences), and its transient case is already handled 429-only-safe at the HTTP-adapter layer. Retries also respect the run's `maxToolCalls` budget (a persistently-failing step can't exhaust it). Composed with slice-1's per-step verify + the actuator HTTP-layer retry + the ask-level grounding verdict, a 2-step task now carries to a verified done THROUGH an injected transient failure ‚Äî the recovery leg that closes "what Muse DOES actually happened" on the action surface (the action-surface analogue of the recall-surface grounding gate). Proof: 2 new contract-faithful integration tests on the REAL plan-execute assembly (real `ToolExecutor` + policy sanitizer, never a fake registry ‚Äî per outbound-safety.md): (1) a READ tool that returns "Error: upstream 503" on its FIRST call then succeeds ‚Üí the 2-step plan's failing step RECOVERS on retry (the tool is executed exactly twice for that step, the step-result span flips to `success`), and the task carries to `synthesis-started` (a verified done); (2) a WRITE tool that fails is executed EXACTLY ONCE (asserted via a call counter ‚Äî no double-act) and is surfaced as failed, so a sole failed write step trips `PLAN_ALL_STEPS_FAILED` (refuses synthesis) rather than fabricating a "done" ‚Äî joining slice-1's 9 post-condition tests. - [Reliability/Actuation] A Google Calendar read/write via Muse no longer crashes with an opaque `SyntaxError` when the third party returns a 2xx with a NON-JSON body (an HTML maintenance / proxy / captive-portal page, a truncated or empty response) ‚Äî it now fails with a clear, typed `CalendarProviderError("MALFORMED_RESPONSE")` carrying the status + a body snippet, so a malformed upstream response is a triageable error instead of an unhandled crash (P41 actuation-reliability hardening ‚Äî the human-focus "malformed third-party response" failure mode; ACT axis). `GoogleCalendarProvider.requestJson` handled `!response.ok` by reading the text and throwing a typed `CalendarProviderError`, but the SUCCESS path did `return await response.json() as T` with NO guard ‚Äî so a 2xx whose body is not valid JSON (real-world: a load-balancer/proxy 200-with-HTML, a captive portal, an empty or truncated body) threw a raw `SyntaxError` ("Unexpected token < in JSON‚Ä¶") that propagated UNWRAPPED, surfacing as an opaque crash the caller couldn't classify or fail-soft on ‚Äî exactly the kind of daily-reliability defect the human focus names, and an INCONSISTENCY with the Telegram provider which already safe-parses via `tryParseJson`.
