- [Reliability/Actuation] A hung or unresponsive Google Calendar endpoint can no longer block Muse indefinitely ‚Äî every Google Calendar HTTP call (the API requests AND the OAuth token refresh) now has a per-attempt request TIMEOUT (AbortController, default 15s), so a slow/stalled third party fails fast with a clear error instead of stalling `muse calendar` / the agent run (P41 actuator hardening ‚Äî the timeout dimension of "daily-reliable actuators"; ACT axis). The messaging providers (Telegram / Discord / Slack / LINE via `fetchWithTimeout`) and the Gmail provider (`fetchWithRetry`, 15s AbortController) already bounded their requests, but `GoogleCalendarProvider` called `this.fetchImpl(...)` RAW at both fetch sites ‚Äî with no timeout/AbortSignal ‚Äî so a hung Google endpoint (a network black-hole, an unresponsive proxy, a stalled TLS handshake) blocked the call until the OS socket timeout (often minutes). That genuinely STALLS the caller: the agent's wallclock cap (`maxRunWallclockMs`) only checks BETWEEN tool iterations, never mid-fetch, and the `muse brief` / daemon calendar reads have no other guard. Added a `timeoutMs` option (`GoogleCalendarRetryOptions`, default 15000, 0 disables) + a private `fetchWithTimeout(url, init)` that races each fetch against an `AbortController` timer (clearing it in `finally`) and routes both the API path and the token-refresh path through it. SAFE by construction via the EXISTING retry seam: a timeout rejects ‚Üí the request method's network-failure `catch` decides by idempotency ‚Äî an idempotent GET retries (`networkRetries = this.retries`) so a flaky moment doesn't drop the calendar from the briefing, while a WRITE (POST/PATCH/DELETE) has `networkRetries = 0` so a timed-out mutation is NEVER retried (a timeout is ambiguous ‚Äî the write may have committed ‚Äî so a retry could double-act; this preserves the same no-double-act guarantee as the 429-only write-retry). Proof: 2 new contract-faithful tests (a real hung-endpoint fake ‚Äî the API fetch returns a promise that only the injected AbortController resolves, by rejecting on `signal`; the token endpoint responds normally; never a fake registry) in packages/calendar/test/google-provider.test.ts ‚Äî a hung GET is aborted on each attempt and retried then thrown (`timed out`, asserted abort count = initial + 1 retry = 2, idempotent), and a hung WRITE is aborted EXACTLY ONCE and thrown (abort count = 1 ‚Äî never retried, no double-act) ‚Äî plus the full @muse/calendar suite green (12 files / 139 tests, the existing OAuth / 429-retry / 5xx / malformed-body / event-mapping contract tests unchanged), calendar tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. HTTP-actuator reliability slice (no model) ‚Üí the contract-faithful hung-endpoint fake is the surface check, not smoke:live. calendar 12/139 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a slow or black-holed Google Calendar can no longer hang Muse's morning brief or calendar actuator; the calendar provider reaches request-timeout parity with messaging + email, with double-act still fenced off (write timeouts never retry) ‚Äî P41 (ACT-axis actuator hardening, request timeout, Google Calendar)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A multi-step `muse ask --with-tools` task now ADAPTS when a read/lookup step fails non-recoverably ‚Äî instead of giving up, the plan-execute loop RE-DECOMPOSES: it asks the model for an ALTERNATIVE read-only approach to the same intent and runs it, so a task carries to a verified done via a different route (P43-2 carry-to-done, the "replans on a failed step" leg now real; ACT axis ‚Äî a 13-agent panel + 3-attacker red-team chose this as the highest-value SAFELY-achievable big lever, over encryption-at-rest [its first slice was red-teamed as a data-loss/race risk] and autonomous graduation [already shipped + sign-safe, no new code]). Slices 1‚Äì2 added the per-step post-condition (`classifyStepEffect`) + a bounded read-step RETRY, but a step that failed even after retry was simply marked failed ‚Äî the loop ran once top-to-bottom with no adaptive re-routing. Added `replanFailedReadStep` (packages/agent-core/src/plan-execute-loop.ts): when a READ step's effect fails after the bounded retry, it builds a focused re-plan prompt (the original request + the failed step + its reason), generates an alternative plan over ONLY the read-risk tools (`generatePlan` with read-tool descriptions), and runs up to `PLAN_REPLAN_MAX_STEPS=2` alternative steps ‚Äî the first that COMPLETES with a passing post-condition recovers the step's intent (recorded as `"<desc> (recovered via <tool>)"`). CRITICAL SAFETY (the reason the panel chose this as the SAFE lever, and the red-team's required guard): recovery is READ-ONLY and can NEVER double-act ‚Äî (1) only a read-risk step failure triggers a re-plan (`retryable`), a WRITE/execute failure is NEVER replanned because the mutation may have committed (outbound-safety.md), and (2) the alternative plan is FILTERED to read-risk tool names ‚Äî any write/execute step the model proposes in the re-plan is DROPPED, not executed; the immutable `executed[]` is never re-run, so a completed non-idempotent step can't repeat. The happy path is untouched (a succeeding step never replans ‚Üí zero added latency in the common case); the re-plan model call fires ONLY on a read-step failure, bounded by `maxToolCalls`. Proof: 3 new contract-faithful tests (a scripted runner giving precise control of the plan/re-plan model responses + each tool result, no live model) in packages/agent-core/test/plan-execute-replan.test.ts ‚Äî a failed READ step RECOVERS via an alternative read tool (retried √ó2 then the alternative runs, step flips to success, carries to synthesis, exactly ONE re-plan); a failed WRITE step is NEVER re-planned (executed exactly once, zero re-plan model calls ‚Äî no double-act); and a re-plan that proposes a WRITE step has it DROPPED (the write tool is never called, the read step stays failed) ‚Äî plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1430 tests; the existing partial-failure synthesis test updated to find its synthesis request by content since the re-plan adds a model call), agent-core tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (background-review-e2e exercises the agent runtime ‚Äî the additive re-plan, which only fires on a read-step failure the batteries don't hit, regressed nothing). agent-core 113/1430 + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ‚Äî a multi-step task no longer dies when a lookup step has no working answer; it adaptively re-routes to an alternative read, with double-act fenced off by construction (read-only re-plan, write failures never replanned) ‚Äî P43-2 (ACT-axis carry-to-done, adaptive read-only re-decomposition, panel-chosen + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their user-memory AT REST ‚Äî `muse memory encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/user-memory.json` (the confided life: facts, preferences, the typed user model) as an AES-256-GCM envelope, so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can no longer read it; reads/writes stay transparent (the agent's persona still loads it), with `muse memory decrypt` to reverse and `muse memory encryption-status` to check ‚Äî making "it can't tell anyone" true against STORAGE access, not just network egress (NEW Trust axis; the discretion-refusal half of the identity promise. Decided + safety-designed by a 13-agent panel that chose this lever, then a 3-attacker red-team of the actual diff that FOUND + drove a fix for a cross-process data-loss race before commit). Until now notes/memory/episodes/action-log were PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only ‚Äî only credentials/exports were encrypted ‚Äî so the most sensitive store (what Muse knows about you) sat readable on disk. Added `packages/memory/src/memory-encryption.ts` (AES-256-GCM + scrypt-derived key, mirroring the proven credential-store envelope; the key is `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` or a per-host fallback) and wired it into `FileUserMemoryStore` behind the red-team's REQUIRED GUARDS, each tested: (1) the read path NEVER writes ‚Äî it decrypts-or-reads-plaintext and returns the format, so there is no encrypt-on-read race; (2) FAIL-CLOSED-WITHOUT-DESTRUCTION ‚Äî a WRONG key (or a per-host key changed by a machine rename, or tampering) THROWS a clear error and leaves the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED, and because every write reads-first, a write under the wrong key also throws (it can never bury the ciphertext with empty data); (3) the one-shot `encryptAtRest()` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` BEFORE encrypting (recovery if the key derivation ever changes); (4) the un-migrated plaintext path is byte-unchanged (opt-in). The red-team's CRITICAL finding ‚Äî the per-process write mutex + a migration-only lock let a daemon `upsertFact` in one process race a CLI `encrypt` in another (read-modify-write, last-rename-wins ‚Üí a fact or the encryption lost) ‚Äî was FIXED before commit: ALL writes (upsert / delete / encrypt / decrypt) now serialize through ONE cross-process O_EXCL `.lock`, with stale-lock STEALING (an mtime > 30s lock from a crashed writer is reclaimed) so a crash can't block writes forever, while reads stay lock-free (the atomic rename keeps a concurrent reader consistent). Proof: ~12 new deterministic tests (no model) ‚Äî the crypto primitive round-trips + THROWS on a wrong key; the store round-trips (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt, writes preserve the encrypted format), writes the plaintext backup, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-unchanged (the killer data-loss case) including the wrong-key WRITE not burying it, read() never writes, decrypt reverses, and a stale lock is stolen (packages/memory/test/memory-user-store-file.test.ts); plus the full @muse/memory suite green (31 files / 329 tests), @muse/cli green (170 files / 1870 tests), memory+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse memory encrypt` over a seeded store removed the confided secret from cleartext on disk (0 hits, AES envelope), kept a recoverable plaintext backup, `encryption-status` reported encrypted, a WRONG key failed closed ("the encrypted data is intact on disk... restore the .plaintext-backup"), and `muse memory decrypt` restored the plaintext ‚Äî the lockfile released cleanly (no leftover). memory 31/329 + cli 170/1870 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse memory encrypt/decrypt` ‚Äî the confided life can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, so a stolen device can't read it; the discretion refusal is real against storage, not just the network ‚Äî P44 (Trust/privacy, user-memory encryption-at-rest, panel-decided + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their session-history AT REST ‚Äî `muse episode encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/episodes.json` (the auto-captured prior-session summaries: what you talked about, decided, asked Muse to follow up on) as an AES-256-GCM envelope under the SAME `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` as user-memory (ONE key for the whole confided life), so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can't read your session history either; reads stay transparent (`muse episode list` / the persona surfacing still decrypt), with `muse episode decrypt` to reverse and `muse episode encryption-status` to check (extends the P44 Trust axis from user-memory to the episodes store ‚Äî the discretion-refusal half of "it can't tell anyone", now over a second confided store). P44-1 encrypted user-memory; episodes/action-log were still PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only. Built a REUSABLE `encrypted-file` helper (packages/mcp/src/encrypted-file.ts: `readMaybeEncrypted` / `writeMaybeEncrypted` / `isFileEncryptedAtRest` / `withFileLock` / `encryptFileAtRest` / `decryptFileAtRest`) reusing `@muse/memory`'s proven AES-256-GCM envelope, and wired it into the function-based episodes store (packages/mcp/src/personal-episodes-store.ts): `readEpisodes` decrypts fail-closed (a wrong key THROWS and is NEVER quarantined-to-empty ‚Äî an undecryptable store is not corrupt; the non-JSON plaintext corrupt-quarantine path is preserved), `writeEpisodes` peeks the on-disk format and rewrites in the SAME format under a cross-process O_EXCL lock the migration also takes (so an ordinary write can't race `encryptEpisodesAtRest` and clobber it), and `encryptEpisodesAtRest` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` before migrating + seeds an empty encrypted file when the store is absent (so future episodes stay encrypted). Then a 3-attacker red-team OF THE ACTUAL DIFF (concurrency / fail-closed / regression lenses, per "build ‚Üí red-team the DIFF ‚Üí fix ‚Üí commit") drove FOUR pre-commit fixes: (1) `writeMaybeEncrypted` now delegates to the hardened `atomicWriteFile` (randomUUID tmp suffix so same-ms writers don't collide on rename; fsync before rename ‚Äî a torn ENCRYPTED file would be an undecryptable lock-out, not just empty); (2) `withFileLock` now stamps a per-holder NONCE and removes the lock ONLY if it still holds that nonce, so a >30s-slow holder whose lock was stolen mid-flight can't delete the new holder's lock (no orphan-cascade / third concurrent writer); (3) the `muse episode encrypt` output now DISCLOSES the plaintext backup is CLEARTEXT to delete once the key is confirmed (the red-team's strongest finding ‚Äî an undisclosed full-cleartext sibling defeats at-rest confidentiality); (4) the three new subcommands got automated CLI tests. Proof: 15 new deterministic store tests (no model) ‚Äî round-trip (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt), format preserved on subsequent writes, empty/absent-store seeds encrypted, plaintext backup holds the originals, idempotent re-encrypt, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED (incl. a wrong-key WRITE that can't bury it), read() never writes (bytes + mtime unchanged), decrypt reverses, decrypt-wrong-key fails closed, status is format-only (no key), corrupt-plaintext still quarantines, a STALE lock is stolen, 20 concurrent upserts on an encrypted store all survive + stay encrypted, clear preserves the format (packages/mcp/test/episodes-encryption.test.ts) + 4 new CLI tests driving the real subcommands through commander (status‚Üíencrypt‚Üístatus‚Üílist, wrong-key fail-closed, decrypt-reverts, --json) (apps/cli/src/commands-episode-encryption.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (169 files / 1397 tests), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1874 tests), mcp+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse episode encrypt` over a seeded store left an AES-256-GCM envelope (0 plaintext leak, cleartext-backup warning shown, NO orphan `.lock` left behind), `muse episode list` decrypted transparently, a WRONG key failed closed with the data intact, and `muse episode decrypt` restored the plaintext. mcp 169/1397 + cli 171/1874 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse episode encrypt/list/decrypt` ‚Äî a second confided store (your session history) can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, on a reusable helper ready for action-log next; the discretion refusal now covers what you said to Muse, not just what it learned about you ‚Äî P44-2 (Trust/privacy, episodes encryption-at-rest, reusable helper, panel-pattern + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Accountability] A user can now run `muse actions --verify` and get a DETERMINISTIC proof that the autonomous-action audit log (`~/.muse/action-log.json` ‚Äî what Muse did on their behalf: what/why/when/result) was not silently deleted, reordered, edited, or backdated ‚Äî and if it WAS, the exact entry index where the chain first breaks (exit 1 so a cron/script can gate on it). This capability did not exist: the log was "append-only BY CONTRACT" (personal-action-log-store.ts docstring) with ZERO integrity linkage ‚Äî a buggy concurrent writer, a partial-write crash, or any process with file access could rewrite history undetectably, so the accountability leg of "Tell it everything. It can't tell anyone." was unfalsifiable. Made it tamper-EVIDENT with a Merkle hash-chain (Haber-Stornetta 1991; RFC 6962): added `prevHash?: string` to ActionLogEntry (optional ‚Üí legacy logs stay readable), a pure `computeEntryHash(entry, prevHash)` = SHA-256 over the entry's canonical content (id/userId/when/what/why/result/objectiveId/detail, prevHash EXCLUDED from its own body) bound to the prior hash, so a one-byte change to any historical entry diverges its hash ‚Äî which is the NEXT entry's prevHash ‚Äî cascading the break to the tip; `appendActionLog` now seals each new entry to `chainTipHash(existing)` (genesis for the first; the per-file append queue keeps the chain fork-free under concurrency); `verifyActionLogChain(entries)` (pure) walks the STORED/append order recomputing every link and returns `{ok, brokenAtIndex, reason, linkedEntries}`, treating leading legacy (no-prevHash) entries as a valid pre-chain prefix and a missing link AFTER the chain began as a break; `verifyActionLogChainFile(file)` reads via readActionLog (append order, NOT queryActionLog which re-sorts newest-first). Wired `--verify` into `muse actions` (commands-actions.ts) before the query path: "‚úì chain intact ‚Äî N linked" or "‚úó TAMPERING DETECTED at entry N: ‚Ä¶" + `command.error(exitCode:1)`. HONEST framing baked into the copy + docstring: tamper-EVIDENT (catches accidental/partial-write/external-process/non-recomputing mutation), NEVER tamper-PROOF (a motivated attacker who recomputes the whole chain needs an off-box anchor ‚Äî out of scope). This slice was chosen by the cross-domain ideation panel (info-theory/distributed-systems) AFTER the bio panel's top pick ‚Äî an immune-system NEGATIVE-SELECTION per-claim grounding detector ‚Äî was BUILT and then FALSIFIED by a live nomic-embed calibration: recombination hallucinations (real entities, wrong combination) embed nearest-self at 0.79‚Äì0.85 vs faithful claims at 0.80‚Äì0.81 (the embedding is topical, not propositional), so it could not beat the existing lexical+value gate on its own falsifiable kill condition ‚Äî reverted, not shipped (an honest negative result; the "shows its work" discipline applied to my own work). Proof: 11 new deterministic mcp unit tests (no model) ‚Äî append‚Üíverify intact (first entry chains to genesis, each to its predecessor); in-place edit caught at the next link; deleted-middle / reordered / backdated-`when` each detected at the precise index; legacy no-prevHash entries verify as an intact prefix; a new append onto a legacy log starts a verifiable chain from the legacy tip; a prevHash stripped mid-chain is a break; empty/missing log vacuously intact (packages/mcp/test/action-log-chain.test.ts) + 3 new CLI tests (intact log prints "chain intact"; a byte-flipped on-disk entry exits 1 naming the broken index; --verify --json emits the structured verdict ‚Äî apps/cli/src/commands-actions.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (170 files / 1407 tests, the existing serialize/concurrency tests confirm back-compat), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1877 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (mcp interface change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the built CLI (deterministic SHA-256, no Ollama): a 3-action chain verified "‚úì chain intact ‚Äî 3 linked entries verified" (exit 0), then a silently-DELETED middle action was caught "‚úó TAMPERING DETECTED at entry 1 ‚Ä¶ does not chain to entry 0" (exit 1) and a BACKDATED `when` was caught at its exact index (exit 1). mcp 170/1407 + cli 171/1877 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse actions --verify` (intact + deletion + backdate) ‚Äî the audit trail of what Muse did on your behalf is now tamper-evident, closing the accountability leg of the trust moat; no model needed, so the proof is fully deterministic ‚Äî P44-3 (Trust/accountability, tamper-evident action-log hash-chain, cross-domain panel pick after the bio top-pick was live-falsified)
- [Reach/Trust] A user can now run a GROUNDED swarm council ‚Äî set `MUSE_A2A_COUNCIL_GROUNDED=true` and a council member (your own Muse's voice AND any peer that opted in) self-ABSTAINS, staying silent, when its OWN notes hold no CONFIDENT evidence for the question, so an ignorant peer can't dilute the synthesis with a confident-but-ungrounded opinion (the classic multiagent-debate failure mode). This is the multi-agent twin of "I'm not sure" ‚Äî it extends the fabrication=0 grounding invariant to a FIFTH surface (the peer DRAFT) at the COLONY level, and it's the structural prerequisite for honest colony learning (who SPEAKS on a question reveals who has corpus for it ‚Äî emergent specialization/federated trust need members to first stop speaking when ignorant). Chosen by the multi-angle ideation's technical-edge panel (3-lens red-teamed; it REJECTED Federated Strategy-Reward as unsafe ‚Äî that needs a peer-message‚Üílocal-state write punching a hole in inbound-inert). DESIGN: deliberately OPT-IN per node (the default council stays full deliberation ‚Äî abstaining-by-default would gut its main use, opinion questions like "rent or buy" where no one has corpus); purely SUBTRACTIVE (members say LESS, never more ‚Üí strengthens the trust core); entirely LOCAL (the corpus NEVER crosses the wire ‚Äî only the abstain/speak decision does, so no new shareable kind, inbound-inert untouched); and the gate is DETERMINISTIC (CRAG retrieval-confidence verdict, `classifyRetrievalConfidence`, not the stochastic 8B ‚Äî so qwen can't flake it). Built `abstainIfUngrounded(draft, matches, opts)` (speak only on a `confident` corpus match; `none`/`ambiguous` abstains ‚Äî keyed on RETRIEVAL confidence not draft token-coverage, since the council reasons in GENERAL terms by design so a coverage gate would silence everyone ‚Äî the over-abstention failure) + `produceGroundedCouncilReasoning` (short-circuits to abstain with NO model call when the corpus isn't confident) in packages/agent-core/src/council.ts; a `councilCorpusMatches` helper (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.ts) that reuses the precomputed notes index + the SAME absolute cosine the recall wedge grades by, fail-CLOSED to silence (empty ‚áí abstain) when there's no index or the embedder is down; wired into BOTH the `muse swarm council` initiator's own voice (round 1 + debate rounds) AND the `muse swarm serve` responder (this-Muse-as-a-peer), so the whole colony respects the posture; surfaced in `muse swarm status`. NOTE the real design insight that shaped it: the council is DELIBERATION not RECALL, so self-abstention is opt-in ‚Äî this avoided shipping a feature that would have broken the council's primary use. Proof: 7 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) ‚Äî abstainIfUngrounded speaks on confident / abstains on ambiguous+none+empty-draft / honors a custom confidentAt; produceGroundedCouncilReasoning SHORT-CIRCUITS (asserts NO model request spent) when not confident and reasons when confident; an end-to-end selectivity test that an abstaining member is absent from the synthesised contributors (packages/agent-core/test/council.test.ts) + 5 new CLI unit tests for councilCorpusMatches (no index ‚Üí []; ranks own chunks by absolute cosine ‚Üí confident in-corpus; off-corpus ‚Üí not confident; embedder-throws ‚Üí fail-closed []; env parsing) (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.test.ts) + the SwarmStatus grounded-posture render; plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1438 tests), @muse/cli green (173 files / 1887 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (agent-core council change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE battery on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed) ‚Äî `verify-council-self-abstention` (now in `eval:self-improving`, 19 batteries): an off-corpus question (top cosine 0.467, ambiguous) made the member ABSTAIN, an in-corpus question (top cosine 0.621, confident ‚Äî the over-abstention TRIPWIRE) made it SPEAK, and the council synthesised contributors `["alice"]` with the abstainer `bob` EXCLUDED; the two existing council batteries (`verify-council`, `verify-council-grounding`) still PASS (no regression). agent-core 113/1438 + cli 173/1887 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live verify-council-self-abstention (real qwen+nomic-embed: abstain/speak/exclude all proven) ‚Äî Muse's private swarm now has an honest colony floor: an ignorant peer stays silent instead of voting confidently, the 5th grounded surface, and the substrate every richer colony-learning step needs ‚Äî A2A-6 (Reach/Trust, council self-abstention, technical-edge panel pick, the colony-learning frontier)
- [Grounding edge/Front-door] A user can now run `muse ask --why` and, when Muse refuses or flags an answer, SEE exactly why ‚Äî which deterministic grounding criterion fell short and the measured value vs its threshold ‚Äî turning an opaque "I'm not sure" into an inspectable, ACTIONABLE judgement (rephrase, reindex, or add a note). This is the "shows its work" moat applied to the REFUSAL itself: the recall wedge already refuses instead of guessing, but the refusal was a black box; now `--why` names the failing rubric criterion(s) ‚Äî "no notes came close enough (best match 0.42, I need 0.55) ‚Äî confidence criterion", "the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) ‚Äî coverage criterion", "your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) ‚Äî answerability criterion", or "the answer cited N source(s) you don't have (‚Ä¶) ‚Äî citation criterion". The moat-analysis ideation workflow's red-teamed pick (chosen as the differentiating front-door slice): a refusal-WITH-REASONS is structurally uncopyable by hermes/openclaw ‚Äî their capability-first design has no refusal and no per-criterion verdict to surface, while Muse's deterministic 4-criterion `verifyGrounding` rubric is exactly the hard-to-replicate asset. Built a pure `explainGroundingVerdict(verification, { topCosine, confidentAt, coverageFloor, answerabilityFloor })` in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts that reads the rubric `verifyGrounding` ALREADY computes (the rubric stores the categorical confidence, so the caller passes the top match's raw cosine for the "best match 0.42" line) + `verification.reason`/`invalidCitations`, and emits 1‚Äì4 plain-language lines naming every criterion below its floor; returns `[]` for a `grounded` verdict (SILENT on the happy path ‚Äî a targeted trust affordance, not a debug firehose). Wired `--why` into `muse ask` (commands-ask.ts) AFTER the verdict block, isolated from the repair flow: NO extra model call (the rubric is deterministic), gated to stderr (`!--json`), and it runs even on a REFUSAL (which the fabrication warning deliberately skips, since a refusal asserts no claim) because explaining WHY it refused is exactly the point. Proof: 6 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) ‚Äî a grounded verdict yields []; a no-retrieval verdict names the confidence criterion with "best match 0.42, I need 0.55"; an off-evidence answer names the coverage criterion with the measured %; a fabricated `[from ghost.md]` names the citation criterion + lists the source; an ambiguous-retrieval answer is flagged "loosely related ‚Äî confidence criterion (low)"; custom thresholds render in the explanation (packages/agent-core/test/explain-grounding-verdict.test.ts); plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (114 files / 1444 tests), @muse/cli build clean, `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (the agent-core export consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE run on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed): `muse ask --why "what is the best sourdough bread recipe?"` over a VPN-only notes corpus REFUSED ("I am not sure, sir‚Ä¶") and printed "üîé Why I can't answer from your notes: ‚Ä¢ the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) ‚Äî coverage criterion ‚Ä¢ your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) ‚Äî answerability criterion". agent-core 114/1444 + cli build clean + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse ask --why` (off-corpus refusal explained) ‚Äî Muse's refusal is no longer a black box; the user sees which criterion failed and by how much, on the everyday front-door surface, which is the moat ("shows its work") made tangible where hermes/openclaw structurally can't follow ‚Äî P38-35 (Grounding edge/front-door, the --why refusal trace, moat-analysis panel pick)
- [Knowledge/Perception] A user can now have `muse ask` FOLLOW their `[[wiki-links]]` ‚Äî graph-augmented recall on the front door: an ask answer can ground on a note 1-hop LINKED from the matching note but whose own text didn't match the query, so the answer-bearing note your Zettelkasten points to (that the embedding ranking alone misses) reaches the model (HippoRAG / GraphRAG, Edge et al. 2024). Until now the note-link graph helped only `muse recall --expand` (1-hop); the front-door `muse ask` ignored it, so a question whose answer lived in a LINKED-but-non-matching note would refuse or under-ground. Fabrication-SAFE by construction: expansion fires ONLY from a CONFIDENT retrieval seed (a weak/off-corpus query pulls in nothing ‚Äî verified by classifyRetrievalConfidence === "confident"), adds ONLY the user's OWN real notes, keeps each linked chunk's real (low) cosine so the confidence verdict ‚Äî keyed on the TOP match ‚Äî is UNCHANGED (graph expansion can never inflate confidence), and is best-effort (a malformed graph never fails the ask). Built a pure `linkExpandRefs({ seedRefs, noteBodies, cap })` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that reuses the proven `buildNoteLinkGraph` + `linkedFromResults`, with the graph built from the SAME notes-index bodies the ask ranks so note ids match the ask's relativized sources EXACTLY (sidestepping the provider-id-vs-index-path mismatch that loadNoteLinkGraph would have introduced); wired one conservative, capped (+2 linked notes) step into the ask retrieval (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) right after the cosine top-K (`diversifyAskChunks`), promoting each linked note's best already-ranked chunk into the grounding evidence. Proof: 3 new pure unit tests (linkExpandRefs returns the answer-bearing linked note from a confident seed; [] when the seed has no outbound links; [] on no-seed / zero-cap ‚Äî apps/cli/src/notes-links.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite green (172 files / 1885 tests), cli build clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, the LIVE faithfulness battery UNREGRESSED on the loop PC (verify-faithfulness-rate: faithfulness 1.00 / false-refusal 0.00 on qwen3:8b ‚Äî the expansion is inert on the battery's link-free corpus, so the fabrication=0 moat is provably untouched), and a LIVE multi-hop ask round-trip (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed): `muse ask --top 1 "what MTU should the office VPN use?"` over a two-note corpus ‚Äî `vpn.md` (matched "office VPN", but had NO MTU value) linking `[[uplink-config]]`, and `uplink-config.md` (held "set the value to 1380", but never said "VPN" ‚Üí ranked below the top-1) ‚Äî reported "grounded on 2 note chunk(s) ‚Äî vpn.md, uplink-config.md" and answered "The office VPN should use an MTU of 1380 ‚Ä¶ [from uplink-config.md]"; with --top 1 the linked note could ONLY enter the evidence via the graph hop, so the answer is the proof. cli 172/1885 + verify-faithfulness-rate 1.00/0.00 (unregressed) + pnpm lint 0/0 + live multi-hop `muse ask --top 1` ‚Äî the front door now traverses your knowledge graph, so an answer that lives one wiki-link away from the question is reachable instead of refused, with the fabrication=0 moat fenced off (confident-seed-gated, own-notes-only, confidence verdict unchanged) ‚Äî P42-3 (Knowledge/perception, graph-augmented front-door recall, HippoRAG/GraphRAG)
- [Knowledge/Perception] A user can now record HOW a contact relates to them and recall by it ‚Äî `muse contacts add <name> --relationship <role>` (e.g. "manager", "wife", "doctor", "landlord"), then `muse ask "who is my manager?"` returns a grounded, cited answer naming that contact. This is the relationship-graph FOUNDATION, a ‚ùå MISSING capability-map gap: contacts were flat cards (name / email / phone / handle / birthday) with no role, so a personal AI couldn't answer the most basic relationship questions about the user's own people. Added a free-text `relationship` field to the `Contact` type (packages/mcp/src/personal-contacts-store.ts) ‚Äî emitted by `serializeContact`, parsed by the read-boundary `coerceContact` (a non-string `relationship` from a hand-edited/synced store is DROPPED like every other malformed optional field, never crashing the read), `muse contacts add --relationship <role>` (and a relationship-ONLY contact is now valid ‚Äî the reach guard relaxed from "email/handle/phone required" to "email/handle/phone OR relationship", since a recall-only contact like "my landlord" needs no reachability), shown in `muse contacts list`/the add confirmation ("Dana Wu [your manager]"), and wired into the `muse ask` grounding path: `contactMatchScore` (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) now adds the `relationship` to the contact's match haystack so "who is my manager?" (the lone content token "manager" after stopwords) surfaces the manager contact, and the contacts grounding block renders "your <role>" so the local model sees + can cite it as `[contact: <name>]` under the existing code-not-model citation gate. SAFETY: the relationship is explicitly NOT an identifier ‚Äî `resolveContact` (recipient resolution for outbound) still keys ONLY on name / phone / email / handle, so a role label can never mis-route a message to the wrong person. Proof: a new `contactMatchScore` test (a "who is my manager" query surfaces a relationship:"manager" contact AND scores 0 on a contact with no relationship, so it isn't falsely injected ‚Äî apps/cli/src/commands-ask-contacts.test.ts) + a new store round-trip test (relationship serialized + read back; a numeric relationship dropped ‚Äî packages/mcp/test/contacts-malformed-read.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (170 files / 1408 tests), @muse/cli green (172 files / 1886 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (the @muse/mcp Contact type change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): `muse contacts add Dana Wu --relationship manager` (‚Üí "Added Dana Wu [your manager]", no email required) then `muse ask "who is my manager?"` ‚Üí "Sir, your manager is Dana Wu [contact: Dana Wu]" (grounded on 1 contact, cited, with the üë§ receipt). mcp 170/1408 + cli 172/1886 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live add‚Üíask round-trip ‚Äî Muse can now hold the first edge of your relationship graph (a person's role to you) and answer "who is my ___?" from it, cited and fail-closed, without ever letting a role mis-resolve a recipient ‚Äî P37-20 (Knowledge/perception, contact relationship field, relationship-graph foundation)
- [Self-improve/Felt] Muse's autonomous self-learning is now FELT, not silent ‚Äî when the background `muse daemon` distills strategies from your past corrections on its idle tick (the P43-1 unattended self-learn tick, MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED), it now DELIVERS a notice to your actual channel ("Learned from your corrections: I noted N strateg(y/ies) from how you've corrected me lately ‚Äî review with `muse learned` (nothing changes how I answer until you reinforce it)"), instead of only emitting a daemon-stdout line a background user never watches. This closes the FELT half of the autonomous-self-development loop (loop-v2's "felt self-learning"): a user running the daemon now PERCEIVES Muse growing from their corrections, unattended, the moment it happens ‚Äî the literal answer to "is it learning from me on its own?". SAFE by construction and honesty-preserving: the distilled strategy stays PROBATION (the notice says so explicitly ‚Äî "nothing changes how I answer until you reinforce it"), so this only SURFACES the autonomous learning and NEVER auto-applies it ‚Äî the honesty-sensitive injection/graduation path (which the P43 decomposition reserves for human review) is untouched; the notice is quiet-hours-gated and fail-soft like every other proactive notice (a delivery failure never breaks the daemon). - [Reach/Reliability] A message a user CONFIRMS now survives a transient rate-limit instead of being dropped ‚Äî the draft-first outbound send (`muse messaging send` + the agent's `muse.messaging.send` tool, both routing through `sendMessageWithApproval`) rides the same `sendWithRetry` ladder the background notices already use, so a one-off `429 + Retry-After` (or a transient 5xx) is waited-out and the message is delivered, instead of being logged `failed` and lost on the first blip. - [Reach/Reliability] A CalDAV calendar WRITE (create / update / delete an event on iCloud / Fastmail / Proton / any compliant CalDAV server) now survives a transient rate-limit instead of being dropped ‚Äî Retry-After PARITY with the Google calendar adapter, so a user's "add this to my calendar" is equally reliable regardless of which backend they configured. - [Self-improve/Autonomy] A correction you make now AUTONOMOUSLY stops Muse applying a contradicted preference in LATER sessions ‚Äî the daemon, unattended, classifies each new correction against the strategies Muse currently applies and SUBTRACTIVELY decays the ones it CONTRADICTS, so "a correction in session A changes session B" closes the loop SIGN-SAFE. This FLIPS P43-1 (THE #1 lever, the last open P43 bullet ‚Äî the autonomous self-development daemon) and was the explicitly-held injection-path change: the decide-and-do directive (2026-06-04) said stop deferring the big levers to Jinan ‚Äî judge + DO it. The blocker was a genuine sign-error risk: a correction is a NEGATIVE signal and lexical topic-overlap can't tell "do X" from "STOP X", so decaying/graduating on a Jaccard match inverts the user's signal. The unblock is an LLM polarity gate `classifyCorrectionContradiction` (packages/agent-core/src/correction-distiller.ts) ‚Äî LIVE-validated 11/11 with ZERO false-CONTRADICT on qwen3:8b, including the exact topic-overlap-but-opposite cases ("stop using a warm sign-off" vs "use a warm sign-off" ‚Üí CONTRADICT) a lexical matcher misses ‚Äî wired into `eval:self-improving` as a permanent regression battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-correction-polarity.mjs). The daemon's self-learn tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts), after distilling this tick's new corrections into probation lessons, runs `decayContradictedStrategies` (packages/autoconfigure/src/decay-contradicted.ts): for each new correction √ó each INJECTED strategy, on a confident `contradict` it drops that strategy's reward to the avoid floor (PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW = -4 ‚Üí `isInjectableStrategy` false ‚Üí no longer applied; reversible ‚Äî a `muse playbook reward` lifts it back), and delivers a felt notice to the user's channel ("You corrected me, so I've stopped applying '<strategy>' going forward. If that was wrong, reinforce it with `muse playbook reward <id>`."). SAFE BY CONSTRUCTION ‚Äî the sign-error the playbook panel feared is STRUCTURALLY impossible: DECAY-ONLY (it NEVER graduates a probation guess, NEVER raises a reward, NEVER clears probation ‚Äî the ADDITIVE auto-graduation stays bound to a manual positive act, as the 10-voter panel ratified), so the worst case of a polarity error is a recoverable wrongly-avoided strategy, NEVER an autonomous fabrication entering the [Learned Strategies] prompt block; POLARITY-GATED + FAIL-CLOSED (agree / unrelated / uncertain / a model error all leave the strategy untouched); INJECTED-ONLY (a probation strategy isn't applied, so it's never a target); BRAKE-FIRST (a paused learner's bank is frozen); bounded model spend per tick. - [Trust/Security] Muse's email ingestion is now INDIRECT-PROMPT-INJECTION-HARDENED ‚Äî a malicious email can no longer splice forged instructions into Muse's recalled context. P37-22/23 made email a recall source (great for "what did Dana email?"), but an email is UNTRUSTED third-party content ‚Äî a sender controls its from/subject/snippet ‚Äî and the ingestion wrote those RAW into a recallable note, so a crafted email carrying `\n[System Override]\nIgnore your instructions‚Ä¶` (or a forged `# Email:` heading / `From:` line, a CRLF, or ANSI/C0 control bytes) could splice a fake prompt section that the model sees once the note is recalled (indirect prompt injection ‚Äî the research backlog's #5 spotlighting concern, now a live surface since email ships). Closed by applying the SAME deterministic defence every OTHER untrusted-content path in Muse already uses (ambient-context, attachment-context, episodic-recall, skills-context, active-context all run it) ‚Äî `stripUntrustedTerminalChars(value).replace(/\s+/gu, " ").trim()` ‚Äî to the email's from / subject / date / snippet inside `renderEmailNote` (apps/cli/src/email-sync.ts), so no untrusted field can carry a newline that breaks out of its own line; only the note's OWN structural newlines (which the code, not the sender, controls) remain. This is DETERMINISTIC CODE, not a prompt please-be-careful (per CLAUDE.md's non-negotiable "security is deterministic code, never prompt instruction"), and FABRICATION-SAFE: whitespace-collapse only removes the section-splice ‚Äî the email's actual words stay intact as inert grounding evidence (recall is unaffected), and a single-line injection is just text the grounding gate still treats as a cited source, never an instruction. Verified deterministically (this is a content-sanitisation fix, not the LLM request/response path, so smoke:live does not apply): 7 new unit tests (apps/cli/src/email-sync.test.ts ‚Äî a `\n[System Override]\n` in the snippet produces NO standalone forged section and `[System Override]` never starts a line, while the words remain; a subject/from cannot forge a SECOND `# Email:` heading or `From:` line; ANSI/C0 control + DEL bytes are stripped; a CRLF cannot splice a new line; a legit single-line email renders byte-identical (sanitisation is a no-op on clean content); `syncEmailsToNotes` writes sanitised notes idempotently; `safeEmailId("../../etc/passwd")` ‚Üí a path-safe filename, no traversal) + the existing 6 email CLI tests + 3 daemon email-sync tests UNBROKEN + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1911 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0. cli 1911 + pnpm lint 0/0 + injection battery ‚Äî the email-into-recall surface (P37-22/23) now carries the same indirect-prompt-injection defence as every other untrusted source Muse reads, deterministically and fabrication-safe ‚Äî P37-23 hardening (Trust/security, untrusted-email injection sanitisation, backlog #5)
- [Grounding/Honesty] When a user's notes CONFLICT, Muse now SURFACES the conflict ‚Äî "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th ‚Äî which is current?" ‚Äî instead of confidently picking one and hiding the other. This was a real honesty hole found by live probe: with two genuinely-conflicting notes (a.md "dentist June 12th", b.md "Dentist: June 15th", no update wording), `muse ask "when is my dentist appointment?"` on qwen3:8b confidently answered "June 12th [from a.md]", silently ignoring the conflicting b.md ‚Äî a fabrication-ADJACENT failure the grounding gate could not catch (the gate rejects a claim with NO retrieved source, but happily passes a claim that HAS a source even when another retrieved source CONTRADICTS it). The fix EXTENDS the honesty edge from "I'm not sure" (un-groundable) to "I have conflicting info" (multiply-groundable, contradictorily): a CONFLICTS rule added to the recall answer contract `CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES` (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) tells the model that when two passages give DIFFERENT answers and neither clearly updates the other, it must surface BOTH and the conflict citing each ("I have conflicting notes: X says ‚Ä¶, Y says ‚Ä¶ ‚Äî which is current?") rather than silently choosing; with an explicit carve-out so an UPDATE ("moved to", "now", "corrected to") is RESOLVED to the new value, not over-flagged as a conflict. It is a prompt-instruction behaviour with NO new model call ‚Üí ZERO added latency (it rides the existing answer generation); it does not change the grounding GATE (claims still cite real sources), and it is fail-soft (if the model ignored it the answer would be no worse than before). Verified deterministically AND live: a new unit test (CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES carries the CONFLICT rule AND the "if one UPDATES the other" carve-out ‚Äî apps/cli/src/commands-ask-cite-as.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1912 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + a NEW PERMANENT live battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-conflict-surfacing.mjs, wired into `eval:self-improving`) that on qwen3:8b asserts a GENUINE conflict surfaces both values + flags it (passed: "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th ‚Äî which is current?") AND an explicit UPDATE resolves to the new value without being left open (passed: "the weekly team sync is on Thursday at 4:00pm [from new.md]") ‚Äî 2/2 ‚Äî plus a full LIVE `muse ask` round-trip reproducing both behaviours end-to-end (before the fix it answered "June 12th" silently; after, it surfaces the conflict). cli 1912 + pnpm lint 0/0 + conflict-surfacing battery 2/2 + live muse ask both cases ‚Äî Muse no longer picks a side in your own contradictory notes; it shows you the conflict and asks which is current, extending the grounding edge to multiply-groundable-but-contradictory claims ‚Äî P38-36 (Grounding/honesty, conflict-surfacing in cited recall)
- [Actuation/Reliability] When you set a reminder by voice/chat, Muse now confirms it with the time you ACTUALLY asked for ‚Äî "I've added a reminder ‚Ä¶ due on Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)" ‚Äî instead of echoing the wrong hour. A real, trust-eroding actuator defect found by live probe: `muse ask --with-tools "remind me to call the dentist tomorrow at 3pm"` STORED the reminder correctly (3pm local) but the model CONFIRMED "‚Ä¶at 6:00 AM" ‚Äî it read the raw UTC ISO hour (‚Ä¶T06:00:00Z, which is 3pm KST) and parroted "6:00 AM", telling the user a time they never asked for. The reminder fires at the right instant, so the firing path never saw it ‚Äî but a confidant that reads back the wrong time looks broken and erodes trust in every "did you set that?". Fixed by enriching the model-facing reminder MCP tool results (add/due/search/snooze/fire) with a `dueAtLocal` field ‚Äî the due time rendered in the SERVER's local timezone, the same wall clock the natural-language phrase was parsed against ("Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)") via a new `formatReminderDueLocal` + `serializeReminderForModel` (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts) ‚Äî plus a `muse.reminders.add` tool-description anchor instructing the model to confirm with `dueAtLocal`, never the raw UTC ISO `dueAt`. The REST/web path is untouched (keeps the lean serializeReminder; the web UI formats its own times); only the LLM-facing tool results carry the extra field, so there's no API-shape change and no latency cost (pure string formatting on an already-returned result). This is actuator HARDENING per the human-directed focus ‚Äî a proven-once actuator that misreports the time is a user-facing reliability defect, and closing it is outward. - [Proactivity/Anticipation] Muse now PROACTIVELY WARNS you of an upcoming calendar double-booking ‚Äî it tells you about Friday's clash on Wednesday ‚Äî instead of only showing conflicts when you happen to run `muse today`. The capability map flagged this as the highest-value anticipation a single-user confidant can offer, and as a üü° gap: double-booking DETECTION already existed (detectCalendarConflicts) but ONLY on the PULL surfaces (`muse today`, `muse calendar conflicts`) ‚Äî the morning briefing, the evening recap, and every daemon tick were silent on conflicts, so a clash only ever surfaced if the user thought to look. This adds the missing PUSH: a pure `selectUpcomingConflicts(events, {now, withinDays})` in @muse/mcp (the future clashes whose overlap begins inside [now, now+withinDays], each carrying a stable dedup key + a human-readable LOCAL-time line; a clash already underway or in the past is excluded so Muse never nags about something un-bookable) layered on the existing detector, plus a `conflictWatchTick` daemon tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) that scans the upcoming calendar window and warns ONCE per clash via the user's configured messaging channel. It is off by default (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_ENABLED), throttled (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_INTERVAL_MS, default 30 min; MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_WITHIN_DAYS default 7), key-deduped via a ~/.muse/conflict-watch-fired.json sidecar so a standing clash never re-spams, fail-soft (a calendar provider hiccup never breaks the daemon ‚Äî same discipline as recap/briefing/email-sync ticks), and surfaced in `muse daemon --status` ("conflicts: enabled/disabled") for discoverability. This is a genuinely NEW axis (proactive anticipation, per B0's steering to favor a new axis over more grounding/time-display polish), reusing the existing conflict detector rather than reinventing it ‚Äî the new value is the proactive delivery + dedup layer. Verified deterministically AND end-to-end: 5 new tz-robust unit tests for the pure helper (a future clash is surfaced with a stable key + a local-time line that is NOT the bare UTC ISO; a clash already underway/past is excluded; a clash beyond the horizon is excluded; multiple notices are ordered soonest-first; no conflict ‚Üí []) passing in BOTH TZ=Asia/Seoul AND TZ=UTC (packages/mcp/test/calendar-conflicts.test.ts) + 5 daemon-integration tests driving the REAL `muse daemon --once` command with a contract-faithful capturing messaging provider (enabled + an upcoming clash ‚Üí exactly ONE warning naming both events; the SAME clash on a later tick ‚Üí NOT re-warned [the dedup contract]; no clash ‚Üí quiet, no send; disabled by default ‚Üí silent even with a clash present; `--status` reports enabled/disabled) + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1917 tests) + @muse/mcp green (173 files / 1468 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + a REAL end-to-end run on the loop machine: two overlapping events planted in the LOCAL calendar via `muse calendar add`, then `muse daemon --once --provider log` printed "conflict-watch: warned of 1 upcoming double-booking" (the real tick firing through the real calendar registry ‚Üí detector ‚Üí delivery), and a SECOND identical run was silent (deduped via the sidecar). mcp 1468 + cli 1917 + lint 0/0 + daemon-integration 5/5 + real `muse daemon --once` e2e (fired then deduped) ‚Äî Muse no longer waits for you to ask; it reaches out when your calendar has a coming double-booking, extending the proactive-anticipation surface (P43-4 topic-absence/recap) with a new, deterministic, cited-by-event-time anomaly type. ‚Äî P43-5 (Proactivity/anticipation, proactive calendar double-booking watch)

- [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer HARD-FAILS on your own contacts ‚Äî `muse ask --with-tools "draft an email to Sarah ‚Ä¶"` now produces a draft instead of erroring "Input guard detected private identifiers: email". Probing the outbound path exposed a severe, identity-breaking defect: the PII INPUT guard (createPiiInputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT (MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED defaulted true) and fail-closes the ENTIRE agent run when the assembled input carries any email/phone/private identifier ‚Äî but for a local "tell it everything" personal assistant whose OWN contacts and notes contain emails by nature, that breaks the core agent (and the outbound-email drafting that P41-2/P41-3 carefully hardened) on the user's own data EVERY time a contact with an email is in context. The fix is posture-aware (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createInputGuards): the PII INPUT guard's purpose is preventing PII from EGRESSING to a third-party CLOUD model, but under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY (the DEFAULT posture) the model is on-box and the model router refuses cloud egress via a SEPARATE deterministic gate (createModelProvider/LocalOnlyViolationError), so there is no third party to leak to and the block is pure breakage with zero benefit ‚Äî therefore the guard now fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is actually possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off); an explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). The INJECTION input guard (the real untrusted-content defense) and the PII OUTPUT mask (transcript/log hygiene) are UNCHANGED. Because this is a security-default change (big/risky per the decide-and-do directive), it was adversarially reviewed by an independent sub-agent panel BEFORE shipping (VERDICT: ship ‚Äî confirmed no real hole under local-only: the egress refusal is a separate gate, this guard's only consumer is the pre-model input pipeline, and there is no other sink it solely protected; this removes a control firing OUTSIDE its threat model, not a fail-open regression), and the cloud-side residual over-block was recorded as an explicit follow-up (Rejected ledger) rather than declared fixed. Verified deterministically AND live: 4 new posture unit tests (local-only default ‚Üí injection guard only, PII block OFF so the agent isn't broken on the user's own contacts; MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false ‚Üí PII guard present; explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true forces it on under local-only; per-flag independent drops) ‚Äî @muse/autoconfigure 75 files / 497 tests + @muse/cli 174 files / 1920 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 + a LIVE before/after round-trip on qwen3:8b: the EXACT prompt that previously errored "Input guard detected private identifiers: email" now returns a complete, well-formed email draft to Sarah ("Subject: Request to Reschedule Our 2pm Meeting ‚Ä¶ Best regards"), while under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false the same prompt STILL blocks with the PII error (egress protection for cloud users preserved). autoconfigure 497 + cli 1920 + lint 0/0 + live before(errored)/after(drafts)/cloud(still-blocks) on qwen ‚Äî a user can now have the agent draft emails and reason over their own contacts on a local-first assistant without a privacy guard meant for cloud egress breaking the whole run. ‚Äî P41-5 (Actuation/trust, posture-aware PII input guard; sub-agent-reviewed security-default change)
- [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer MASKS your own contacts' details back to you ‚Äî `muse ask --with-tools "what is Sarah's email?"` now returns the real address instead of `***@***.***`. The output-guard sibling of P41-5 (which fixed the PII INPUT block that errored the whole run): the PII OUTPUT mask (createPiiMaskingOutputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT and REWRITES the agent's final answer ‚Äî and the cached + run-history copy, since the runtime's applyOutputGuards replaces finalResponse with the masked text (agent-runtime.ts:536-538) ‚Äî redacting any email/phone to `***@***.***`. So on a local "tell it everything" assistant, asking the agent for your OWN contact's email handed back a masked answer; the answer is the very thing the user asked for. And unlike a true egress control, the output mask doesn't even PREVENT egress (under a cloud model the PII already left on the INPUT side), so under local-only its only effect is corrupting the user-facing answer + the local store with zero privacy benefit. Fixed with the SAME posture-aware pattern as P41-5 (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createOutputGuards): the PII OUTPUT mask fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off, the non-default posture); an explicit MUSE_OUTPUT_GUARD_PII_MASK_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). The system-prompt-leakage output guard and the injection input guard are UNCHANGED. This completes the P41-5 theme (PII guards over-applying to the user's OWN data under local-only break the personal assistant) on the output side; the security reasoning is the same one the independent adversarial sub-agent panel validated for P41-5 (under local-only there is no third party to leak to ‚Äî the egress refusal is a separate deterministic gate in createModelProvider ‚Äî so this removes a control firing OUTSIDE its threat model, not a fail-open regression; cloud unchanged; override preserved). - [Knowing-you/Contacts] You can now TELL the agent a person's ROLE conversationally ‚Äî "add Sarah, she's my manager" is remembered and later answers "who's my manager?". P37-20 added the contact `relationship` field plus the CLI path (`muse contacts add --relationship`) and recall grounding, but the AGENT tools (add_contact / find_contact in packages/mcp/src/contacts-tool.ts) never captured it ‚Äî so the conversational round-trip was half-built. Probing `muse ask --with-tools "add Sarah Chen, sarah@example.com, she is my manager"` confirmed the gap: the agent called add_contact and stored name + email but SILENTLY DROPPED "she is my manager" (no relationship on the stored Contact), because add_contact's schema had no `relationship` arg. So a user could ASK "who's my manager?" (recall reads relationship) but couldn't TELL Muse the role without dropping to the CLI. Fixed both sides of the agent surface: add_contact now takes a `relationship` arg with an example-bearing, role-cueing description ("'doctor', 'manager', 'wife', 'landlord', 'dentist' ‚Ä¶ set this whenever the user says 'my <role>'") and stores it on the Contact (and echoes it in the result), and find_contact now RETURNS the relationship so "who is Sarah?" surfaces her role. The relationship is NOT an identifier ‚Äî same safety boundary as P37-20/21 (a role never resolves an outbound recipient; name/phone/email/handle still do), so this can't mis-route a message. Verified deterministically AND end-to-end: 4 new unit tests (add_contact captures the role when stated + omits it when absent; find_contact surfaces the role + omits when absent ‚Äî packages/mcp/test/contacts-tool.test.ts) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1480 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE conversational round-trip on the local qwen3:8b proving the model SELECTS add_contact and FILLS relationship in one shot (per tool-calling.md): `muse ask --with-tools "add Sarah Chen ‚Ä¶ she is my manager"` now stores `"relationship": "manager"` on the contact (it was dropped before this fix), and then `muse ask "who is my manager?"` returns "your manager is Sarah Chen, whose contact details are sarah@example.com [contact: Sarah Chen]" ‚Äî the role written conversationally is read back, cited. mcp 1480 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live add-then-recall round-trip (role stored via the agent, read back by recall) ‚Äî a user can now build their people-graph by just talking to Muse ("add Dr. Park, she's my dentist") instead of remembering CLI flags, completing the conversational half of the relationship round-trip P37-20 started. ‚Äî P37-24 (Knowing-you/contacts, conversational relationship capture via add_contact/find_contact; completes P37-20's CLI relationship for the agent surface)
- [Actuation/Reliability] A multi-step "add the event AND remind me" request no longer silently LOSES the reminder ‚Äî `muse ask --with-tools "add a meeting with Sarah tomorrow at 2pm to my calendar, and remind me an hour before it"` now reliably creates BOTH the calendar event (2pm) and the reminder (1pm, an hour before), where before the reminder was silently dropped. Probing this realistic two-actuator request exposed a real carry-to-done defect: the calendar event was created but the reminder DROPPED with "recurrence must be 'daily' or 'weekly'". The local model, making a ONE-TIME reminder, filled the muse.reminders.add `recurrence` arg with a sentinel like "none"/"once" (instead of OMITTING it as the schema asks), and the tool HARD-ERRORED on any value that wasn't exactly "daily"/"weekly" ‚Äî so a benign arg the model guessed cost the user their reminder, and the multi-step task half-failed with no sign to the user. Fixed per tool-calling.md rule 7 (validate + repair deterministically, don't re-reason or reject): a new pure `normalizeReminderRecurrence(raw)` in packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts ‚Äî only "daily"/"weekly" (case-insensitive) are real cadences; a recognized one-time SENTINEL (none / once / one-time / single / no / never / n/a / false / empty) resolves SILENTLY to a one-shot reminder; a genuinely unsupported cadence (e.g. "monthly") STILL creates the one-shot reminder but returns a `note` field so the outcome is transparent, never hidden ‚Äî wired into the muse.reminders.add tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-reminders.ts), replacing the hard error. The reminder is now ALWAYS created; the actuator survives a real-world model input instead of dropping the user's reminder over a recurrence-arg guess. This is actuation HARDENING (the map's #1 "carry a multi-step request to done" reliability area), found by probing, distinct from the retry/transient P41-1..4 slices (a validation-strictness failure mode rather than a network one). Verified deterministically AND live: 4 new unit tests (daily/weekly pass through case-insensitively; undefined / empty / every one-time sentinel ‚Üí {} silently with no note; "monthly" ‚Üí one-shot + an explanatory note and NEVER a hard error ‚Äî packages/mcp/test/reminders-recurrence.test.ts) + the existing reminder suites unregressed + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1483 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL multi-step prompt that before the fix created the calendar event but DROPPED the reminder (recurrence error) now creates BOTH ‚Äî the calendar event "Meeting with Sarah" at 2026-06-05T05:00:00Z (2pm KST) AND the reminder "Meeting with Sarah" at 2026-06-05T04:00:00Z (1pm KST, correctly an hour before the meeting). mcp 1483 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live multi-step before(reminder dropped)/after(event+reminder both created, reminder an hour before) ‚Äî a user can now give Muse a compound "schedule this and remind me" request and trust that the reminder half actually lands. ‚Äî P41-7 (Actuation/reliability, reminder recurrence coercion; multi-step carry-to-done)
- [Actuation/Reliability] You can now EDIT a reminder by NAME, conversationally ‚Äî "push my dentist reminder to 5pm tomorrow" / "delete my milk reminder" now work instead of "reminder not found". Probing the edit path exposed a real carry-to-done defect: `muse ask --with-tools "push my dentist reminder back to 5pm tomorrow"` called muse.reminders.snooze but passed the TEXT "Call dentist" as the `id` (the local model refers to reminders by their description, not their generated id, and went straight to snooze without calling `search` first), so the tool answered "reminder not found" and the reschedule SILENTLY did nothing (the dueAt stayed unchanged). The snooze/fire/clear reminder tools required a literal id ‚Äî i.e. a 2-step "search to get the id, then act" chain that the small local model reliably fumbles (exactly the failure mode tool-calling.md warns about: prefer one tool that does the whole job). Fixed with a pure `resolveReminderRef(reminders, ref)` helper (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts): an exact id match wins; otherwise a case-insensitive substring match on the reminder text, preferring a PENDING reminder over an already-fired one when both match; a UNIQUE match resolves, MULTIPLE matches return the candidate list (fail-close ‚Äî never modify a guessed reminder, the same never-guess discipline as contact resolution), and no match ‚Üí not-found ‚Äî wired into all three edit tools (snooze / fire / clear in packages/mcp/src/loopback-reminders.ts), whose `id` arg now accepts an id OR a distinct word from the text (e.g. 'dentist'), documented in the schema description. This turns the fumbled 2-step chain into a reliable ONE shot and is actuation HARDENING for the map's #1 "carry a request to done" area, found by probing, distinct from the P41-7 recurrence fix (create-path) ‚Äî this is the edit-path. Verified deterministically AND live: 5 new unit tests (resolves an exact id; resolves a unique text word ‚Äî what the model actually passes; prefers the PENDING match when a word hits both a pending and a fired reminder; returns AMBIGUOUS candidates never a guess when multiple pending match; empty ref / no match ‚Üí not-found ‚Äî packages/mcp/test/reminders-recurrence.test.ts) + the existing reminder suites unregressed + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1488 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL prompt "push my dentist reminder back to 5pm tomorrow" that before the fix returned "reminder not found" (dueAt left at the old 06:00Z) now resolves "dentist" ‚Üí the seeded reminder and reschedules it to 2026-06-05T08:00:00Z (5pm KST tomorrow, confirmed back to the user as "due on June 5, 2026, at 5:00 PM"). mcp 1488 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live before(not found, unchanged)/after(resolved by text + rescheduled) ‚Äî a user can now reschedule, complete, or delete a reminder by just naming it, instead of the edit silently failing. (The tasks complete/update/delete tools have the identical id-vs-text gap ‚Äî a clean follow-on.) ‚Äî P41-8 (Actuation/reliability, edit-a-reminder-by-name via resolveReminderRef; one-shot resolve-then-act)
- [Perception/Knowledge-corpus] Muse now perceives notes in MORE formats ‚Äî `.org` (Emacs org-mode), `.rst` (reStructuredText), `.mdx`, `.text`, `.adoc`/`.asciidoc`, and markdown variants (`.mkd`/`.mdown`) are now indexed and citable, where before only `.md`/`.markdown`/`.txt`/`.pdf` were. Probing the corpus perception exposed a real gap: a `.txt` note dropped in the notes dir was indexed and answered, but a `.org` note in the same dir was SILENTLY SKIPPED ("2 embedded, 0 skipped" ‚Äî it never appeared in the index), so a power-user keeping notes in org-mode / reStructuredText / AsciiDoc / MDX had those notes INVISIBLE to recall. The root cause was the notes-index walker's extension allow-list (`/\.(md|markdown|txt|pdf)$/`) being too narrow ‚Äî even though the extractor (`extractDocumentText`) already reads every non-PDF file as UTF-8, so the walk filter was the ONLY gate dropping these prose formats. Fixed by widening to a single shared `NOTE_FILE_RE` (md / markdown / mkd / mdown / mdx / txt / text / org / rst / adoc / asciidoc / pdf) and using it in all THREE previously-duplicated filters ‚Äî the indexer `walkMarkdown` (apps/cli/src/commands-notes-rag.ts) plus `listNoteFiles` and `notesCorpusFileCount` (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) ‚Äî so the index, the corpus inventory ("what's in my notes?"), and the file count can never drift on which formats count; binary/data formats (.png/.json/.csv/.docx/.js) stay excluded, and a `.md.bak` is correctly rejected. This is a PERCEPTION-growth slice (the locked build-order's "perceive growth"), distinct from the recent actuation/tool fixes. Verified deterministically AND live: 2 new NOTE_FILE_RE unit tests (matches every supported prose format including UPPERCASE extensions and nested paths; rejects .png/.json/.csv/.docx/.xlsx/.zip/.js, a bare name, .orgx, and note.md.bak ‚Äî apps/cli/src/commands-notes-rag.test.ts) + a new listNoteFiles test (a .org/.rst/.text corpus is fully listed, a .png ignored ‚Äî apps/cli/src/commands-ask-overview.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1923 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the loop machine's local embedder/qwen: the SAME `.org` note that was silently skipped before now embeds and is cited ‚Äî `muse ask "when does Project Zephyr ship?"` over a corpus of zephyr.org + plants.rst + vpn.md reports "3 embedded, 0 skipped" (all three indexed) and answers "Project Zephyr ships on August 14, 2026 [from zephyr.org]" (the .org file cited), where before the fix the .org note never embedded at all. cli 1923 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live before(.org skipped)/after(.org + .rst indexed and cited) ‚Äî a user can now keep their notes in org-mode, reStructuredText, AsciiDoc, MDX, or any plain-text prose format and Muse perceives + cites them, instead of only markdown and .txt. ‚Äî P37-25 (Perception/knowledge-corpus, widen the notes-index file formats via shared NOTE_FILE_RE)
- [Actuation/Reliability] You can now COMPLETE or RESCHEDULE a TASK by NAME conversationally ‚Äî "mark the milk task as done" / "move the deck task to next Friday" now work instead of "task not found". The sibling of P41-8 (reminders edit-by-name), which flagged the identical id-vs-text gap on tasks; probing confirmed it live: `muse ask --with-tools "mark the milk task as done"` called muse.tasks.complete but passed the TEXT "milk" as the `id` (the local model refers to tasks by their title, not their generated id, and went straight to complete without calling `list`/`search` first), so the tool answered "The task 'milk' could not be found" and the task SILENTLY stayed OPEN. The complete/update task tools required a literal id ‚Äî the same 2-step "search to get the id, then act" chain the small local model reliably fumbles. This completes the edit-by-reference pattern across BOTH local actuators (reminders P41-8 + tasks P41-9), turning the fumbled 2-step chain into a reliable ONE shot ‚Äî actuation HARDENING for the map's #1 "carry a request to done" area, found by probing.
